## Agent 6 report — canonical object and error-budget audit

The sprint target is correctly stated as Gate 1 for the **full canonical actual-zeta curvature**

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''
\]

not for any affine-subtracted complement curvature, proxy zero kernel, or flexible Dirichlet-polynomial surrogate. The attached brief explicitly identifies this as the decisive theorem and warns that proving a proxy statement would not close the rank-two route. 

---

# 1. Canonical pass/fail criterion

A proposed proof **passes Agent 6 audit** only if it proves, with polynomial losses only,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

or equivalently, after \(m=m_0+\lambda x\),

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3 q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\qquad
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6 |X|.
\]

A proof **does not pass** if it proves only one of:

\[
\int |q''_{\source,R}|^2,
\qquad
\int |\sum_\rho K_2^{\proxy}(m;\rho)|^2,
\qquad
\int |B_2+P_2|^2,
\qquad
\int |P_2|^2
\]

without a certified transfer estimate to \(q''_{\can}\).

The required transfer estimate is:

\[
\left\|
q''_{\can}
-
q''_{\model}
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}
\]

or, in normalized form,

\[
\left\|
F_\lambda-F_{\lambda,\model}
\right\|_{L^2(X)}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-B/2}\lambda^3 |X|^{1/2}.
\]

Without this, a lower bound for the model object is not a Gate 1 lower bound.

---

# 2. Required canonical decomposition

Every proof must specify which of the following two canonical representations it uses:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\reg}K_2(m;\rho),
\]

or

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m).
\]

The attached brief flags exactly these fidelity requirements: exact \(B_2\), critical-line zero treatment, regularized or symmetric tails, dual term \(D_2\), error \(E_2\), and zero-side/AFE-side agreement. 

Thus I will classify future agent outputs as follows:

\[
\boxed{\text{Green}}
\]

proves Gate 1 for \(q''_{\can}\) with all \(B_2,D_2,E_2\), tail, and interval-scale losses accounted for.

\[
\boxed{\text{Yellow}}
\]

proves Gate 1 only for a canonical truncation or AFE approximation, but gives a plausible missing error estimate.

\[
\boxed{\text{Red}}
\]

proves only a proxy kernel, affine-subtracted source, generic Dirichlet polynomial, relaxed zero packet, or numerical surrogate.

---

# 3. Audit of the six lanes before results arrive

## Agent 1 — formal theorem/reductions

Likely status: **Yellow until the object is named correctly.**

Agent 1 must state Gate 1 for

\[
q''_{\can}
\]

on the actual packet interval \(I_\rho\), not merely for an abstract analytic function \(F\). A finite-jet theorem is acceptable only if it includes a quantitative analytic-complexity lemma:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_0)|
\ge \eta
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_X|F_\lambda|^2\ge Q^{-C}\eta^2 |X|
\]

with derivative growth for the actual canonical \(F_\lambda\), not a model.

Critical audit item:

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

is acceptable only if the Bernstein/Remez constants stay polynomial in \(Q\). If \(R=O(\log Q)\) creates exponential-in-\(R\) constants that become \(Q^{O(1)}\), still acceptable; if they become \(e^{Q^c}\), fail.

## Agent 2 — prime/AFE nonrecurrence

Likely status: **Green only if fixed-coefficient and full AFE.**

The proof must use

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

with \(P_2\) fixed by actual zeta coefficients. It is **not enough** to prove that a generic Dirichlet polynomial cannot vanish to high order.

A valid theorem should look like:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r
\{B_2+P_2+D_2\}(m_0)
\right|
\ge 2Q^{-B},
\]

plus

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r E_2(m_0)
\right|
\le Q^{-B}.
\]

Then it transfers to \(q''_{\can}\).

Failure mode:

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}
\]

is treated as if \(a_n\) were tunable or generic. That proves a proxy theorem only.

## Agent 3 — zero-prime anti-design

Likely status: **Yellow or Red unless explicit formula transfer is quantitative.**

The local zero-side quadrature obstruction is real:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Because positive same-scale quadrature can flatten finite jets, Agent 3 cannot win using only zero-counting, quartet symmetry, simplicity, or pair correlation. The attached brief explicitly says local geometry alone cannot give Gate 1 and actual zeta arithmetic must forbid the anti-design. 

A valid Agent 3 theorem must have the form:

\[
\text{same-scale zero anti-design}
\Longrightarrow
\text{explicit-formula violation on the prime/AFE side}.
\]

The coercive quantity must involve actual \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\), not merely a formal packet sum.

## Agent 4 — trace / Weil-positive route

Likely status: **Red unless coercive, not just nonnegative.**

A functional

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)
=
\int w(m-m_0)|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

is automatically nonnegative, but nonnegativity is useless. The required output is a lower bound:

\[
\mathcal E_w(m_0)\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

under the off-line packet hypotheses.

If Agent 4 produces only

\[
\mathcal E_w\ge0,
\]

or a positivity formula with a nullspace that still contains source-flat packets, it does not prove Gate 1.

Acceptable trace route:

\[
\mathcal E_w
=
\text{positive prime-side quadratic form}
+
\text{controlled errors}
\]

and the off-line condition excludes the nullspace.

## Agent 5 — adversarial counterexample hunter

Likely status: **High-value Red/Green discriminator.**

Agent 5’s role is not to prove Gate 1 but to test whether a source-flat family survives increasing canonical constraints:

\[
\text{quadrature}
\to
+B_2
\to
+D_2
\to
+E_2
\to
+Z_\alpha(m_0)
\to
\text{zero/AFE agreement}.
\]

If it survives all of these, we should pause the sprint, as stated in the stop rule. 

My audit requirement for Agent 5: the counterexample must be evaluated against the **same normalized scale** \(\lambda\) and interval \(I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X\). A model that is flat at one point but not in interval energy is not yet a Gate 1 counterexample.

---

# 4. Error-budget theorem needed for all lanes

All lanes implicitly need the following transfer lemma.

## Canonical transfer lemma

Let

\[
q''_{\can}=q''_{\model}+R_{\model}
\]

on \(I_\rho\). Suppose

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\model}|^2\,dm
\ge 4Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

and

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|R_{\model}|^2\,dm
\le Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Proof:

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_2
\ge
\|q''_{\model}\|_2-\|R_{\model}\|_2
\ge
2Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}
-
Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

Squaring gives Gate 1.

So every proof may work with a model only if it supplies:

\[
\|R_{\model}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

For finite jets, the analogous requirement is:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^rR_{\model}(m_0)|
\le Q^{-B}.
\]

---

# 5. Concrete canonicalization obligations

## 5.1 Background term \(B_2\)

No lower bound may drop \(B_2\) unless it proves either:

\[
\|B_2\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le \frac12\|P_2+D_2\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\]

or includes \(B_2\) inside the nonrecurrence theorem.

Dropping \(B_2\) is especially dangerous because source flattening is a cancellation problem. A smooth background term can either break or assist cancellation.

## 5.2 Dual AFE term \(D_2\)

A proof using only \(P_2\) is not canonical. It must show:

\[
\|D_2+E_2\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ll Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}
\]

or prove nonrecurrence for

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2.
\]

A main-term-only lower bound can be invalidated by main/dual cancellation.

## 5.3 Error \(E_2\)

For \(E_2\), the required estimate is not merely pointwise small at \(m_0\). Gate 1 is interval-energy, so we need either:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|E_2(m)|\le Q^{-B}
\]

or

\[
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^{-B}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

For finite-jet reductions:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_m^rE_2(m_0)|
\le Q^{-B}\Delta^{-r}
\]

where \(\Delta\) is the derivative normalization scale used by the theorem.

## 5.4 Critical-line zero treatment

The zero-side kernel must use the completed-phase convention. Any artificial regularization of critical-line zeros must be accompanied by a limit theorem:

\[
q''_{\can,\varepsilon}\to q''_{\can}
\]

in \(L^2(I_\rho)\), with polynomially controlled convergence.

If the proof depends on a regularized kernel that changes singular behavior near shallow packets, it is proxy-only.

## 5.5 Regularized tail

For zero-side truncations,

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+\sum_{|\gamma-m_0|\le W}^{\reg}K_2(m;\rho)+T_W(m),
\]

the proof must include

\[
\|T_W\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^{-B}|I_\rho|^{1/2}
\]

with \(W\) chosen polynomially admissible in \(Q\), or else show that the lower bound is monotone/stable under symmetric tail completion.

A tail cutoff that shares the same zero-list edge for \(I_\rho\) and \(2I_\rho\) cannot be trusted unless a separate edge flag or explicit tail bound is carried.

## 5.6 Interval scale

All estimates must name the scale:

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X.
\]

The two admissible cases are:

\[
\lambda=d
\quad\text{ordinary packet scale},
\]

and

\[
\lambda=c
\quad\text{singular/shallow packet scale}.
\]

A theorem proven only at fixed macroscopic scale does not imply Gate 1 unless it transfers down to packet scale without losing more than a polynomial power of \(Q\).

---

# 6. Current classification of known evidence

Based on the shared background:

| Evidence/proof object | Agent 6 classification | Reason |
|---|---:|---|
| Deterministic sine quadrature control | Red as proof, useful as negative control | It proves local packet geometry can flatten; not actual zeta. |
| Low-height zero-kernel proxy scans | Red/Yellow | Useful diagnostic, but not canonical and not proof evidence. |
| Fixed-prime relaxed surrogate valleys | Red as proof, useful as adversary | Coefficients/phase freedom may not match actual zeta. |
| Prime/AFE theorem with fixed actual coefficients and \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) | Green if completed | This directly targets \(q''_{\can}\). |
| Zero-prime anti-design via explicit formula | Green if quantitative | Must coerce actual prime/AFE imbalance. |
| Trace/Weil-positive functional | Yellow until coercive | Nonnegative is insufficient; needs lower bound and nullspace exclusion. |

---

# 7. Recommended audit protocol for future agent outputs

For each theorem returned by Agents 1–5, I will apply this checklist:

1. **Object identity**

\[
q''_{\text{proved}}=q''_{\can}?
\]

If no, identify residual.

2. **Representation**

Zero-side canonical, AFE canonical, or proxy?

3. **Missing terms**

Are \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) included or bounded?

4. **Tail**

Is the zero tail regularized symmetrically and bounded on \(I_\rho\)?

5. **Scale**

Does the proof hold on \(I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X\) for both ordinary and singular \(\lambda\)?

6. **Critical-line convention**

Does the proof use the completed phase and handle critical-line zeros correctly?

7. **Constants**

Do all complexity constants remain \(Q^{O(1)}\)?

8. **Conclusion type**

Does it prove interval energy, finite jet, or only pointwise nonvanishing?

9. **Transfer**

If finite-jet, is there a valid Remez/Bernstein transfer to interval energy?

10. **Dependency**

Does it rely on an unproved anti-cancellation assumption equivalent to Gate 1?

---

# 8. Bottom-line audit

The sprint is correctly aimed, but Agent 6’s constraint is strict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A Gate 1 proof must be a theorem about }q''_{\can},
\text{ not about a cleaner object nearby.}
}
\]

At present, the most likely valid route is Agent 2 or Agent 3: a fixed actual-zeta prime/AFE nonrecurrence theorem or a zero-prime anti-design contradiction. Agent 4 is viable only if it becomes coercive. Agent 1 is useful only if it locks exact hypotheses without weakening the target. Agent 5 is the stop-rule trigger.

My current status classification: **no Green proof yet; all lanes are pending.** The next useful input for Agent 6 is the actual theorem/proof skeleton from each agent, after which I can classify each as Green/Yellow/Red and identify the exact missing canonical transfer.

# Green standard

A result is **Green** only if it gives, for the actual canonical object,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Equivalently, with

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q''_{\can}(m_0+\lambda x),
\]

it must prove

\[
\int_X|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

The coordinator’s current target is the finite-jet anti-design theorem

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B_{\jet}}\lambda^3,
\]

with the simultaneous bad event being \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) and \(\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)\approx0\) for \(0\le r\le R(Q)\). 

# Required transfer lemma for any Yellow theorem

If an agent proves a lower bound for a model object

\[
q''_{\model},
\]

then it transfers to Gate 1 only under the explicit bound

\[
\|q''_{\can}-q''_{\model}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12 Q^{-B/2}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

For finite jets, the corresponding condition is

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r
(q''_{\can}-q''_{\model})(m_0)
\right|
\le
\frac12 Q^{-B_{\jet}}.
\]

Without one of these, a theorem for \(q''_{\model}\) is not a theorem for \(q''_{\can}\).

# Exact audit conditions

Every future proposed theorem must explicitly account for the following.

## 1. \(B_2\)

If \(B_2\) is dropped, the theorem is not Green. Since the bad event is cancellation, \(B_2\) can either break or enable flattening. Acceptable treatments are:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

inside the theorem, or a bound showing \(B_2\) is absorbed into a fixed inhomogeneous target.

## 2. \(D_2\)

A \(P_2\)-only theorem is Red/Yellow, never Green. The dual AFE term must either be included in the transversality/nonrecurrence theorem or removed by a differential/filter operator with polynomial loss and certified residual control.

## 3. \(E_2\)

The error cannot be merely “small” in an informal sense. Required:

\[
\|E_2\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{1/2}
\]

or, for finite-jet arguments,

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^rE_2(m_0)|
\le Q^{-C}.
\]

The exponent \(C\) must exceed the loss in the proposed lower bound.

## 4. Critical-line zero treatment

Any zero-side formulation must use the completed phase convention. If it regularizes critical-line singularities, it must prove convergence back to the canonical object in \(L^2(I_\rho)\) or in normalized finite jets.

## 5. Regularized/symmetric tail

A zero-side truncation must carry a tail estimate:

\[
\left\|
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal Z_W}^{\reg}K_2(\cdot;\rho)
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

Otherwise it is only a finite-zero proxy.

## 6. Ordinary and singular packet scales

All arguments must cover

\[
I_\rho=m_0+\lambda X
\]

with both ordinary packet scale and singular/shallow packet scale. A theorem at fixed macroscopic scale does not imply Gate 1 at packet scale.

## 7. Finite-jet to interval-energy transfer

Finite-jet anti-design is acceptable only with analytic-complexity control:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge \eta
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_X|F_\lambda|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-C}\eta^2|X|.
\]

The constants must stay polynomial in \(Q\).

## 8. Constants

All determinant, Remez, large-sieve, explicit-formula, and tail constants must be

\[
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Any loss like \(\exp(Q^c)\) or uncontrolled dependence on \(R\) breaks the proof chain.

# Bottom-line classification

No current lane is Green yet. The hierarchy is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 2 Wronskian/transversality is the closest Green candidate.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 3 main/dual incompatibility is the next closest.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Agents 1, 4, and 5 are valuable only if converted into fixed actual-zeta theorems.}
}
\]

The highest-risk false positive remains proving anti-flattening for one of:

\[
P_2,\qquad
P_2+D_2,\qquad
\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal Z_W}K_2^{\proxy},
\qquad
q''_{\source,R},
\]

and then treating it as a theorem for

\[
q''_{\can}.
\]

That transfer is exactly where the next proofs must be forced to pay their error budget.

_Thought for 38s_

## Agent 6 / F — Canonical Wronskian audit and derivative-order budget

The current sprint correctly identifies the Wronskian/transversality route as the closest candidate, but the route is still **Yellow**, not Green: the missing theorem is a fixed actual-zeta determinant/nonrecurrence lower bound for the canonical object, not merely distinctness of frequencies or a formal Vandermonde expansion. 

---

# 1. Exact derivative order required

The Wronskian is built from

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\Delta^j\partial_m^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

The matrix entries are

\[
\partial_m^\ell G_j,
\qquad
0\le j,\ell\le R+1.
\]

For the \(q''_{\can}\)-rows,

\[
\partial_m^\ell G_{j+1}
=
\Delta^j\partial_m^{j+\ell}q''_{\can}.
\]

The maximum occurs at

\[
j=R,\qquad \ell=R+1,
\]

so the Wronskian requires

\[
\boxed{
\partial_m^{2R+1}q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta'',
\]

this is equivalent to requiring physical derivatives of \(q_\zeta\) up to

\[
\boxed{
2R+3.
}
\]

For the \(Z_\alpha\)-row, the maximum derivative order is

\[
\boxed{
\partial_m^{R+1}Z_\alpha.
}
\]

So the canonical AFE package must control:

\[
\partial_m^k q''_{\can},\qquad 0\le k\le 2R+1,
\]

and

\[
\partial_m^k Z_\alpha,\qquad 0\le k\le R+1.
\]

---

# 2. Use normalized derivatives, or the route becomes unstable

The raw Wronskian

\[
\det(\partial_m^\ell G_j)
\]

is badly scaled. Each derivative of an AFE term contributes factors like

\[
(\log n)^k.
\]

On the active conductor range,

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

Thus raw \(k\)-th derivatives carry factors roughly

\[
Q^k.
\]

For \(k\le 2R+1\), this gives factors as large as

\[
Q^{2R+1}.
\]

Inside an \((R+2)\times(R+2)\) determinant, unnormalized derivative scaling can produce powers comparable to

\[
Q^{O(R^2)}.
\]

That is not automatically fatal if one tracks determinant scaling exactly, but it makes lower bounds and error stability opaque.

The audit requirement is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the normalized operator }
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m
\text{ throughout the Wronskian.}
}
\]

Define instead

\[
\widetilde G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
\widetilde G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\]

and use columns

\[
\mathcal D^\ell\widetilde G_j.
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal D^\ell\widetilde G_{j+1}
=
\mathcal D^{j+\ell}q''_{\can},
\]

with maximum normalized derivative order still

\[
2R+1.
\]

If

\[
\Delta Q\asymp 1,
\]

then differentiated AFE terms remain naturally \(O(1)\)-scaled rather than \(Q^k\)-scaled.

**Conclusion:** raw Wronskian is Yellow/severe; normalized Wronskian is the only plausible Green candidate.

---

# 3. Required AFE error budget for \(E_2\)

The canonical decomposition is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

For the Wronskian route, it is not enough to know

\[
E_2=o(1).
\]

We need all normalized derivatives up to order \(2R+1\):

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
\left|
\mathcal D^k E_2(m)
\right|
\le \varepsilon_R
\quad
\text{on }I_\rho^\ast.
}
\]

The size of \(\varepsilon_R\) depends on the determinant lower bound.

Let

\[
N=R+2
\]

be the Wronskian size. Suppose the normalized canonical main matrix has entries bounded by

\[
|M_{ij}|\le Q^{C_0},
\]

and the desired determinant lower bound is

\[
|\det M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A crude determinant perturbation bound gives the sufficient condition

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_R
\le
Q^{-A-C_0(N-1)} \cdot \exp(-O(N\log N)).
}
\]

If the entries are normalized to \(O(1)\), this becomes roughly

\[
\varepsilon_R
\le
Q^{-A}\exp(-O(R\log R)).
\]

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So the determinant stability budget remains polynomial.

For

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

we get

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))=Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which is no longer a fixed polynomial power of \(Q\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\text{ is compatible with a polynomial determinant error budget;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R=O(\log Q)
\text{ is severe and likely non-polynomial unless extra structure removes factorial losses.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Factorial and high-derivative losses

High derivatives of AFE weights, gamma factors, and smooth cutoffs usually introduce losses of the form

\[
C^K K!,
\]

where

\[
K=2R+1.
\]

If

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then

\[
K!\le \exp(O(K\log K))
=
\exp(O(\log Q))
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

This is acceptable.

If

\[
R=c\log Q,
\]

then

\[
K!
=
\exp(O(\log Q\log\log Q))
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)}.
\]

That is not acceptable under the current \(Q^{O(1)}\) bookkeeping.

Therefore the Wronskian route should **not** use the conservative \(R=O(\log Q)\) version unless a special analytic lemma avoids factorial dependence.

Recommended working depth:

\[
\boxed{
R=\left\lfloor c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right\rfloor.
}
\]

---

# 5. \(B_2\) audit

The background term \(B_2\) must remain inside the Wronskian rows:

\[
\mathcal D^j q''_{\can}
=
\mathcal D^j(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2).
\]

Dropping \(B_2\) is not allowed because the bad locus is a cancellation locus. \(B_2\) may shift or assist the flattening equations.

For \(K=2R+1\), we need

\[
\max_{0\le k\le K}
|\mathcal D^k B_2(m)|
\le Q^{C}
\]

on the enlarged packet interval \(I_\rho^\ast\).

This is likely manageable, because \(B_2\) is smooth/gamma-background rather than oscillatory. But it must be included in the determinant or treated as a fixed inhomogeneous term.

Classification if omitted:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Red.}
}
\]

Classification if included with polynomial high-derivative bounds:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow/Green possible.}
}
\]

---

# 6. \(D_2\) audit

The dual AFE term \(D_2\) must also remain inside the Wronskian.

A Wronskian theorem for

\[
B_2+P_2
\]

does **not** prove the canonical theorem unless it also proves

\[
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kD_2(m)|
\ll Q^{-C}
\]

or shows that \(D_2\) is eliminated by a normalized operator with controlled loss.

But the previous sprint already indicated that \(D_2\) is not merely an opposite-frequency nuisance; after the gamma phase it is a complementary AFE frequency block. So one should assume:

\[
\boxed{
D_2\text{ is structurally active.}
}
\]

Classification:

\[
\text{\(P_2\)-only Wronskian}=\boxed{\text{Red/Yellow}},
\]

\[
\text{\(B_2+P_2+D_2\) Wronskian with }E_2\text{ control}
=\boxed{\text{Green possible}}.
\]

---

# 7. Critical-line zero and tail audit

If the Wronskian is proved through AFE, critical-line zero singularities are hidden inside the canonical equality and do not need separate zero-kernel handling, provided the AFE representation is genuinely for

\[
q''_{\can}.
\]

If the Wronskian is proved through a zero-side expansion, then the proof must handle:

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho)
\]

with derivatives up to

\[
2R+1.
\]

The required tail bound is then:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
\left\|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal Z_W}^{\rm reg}K_2(\cdot;\rho)
\right\|_{L^\infty(I_\rho^\ast)}
\le Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Or, for an \(L^2\)-based proof,

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
\left\|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal Z_W}^{\rm reg}K_2(\cdot;\rho)
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho^\ast)}
\le Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Critical-line regularization must commute with derivatives up to order \(2R+1\), or the zero-side Wronskian is only a proxy.

---

# 8. Ordinary versus singular packet scale

The normalized derivative should use the actual packet scale:

\[
\mathcal D_\lambda=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

For ordinary same-scale packets,

\[
\lambda\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

so

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp 1
\]

on the AFE conductor range. This is the stable case.

For singular/shallow packets,

\[
\lambda=c
\]

may be smaller. Then

\[
\lambda\log n
\]

may be much smaller than \(1\), and high normalized derivatives may lose sensitivity to prime oscillation.

This creates two options:

1. **Handle singular packets separately by dominance**, as earlier Gate 2 analysis suggests; or  
2. **Prove a singular-scale Wronskian theorem** with explicit dependence on \(\lambda Q\).

The Wronskian route is Green only if it states which option is being used.

Current classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary scale: Green possible;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular scale: Yellow unless dominance or }\lambda Q\text{-dependent determinant bounds are supplied.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Finite-jet to interval-energy transfer

Even a successful Wronskian lower bound gives only finite-jet anti-design:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\mathcal D^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

To prove Gate 1, we still need the analytic transfer:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rF_\lambda(x_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-B}
\lambda^3
\Longrightarrow
\int_X|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B'}\lambda^6|X|.
\]

This transfer must use derivative bounds for \(F_\lambda\) beyond order \(R\), typically up to \(2R+1\) or a comparable analytic-complexity bound.

The same derivative budget therefore appears twice:

1. Wronskian determinant construction;
2. Remez/Bernstein finite-jet-to-energy transfer.

Both must remain \(Q^{O(1)}\).

---

# 10. Final classification of the Wronskian route

## Raw Wronskian

\[
\det(\partial_m^\ell G_j)
\]

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow but derivative budget severe.}
}
\]

Reason: raw derivative powers \(Q^k\) produce determinant scaling \(Q^{O(R^2)}\). This is manageable only if every scaling factor is explicitly normalized out.

## Normalized Wronskian with \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\)

\[
\det(\mathcal D^\ell \widetilde G_j)
\]

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Green possible.}
}
\]

Required conditions:

\[
\begin{aligned}
&\text{fixed actual coefficients;}\\
&B_2+P_2+D_2\text{ included;}\\
&\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-C};\\
&\text{determinant lower bound }|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A};\\
&\text{ordinary and singular scales handled;}\\
&\text{finite-jet }\Rightarrow\text{ interval-energy transfer.}
\end{aligned}
\]

## Normalized Wronskian with \(R=O(\log Q)\)

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow/Red unless factorial losses are eliminated.}
}
\]

Reason:

\[
R!\sim Q^{O(\log\log Q)}
\]

is not a fixed polynomial loss.

---

# Bottom line

The Wronskian route is not disqualified, but it must be run in a very specific normalized form:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
}
\]

The exact derivative budget is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}\text{ derivatives up to }2R+1,
\quad
q_\zeta\text{ derivatives up to }2R+3,
\quad
Z_\alpha\text{ derivatives up to }R+1.
}
\]

With normalized derivatives and \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\), the route remains **Green possible**.

With raw derivatives or \(R=O(\log Q)\), the route becomes **severe Yellow** and likely fails the \(Q^{O(1)}\) bookkeeping unless a special determinant/AFE lemma removes factorial and derivative-growth losses.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:02:58)

I’ll give the derivative budget in the normalized \(\mathcal D\)-calculus, then separate what is merely plausible from what would need a formal AFE theorem.

## Agent 6 / F — Canonical derivative/error budget for normalized Wronskian

The attached coordinator brief sets the current route as

\[
\text{normalized Wronskian/transversality}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite-jet anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 1},
\]

with normalized derivatives

\[
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

and preferred depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The route is explicitly only Green-possible if it proves the determinant/nonrecurrence lower bound for the actual canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

---

# 1. Exact derivative-order budget

The normalized Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det(\mathcal D^\ell G_j(m,\alpha))_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

where

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

For the source rows,

\[
\mathcal D^\ell G_{j+1}
=
\mathcal D^{j+\ell}q''_{\can}.
\]

The largest order occurs at

\[
j=R,\qquad \ell=R+1,
\]

so the Wronskian requires

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{2R+1}q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta'',
\]

this requires physical derivatives of \(q_\zeta\) up to

\[
\boxed{
2R+3.
}
\]

For the \(Z_\alpha\)-row, the maximum order is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha.
}
\]

---

# 2. Derivative budget table

| Object | Appears as | Highest normalized derivative required | Equivalent physical derivative order |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| \(q''_{\can}\) | source curvature row | \(\mathcal D^{2R+1}q''_{\can}\) | \(\partial_m^{2R+1}q''_{\can}\) |
| \(q_\zeta\) | underlying phase/source primitive | — | \(\partial_m^{2R+3}q_\zeta\) |
| \(Z_\alpha\) | off-line center row | \(\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha\) | \(\partial_m^{R+1}Z_\alpha\) |
| \(B_2\) | background term in \(q''_{\can}\) | \(\mathcal D^{2R+1}B_2\) | \(\partial_m^{2R+1}B_2\) |
| \(P_2\) | main AFE term | \(\mathcal D^{2R+1}P_2\) | \(\partial_m^{2R+1}P_2\) |
| \(D_2\) | dual AFE term | \(\mathcal D^{2R+1}D_2\) | \(\partial_m^{2R+1}D_2\) |
| \(E_2\) | AFE error | \(\mathcal D^{2R+1}E_2\) | \(\partial_m^{2R+1}E_2\) |

Thus the canonical AFE theorem needed is not a low-order estimate. It must control

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
}
\]

on the enlarged packet interval \(I_\rho^\ast\), not merely \(E_2\) itself.

---

# 3. Required \(E_2\) stability

Suppose the normalized determinant theorem aims to prove

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Let

\[
N=R+2
\]

be the matrix size. If every normalized main matrix entry is bounded by

\[
Q^{C_0},
\]

then a crude determinant perturbation bound requires

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le
Q^{-A-C_0(N-1)}e^{-O(N\log N)}.
}
\]

If normalization keeps entries \(O(Q^{C_0})\) with fixed \(C_0\), then this is still polynomially small provided

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So the needed \(E_2\) theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

for a sufficiently large fixed \(C_E\), uniformly on \(I_\rho^\ast\).

This is plausible only if the AFE remainder is proved with uniform high-derivative control after smoothing.

---

# 4. Smoothing and gamma-factor losses

The dangerous losses come from differentiating:

\[
\text{AFE smoothing weights},
\qquad
\text{gamma factors},
\qquad
\text{saddle/conductor-dependent amplitudes}.
\]

At derivative order

\[
K=2R+1,
\]

standard smooth-weight and gamma/Stirling differentiation costs are usually of the form

\[
C^K K!
\]

or, more generally,

\[
e^{O(K\log K)}.
\]

With

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
K\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

so

\[
e^{O(K\log K)}
=
e^{O(\log Q)}
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}
}
\]

at the preferred depth.

This is the main reason the normalized Wronskian route remains canonically feasible.

---

# 5. What breaks at \(R=O(\log Q)\)

If instead

\[
R=c\log Q,
\]

then

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
e^{O(\log Q\log\log Q)}
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)}.
\]

That is not a fixed polynomial power of \(Q\).

The following become non-polynomial or at least severe:

\[
K!,
\qquad
\text{high derivatives of AFE cutoffs},
\qquad
\text{gamma-factor derivative constants},
\qquad
\text{determinant perturbation constants},
\qquad
\text{Remez/Bernstein constants},
\qquad
\text{filter-polynomial coefficient growth}.
\]

So the \(R=O(\log Q)\) version should be treated as **not canonically safe** unless a special lemma removes factorial-type losses.

---

# 6. \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) audit

## \(B_2\)

The Wronskian must include

\[
\mathcal D^kB_2,
\qquad 0\le k\le 2R+1.
\]

Dropping \(B_2\) is invalid because the bad event is a cancellation event. \(B_2\) may shift the affine target for flattening.

Required bound:

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kB_2|
\le Q^{C}.
\]

This is plausible, since \(B_2\) is smooth background/gamma data, but it must be part of the determinant or the inhomogeneous target.

## \(D_2\)

The dual term must be included:

\[
\mathcal D^kD_2,
\qquad 0\le k\le 2R+1.
\]

A Wronskian theorem for \(P_2\) or \(B_2+P_2\) alone is not canonical. The previous sprint already established that main/dual filtering does not automatically remove \(D_2\); it merely shifts the nonrecurrence problem.

Required bound if \(D_2\) is treated as an error:

\[
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kD_2|
\le Q^{-C},
\]

which is generally not credible. Therefore \(D_2\) should be structurally included.

## \(E_2\)

The remainder may be treated as an error only if

\[
\boxed{
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
}
\]

This is the hardest canonical bookkeeping item apart from the determinant lower bound itself.

---

# 7. Critical-line and tail treatment

If the proof runs purely through the canonical AFE identity

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

then critical-line zero regularization and zero-tail truncation are hidden inside the validity of that canonical identity.

If the proof switches to a zero-side kernel representation, it must prove high-derivative tail control:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
\left\|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal Z_W}^{\rm reg}
K_2(\cdot;\rho)
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho^\ast)}
\le
Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
}
\]

Also, any critical-line regularization must commute with derivatives through order

\[
2R+1.
\]

Otherwise the proof is a zero-kernel proxy theorem, not a canonical theorem.

---

# 8. Ordinary and singular packet scales

The natural normalized derivative is

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

For ordinary packet scale, one expects

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so normalized derivatives of AFE phases are \(O(1)\).

For singular/shallow packet scale, \(\lambda Q\) may be much smaller. Then

\[
(\lambda\log n)^k
\]

can suppress high derivative rows and damage the Wronskian’s effective rank.

Therefore the normalized Wronskian route must choose one of two paths:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Path A: prove the Wronskian theorem only in the ordinary scale and handle singular scale by dominance.}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Path B: prove a }\lambda Q\text{-dependent Wronskian theorem for singular scale.}
}
\]

Without one of these, singular packets remain Yellow.

---

# 9. Route classification

| Version of Wronskian route | Classification | Reason |
|---|---:|---|
| Raw \(\partial_m\)-Wronskian | **Yellow/Red** | Derivative powers create \(Q^{O(R^2)}\)-type scaling unless completely renormalized. |
| Normalized \(\mathcal D\)-Wronskian with \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\) | **Green feasible** | Derivative, smoothing, and determinant perturbation losses remain \(Q^{O(1)}\). |
| Normalized \(\mathcal D\)-Wronskian with \(R=O(\log Q)\) | **Yellow/Red** | Factorial and smoothing losses become \(Q^{O(\log\log Q)}\), not fixed polynomial. |
| \(P_2\)-only determinant theorem | **Red** | Does not prove canonical \(q''_{\can}\). |
| \(B_2+P_2+D_2\) determinant theorem with \(E_2\) controlled through \(2R+1\) | **Green feasible** | Correct object, assuming determinant lower bound and finite-jet transfer. |
| Zero-side finite truncation theorem | **Yellow** | Needs high-derivative regularized-tail and critical-line convergence estimates. |

---

# 10. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{The normalized Wronskian route is Green feasible, but only with a hard AFE derivative theorem.}
}
\]

The required canonical package is:

\[
\boxed{
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m\text{ or }\Delta\partial_m,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\max_{k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-C_E},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
B_2+P_2+D_2
\text{ included structurally, not treated as optional correction terms,}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual fixed-coefficient canonical determinant.

So the route is **not Red** on derivative/error grounds. But it is still **Yellow overall** until two hard inputs are supplied:

1. the high-derivative canonical AFE error theorem through order \(2R+1\);
2. the normalized fixed actual-zeta Wronskian lower bound.

## Agent 6 / F — Canonical derivative/error budget for normalized Wronskian

The current route is:

\[
\text{normalized Wronskian/transversality}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite-jet anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 1}.
\]

The coordinator brief correctly restricts the Wronskian route to normalized derivatives,

\[
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\]

with preferred depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and requires the canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

No proxy Wronskian counts. 

---

# 1. Exact highest derivative orders

The normalized Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det(\mathcal D^\ell G_j(m,\alpha))_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

For source rows,

\[
\mathcal D^\ell G_{j+1}
=
\mathcal D^{j+\ell}q''_{\can}.
\]

The maximum is attained when

\[
j=R,\qquad \ell=R+1,
\]

hence the Wronskian requires

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{2R+1}q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta'',
\]

this is equivalent to physical derivatives of \(q_\zeta\) through order

\[
\boxed{
2R+3.
}
\]

For the off-line row,

\[
\mathcal D^\ell Z_\alpha,
\qquad 0\le \ell\le R+1,
\]

so the required order is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha.
}
\]

---

# 2. Canonical derivative budget table

| Object | Required normalized derivatives | Physical derivative order |
|---|---:|---:|
| \(q''_{\can}\) | \(\mathcal D^kq''_{\can}\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) | \(\partial_m^k q''_{\can}\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) |
| \(q_\zeta\) | induced by \(q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''\) | \(\partial_m^k q_\zeta\), \(0\le k\le 2R+3\) |
| \(Z_\alpha\) | \(\mathcal D^kZ_\alpha\), \(0\le k\le R+1\) | \(\partial_m^kZ_\alpha\), \(0\le k\le R+1\) |
| \(B_2\) | \(\mathcal D^kB_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) | \(\partial_m^kB_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) |
| \(P_2\) | \(\mathcal D^kP_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) | \(\partial_m^kP_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) |
| \(D_2\) | \(\mathcal D^kD_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) | \(\partial_m^kD_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) |
| \(E_2\) | \(\mathcal D^kE_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) | \(\partial_m^kE_2\), \(0\le k\le 2R+1\) |

The core canonical requirement is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
\quad
\text{on }I_\rho^\ast.
}
\]

This is the required high-derivative AFE error theorem.

---

# 3. Does the \(E_2\) error remain polynomially controllable?

Let

\[
N=R+2
\]

be the determinant size. Suppose the canonical main matrix has normalized entries bounded by

\[
Q^{C_0},
\]

and the desired Wronskian lower bound is

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

A crude determinant perturbation bound requires roughly

\[
\boxed{
\max_{k\le 2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le
Q^{-A-C_0(N-1)}e^{-O(N\log N)}.
}
\]

At

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So the perturbation budget is still a fixed polynomial power of \(Q\). This is severe but feasible in principle.

At

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

the same factor becomes

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which is not acceptable under fixed-polynomial \(Q^{O(1)}\) bookkeeping.

---

# 4. Smoothing weights and gamma factors

High derivatives of AFE smoothing weights, gamma factors, saddle terms, and conductor-dependent amplitudes typically produce losses of the form

\[
C^K K!
\]

or

\[
e^{O(K\log K)},
\]

where

\[
K=2R+1.
\]

With

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this gives

\[
e^{O(K\log K)}
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore the normalized Wronskian is not killed by high derivatives at the preferred depth.

But with

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

the same loss is

\[
Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which is no longer fixed-polynomial. Thus \(R=O(\log Q)\) should be rejected unless a special AFE/weight lemma eliminates factorial derivative losses.

---

# 5. \(B_2,D_2,E_2\) requirements

## \(B_2\)

The background term must be included structurally:

\[
\mathcal D^kq''_{\can}
=
\mathcal D^k(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2).
\]

Dropping \(B_2\) is invalid because the bad locus is a cancellation locus. \(B_2\) can shift the flattening target.

Required:

\[
\max_{k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kB_2|
\le Q^C.
\]

This is plausible because \(B_2\) is smooth/gamma-background, but it must be proved or recorded.

## \(D_2\)

The dual term cannot be treated as negligible by default. The earlier sprint already found that main/dual filtering does not automatically eliminate \(D_2\); it shifts the nonrecurrence burden.

Thus the determinant must include

\[
B_2+P_2+D_2.
\]

A \(P_2\)-only determinant theorem is **Red**.

## \(E_2\)

\(E_2\) may be treated perturbatively only if

\[
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-C_E}
\]

for \(C_E\) exceeding the determinant perturbation loss.

This is the main canonical analytic theorem needed besides the determinant lower bound.

---

# 6. Critical-line and tail treatment

If the Wronskian is proved through the canonical AFE identity,

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

then critical-line zero treatment and zero-tail regularization are absorbed into that identity.

If the proof switches to the zero side, it must prove high-derivative tail control:

\[
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
\left\|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal Z_W}^{\rm reg}
K_2(\cdot;\rho)
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho^\ast)}
\le
Q^{-C}|I_\rho|^{1/2}.
\]

It must also show that the critical-line regularization commutes with all derivatives through order

\[
2R+1.
\]

Otherwise the zero-side proof remains a proxy theorem.

---

# 7. Ordinary versus singular packet scale

The natural normalization is

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m.
\]

For ordinary packets one expects

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

so the normalized frequencies

\[
\lambda\log n
\]

are \(O(1)\) on the active AFE conductor range.

For singular or shallow packets, \(\lambda Q\) may be much smaller. Then high normalized derivatives can become rank-deficient because

\[
(\lambda\log n)^k
\]

may be tiny.

So the route needs an explicit split:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packets: normalized Wronskian theorem;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular packets: dominance argument or a separate }\lambda Q\text{-dependent determinant theorem.}
}
\]

Without this split, the route is only Yellow.

---

# 8. What becomes non-polynomial at \(R=O(\log Q)\)

At \(R=O(\log Q)\), the following no longer have fixed-polynomial bounds unless new structure is proved:

\[
R!,
\]

\[
e^{O(R\log R)},
\]

\[
\text{smooth cutoff derivative constants},
\]

\[
\text{gamma/Stirling derivative constants},
\]

\[
\text{determinant perturbation constants},
\]

\[
\text{Remez/Bernstein finite-jet transfer constants},
\]

\[
\text{filter-polynomial coefficient growth}.
\]

Therefore the safe depth is not the conservative \(O(\log Q)\) depth but specifically

\[
\boxed{
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
}
\]

---

# 9. Route classification

| Route version | Classification | Reason |
|---|---:|---|
| Raw \(\partial_m\)-Wronskian | **Yellow/Red** | Raw derivatives create uncontrolled \(Q^{O(R^2)}\)-type scaling unless fully normalized. |
| Normalized \(\mathcal D\)-Wronskian, \(R\asymp\log Q/\log\log Q\) | **Green feasible** | Derivative, smoothing, gamma, and determinant perturbation losses can remain \(Q^{O(1)}\). |
| Normalized \(\mathcal D\)-Wronskian, \(R=O(\log Q)\) | **Yellow/Red** | Factorial/gamma/smoothing losses become \(Q^{O(\log\log Q)}\). |
| \(P_2\)-only Wronskian | **Red** | Not canonical. Omits \(B_2,D_2,E_2\). |
| \(B_2+P_2+D_2\) Wronskian with \(E_2\) controlled through \(2R+1\) | **Green feasible** | Correct canonical object, assuming determinant lower bound and finite-jet transfer. |
| Zero-side finite-zero Wronskian | **Yellow** | Needs high-derivative tail and critical-line regularization transfer. |

---

# 10. Final classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Normalized Wronskian route: Green feasible on derivative/error grounds.}
}
\]

But the full route remains

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow overall}
}
\]

until two hard inputs are supplied:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual fixed-coefficient canonical determinant.

So there is no derivative-budget obstruction at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The real remaining obstruction is arithmetic: proving the normalized fixed actual-zeta Wronskian lower bound at admissible centers.

## Agent 6 / F — Canonical AFE derivative theorem through \(2R+1\)

The current Wronskian route is explicitly constrained to the full canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

with normalized derivatives

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m,
\]

and safe depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The attached coordinator brief correctly identifies the remaining route as basis-normalized Wronskian plus \(Z_\alpha\)-rank plus actual determinant incidence exclusion, and assigns Agent 6 the high-derivative AFE error theorem. 

---

# 1. Required derivative order

The Wronskian uses

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^j q''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R,
\]

and entries

\[
\mathcal D^\ell G_j,
\qquad
0\le j,\ell\le R+1.
\]

For the source rows,

\[
\mathcal D^\ell G_{j+1}
=
\mathcal D^{j+\ell}q''_{\can}.
\]

The highest order occurs at

\[
j=R,\qquad \ell=R+1,
\]

so the required source derivative is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{2R+1}q''_{\can}.
}
\]

Since

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta'',
\]

this means physical derivatives of \(q_\zeta\) through

\[
\boxed{
2R+3.
}
\]

For the off-line row,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D^{R+1}Z_\alpha
}
\]

is required.

---

# 2. Canonical smoothed AFE form

The canonical form needed is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m).
}
\]

A sufficiently precise smoothed model should have the shape

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
c_n(m)\,
V_2\!\left(\frac{n}{N(m)}\right)
e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
D_2(m)
=
\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
d_n(m)\,
V_2^\ast\!\left(\frac{n}{N^\ast(m)}\right)
e^{i\Theta(m)}e^{+im\log n},
\]

where:

\[
B_2(m)
\]

contains the completed gamma/conductor background,

\[
P_2
\]

is the main AFE block,

\[
D_2
\]

is the dual folded AFE block, and

\[
E_2
\]

is the residual after smoothing, contour shift, and truncation.

This must be an identity for the **same** \(q''_{\can}\) used in Gate 1. If this decomposition is only for a proxy phase, a truncated zero kernel, or a \(P_2\)-only main term, it is not canonical.

---

# 3. Required error theorem

The Wronskian route needs:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

uniformly for

\[
m\in I_\rho^\ast.
\]

This is stronger than a scalar AFE error estimate. It requires high normalized derivative control through the full Wronskian order.

A clean theorem candidate is:

## High-derivative canonical AFE error theorem

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
R\le c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
K=2R+1.
\]

Let \(I_\rho^\ast\) be the enlarged packet interval, and suppose the normalized scale satisfies

\[
\lambda Q\asymp 1
\]

or, more generally, the chosen \(\mathcal D\) is normalized so that active AFE phases obey

\[
|\mathcal D(m\log n)|\ll 1
\]

on the active conductor range. Assume the smoothed canonical AFE for \(q''_{\can}\) extends analytically to a complex tube

\[
\mathcal U
=
\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I_\rho^\ast)\le c_0/Q\}
\]

and satisfies

\[
\sup_{z\in\mathcal U}|E_2(z)|
\le Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Then for \(0\le k\le K\),

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
Q^{-A_0+C_1},
\]

where \(C_1\) is fixed if

\[
K\ll \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Thus, choosing

\[
A_0\ge C_E+C_1
\]

gives

\[
\max_{k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
\]

### Proof sketch

Cauchy’s estimate on the tube gives

\[
|\partial_m^kE_2(m)|
\le
k!\left(\frac{Q}{c_0}\right)^k Q^{-A_0}.
\]

Multiplying by \(\lambda^k\), with \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), gives

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
k! C^k Q^{-A_0}.
\]

For

\[
k\le K\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
k!C^k
\le
\exp(O(k\log k))
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
Q^{-A_0+O(1)}.
\]

This is the desired polynomial derivative stability.

---

# 4. Smoothing parameter requirements

The AFE smoothing must be analytic or sufficiently Gevrey-regular. Hard cutoffs are not acceptable.

The smoothing parameters should be chosen so that:

\[
V_2(y),\quad V_2^\ast(y)
\]

satisfy derivative bounds of the form

\[
|y^a\partial_y^aV_2(y)|
+
|y^a\partial_y^aV_2^\ast(y)|
\le
C^a a!
\]

for

\[
a\le 2R+1.
\]

This produces losses

\[
C^K K!
=
\exp(O(K\log K)).
\]

At

\[
K=2R+1
\asymp
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\exp(O(R\log R))
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So smoothing losses remain polynomial.

---

# 5. Gamma/Stirling and conductor dependence

The gamma and conductor factors must be differentiated through order \(2R+1\).

For the gamma/background part, one needs estimates of the form:

\[
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kB_2(m)|
\le Q^C.
\]

For AFE amplitudes and saddle terms, one needs:

\[
\mathcal D^k c_n(m),
\quad
\mathcal D^k d_n(m),
\quad
\mathcal D^k \Theta(m),
\quad
\mathcal D^k N(m),
\]

to cost at most

\[
e^{O(k\log k)}Q^C.
\]

This is plausible under standard Stirling-type differentiation because:

\[
\Theta'(m)\asymp Q,
\]

and normalization by

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m,
\qquad
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

makes first derivatives \(O(1)\), while higher derivatives of gamma/conductor data are smaller or factorial-controlled.

Thus gamma and saddle movement are not fatal at the preferred \(R\).

---

# 6. Truncation tails

The main and dual sums must be smoothed and truncated with enough slack that tails remain negligible after \(2R+1\) normalized derivatives.

A sufficient tail requirement is:

\[
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
\left|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{n\notin\mathcal N_{\rm trunc}}
c_n(m)
V_2\!\left(\frac{n}{N(m)}\right)
e^{-im\log n}
\right|
\le Q^{-C_E},
\]

and similarly for the dual block.

Because each normalized derivative contributes roughly

\[
(\lambda\log n)^k,
\]

this remains polynomial if the active/truncated range satisfies

\[
\lambda\log n\ll 1
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda\log n=O(1),
\]

which is the ordinary packet normalization. The smoothing tails must decay by more than the polynomial loss

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}.
\]

---

# 7. Verification of the key growth identity

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
R\log R
=
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\left(
\log\log Q-\log\log\log Q+O(1)
\right)
=
O(\log Q).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

This validates the derivative/error budget at the chosen depth.

For

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

we instead get

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
e^{O(\log Q\log\log Q)}
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which is not a fixed polynomial power of \(Q\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\text{ is canonically safe;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
R=O(\log Q)
\text{ is not safe without a special no-factorial-loss lemma.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Canonical obstruction list

The normalized Wronskian becomes non-canonical or invalid if any of the following occur.

## Obstruction 1 — \(E_2\) only controlled at order zero

A scalar estimate

\[
|E_2|\le Q^{-C}
\]

is insufficient unless it holds analytically in a complex tube, allowing Cauchy differentiation. Otherwise high derivatives of \(E_2\) may destroy the determinant.

## Obstruction 2 — hard cutoff AFE

Hard truncation creates derivative boundary terms and prevents clean high-order control. The AFE must be smoothed.

## Obstruction 3 — \(P_2\)-only treatment

A theorem for

\[
P_2
\]

or

\[
B_2+P_2
\]

does not prove a theorem for

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The dual term \(D_2\) is structurally active.

## Obstruction 4 — singular packet scale

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll1,
\]

then derivative error control may be easier, but Wronskian rank may degenerate because

\[
(\lambda\log n)^k
\]

becomes small. Singular packets need either a dominance argument or a separate \(\lambda Q\)-dependent Wronskian theorem.

## Obstruction 5 — log-derivative singularities near zeros

If \(q''_{\can}\) is represented through a logarithmic derivative or phase derivative, then a uniform AFE in a complex tube may fail near actual zeros unless the singular part is explicitly included in the canonical object. This is the main conceptual risk.

A valid proof must either:

\[
\text{work with a canonical completed-phase AFE that already includes this behavior,}
\]

or

\[
\text{split off singular zero contributions and prove tail/error control separately.}
\]

## Obstruction 6 — \(R=O(\log Q)\)

At this depth, factorial/gamma/smoothing losses become

\[
Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which breaks the fixed-polynomial budget.

---

# 9. Final theorem candidate

The required canonical analytic input can be stated as follows.

## Theorem candidate: high-derivative smoothed AFE for \(q''_{\can}\)

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
R\le c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
K=2R+1.
\]

Let \(I_\rho^\ast\) be an enlarged packet interval with ordinary normalized scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Assume the completed canonical curvature admits a smoothed AFE

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]

on a complex \(c/Q\)-tube around \(I_\rho^\ast\), with analytic smoothing and exact completed gamma/conductor convention. Then for every prescribed \(C_E>0\), the smoothing/truncation parameters may be chosen so that

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
}
\]

Moreover,

\[
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kB_2(m)|
\le Q^{C_B},
\]

and the corresponding differentiated main and dual AFE blocks have only

\[
Q^{O(1)}
\]

loss from smoothing, gamma factors, saddle motion, and truncation.

---

# 10. Route classification

\[
\boxed{
\text{Derivative/error budget: Green feasible at }
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
}
\]

But this is not a proof of Gate 1. The whole Wronskian route remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Yellow overall.}
}
\]

Two hard inputs are still required:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

as a formal canonical AFE theorem, and

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

as the actual arithmetic determinant incidence theorem.

No derivative-budget obstruction kills the route at the safe depth. The remaining obstruction is arithmetic, not analytic bookkeeping.

## Agent 6 / F — Smoothed canonical AFE derivative theorem with ordinary/singular split

The current instruction is to formalize the high-derivative canonical AFE theorem needed for the normalized Wronskian route, while separating ordinary packet scale from singular/shallow packet scale. The coordinator brief identifies the unresolved theorem as the actual incidence bound at \(Z_\alpha\)-centers and assigns Agent 6 the canonical AFE derivative theorem with ordinary/singular split. 

---

# 1. Required canonical AFE statement

The Wronskian route must use the full canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

not a main-term-only approximation. The needed theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

where

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

Here \(I_\rho^\ast\) is an enlarged packet interval around \(I_\rho\), large enough to support Cauchy estimates or finite-jet-to-energy propagation.

The exact derivative order is:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}: \mathcal D^k,\ 0\le k\le 2R+1,
}
\]

equivalently

\[
\boxed{
q_\zeta: \partial_m^j,\ 0\le j\le 2R+3.
}
\]

For the off-line equation,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha: \mathcal D^k,\ 0\le k\le R+1.
}
\]

---

# 2. Smoothed canonical AFE theorem candidate

A usable theorem should be stated as follows.

## Theorem candidate: high-derivative smoothed AFE for \(q''_{\can}\)

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
R\le c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
K=2R+1.
\]

Let \(I_\rho^\ast\) be an enlarged packet interval. Suppose \(q''_{\can}\) admits a smoothed completed AFE on a complex tube

\[
\mathcal U=\{z:\operatorname{dist}(z,I_\rho^\ast)\le \tau/Q\},
\]

of the form

\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_n c_n^+(m)
V_2^+\!\left(\frac{n}{N^+(m)}\right)
e^{-im\log n},
\]

\[
D_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_n c_n^-(m)
V_2^-\!\left(\frac{n}{N^-(m)}\right)
e^{i\Theta(m)}e^{+im\log n},
\]

and \(B_2\) contains the completed gamma/conductor background. Assume the smoothing weights are analytic/Gevrey with

\[
\left|y^a\partial_y^aV_2^\pm(y)\right|
\le C^a a!,
\qquad
0\le a\le K.
\]

If the residual satisfies

\[
\sup_{z\in\mathcal U}|E_2(z)|\le Q^{-A_0},
\]

then for every \(0\le k\le K\),

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
Q^{-A_0+O(1)}
\]

provided the normalized derivative obeys

\[
|\mathcal D(m\log n)|\ll 1
\]

on the active AFE range.

Thus, choosing \(A_0\) sufficiently large gives

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le 2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Proof outline by Cauchy estimates

If \(E_2\) is analytic in a tube of radius

\[
r\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

then Cauchy gives

\[
|\partial_m^kE_2(m)|
\le
k!r^{-k}Q^{-A_0}
\asymp
k!Q^kQ^{-A_0}.
\]

If

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

and ordinary packet scale gives

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\]

then

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
k!(\lambda Q)^kQ^{-A_0}
\le
k!C^kQ^{-A_0}.
\]

For

\[
k\le K=2R+1,
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
k!C^k
\le
\exp(O(k\log k))
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le
Q^{-A_0+O(1)}.
\]

This proves the desired high-derivative stability after choosing \(A_0\) larger than the determinant perturbation budget.

---

# 4. Loss accounting

The following losses must be included.

## Smoothing weights

Analytic/Gevrey smoothing contributes

\[
C^k k!
=
e^{O(k\log k)}.
\]

At \(k\le 2R+1\),

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
\]

Hard cutoffs are not acceptable.

## Conductor dependence

Derivatives of

\[
N^\pm(m),
\qquad
V_2^\pm(n/N^\pm(m))
\]

must satisfy

\[
|\mathcal D^k N^\pm(m)|,\ 
|\mathcal D^k V_2^\pm(n/N^\pm(m))|
\le
Q^{O(1)}e^{O(k\log k)}.
\]

This is plausible under smooth conductor dependence because normalized derivatives remove the leading \(Q^k\)-growth.

## Gamma/Stirling factors

Gamma derivatives and saddle phases must obey

\[
|\mathcal D^k\Theta(m)|
+
|\mathcal D^k c_n^\pm(m)|
\le
Q^{O(1)}e^{O(k\log k)}.
\]

This is compatible with Stirling expansions at depth

\[
k\ll\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

## Saddle movement

Differentiating the AFE saddle or transition point can produce factorial-type combinatorics. This remains safe only if all such losses are bounded by

\[
e^{O(k\log k)}.
\]

Any \(e^{O(k^2)}\) saddle-motion loss would need separate treatment, because at

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

it gives

\[
e^{O(R^2)}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{(\log\log Q)^2}\right)
\right),
\]

which is not \(Q^{O(1)}\).

## Truncation tails

The main and dual sums must be truncated only after smoothing. Required:

\[
\max_{0\le k\le K}
\left|
\mathcal D^k
\sum_{n\notin\mathcal N_{\rm trunc}}
c_n^\pm(m)
V_2^\pm(n/N^\pm(m))
e^{\mp im\log n}
\right|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
\]

The tail decay must beat

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}.
\]

---

# 5. Verification of the key growth identity

At the safe depth,

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
R\log R
=
\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\left(\log\log Q-\log\log\log Q+O(1)\right)
=
O(\log Q).
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

This is the analytic reason the high-derivative AFE package is feasible.

If instead

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

then

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)},
\]

which is not fixed-polynomial. Thus \(R=O(\log Q)\) is not safe unless a special no-factorial-loss lemma is available.

---

# 6. Ordinary packet scale

For ordinary packet scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Then

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

is the correct normalization, since

\[
\mathcal D(e^{-im\log n})
=
-i(\lambda\log n)e^{-im\log n},
\]

and on the active AFE range

\[
\lambda\log n=O(1).
\]

So ordinary scale is compatible with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{basis-normalized Wronskian + high-derivative AFE control.}
}
\]

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packets: Wronskian route is analytically Green-feasible.}
}
\]

The remaining issue there is arithmetic incidence, not derivative/error control.

---

# 7. Singular or shallow packet scale

For singular/shallow scale,

\[
\lambda Q\ll1.
\]

Then high-derivative error control becomes easier:

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le
k!(\lambda Q)^kQ^{-A_0},
\]

which is no worse than ordinary scale.

But Wronskian rank becomes worse, because the frequency nodes

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

may collapse toward zero. Then the rows

\[
1,\ x_n,\ x_n^2,\ldots,x_n^R
\]

or their basis-normalized analogues may lose effective rank.

So in singular scale, the analytic AFE theorem is not the problem. The determinant rank is.

There are three possible treatments.

## Option A — singular dominance outside Wronskian

Use a local singular-packet dominance argument to prove Gate 1/Gate 2 directly, without the Wronskian. This is the preferred route if available.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{best option for singular packets.}
}
\]

## Option B — \(\lambda Q\)-dependent Wronskian

Prove a determinant theorem with explicit dependence on

\[
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

The lower bound would degrade like

\[
\mu^{C R}
\]

or worse. This is acceptable only if

\[
\mu^{CR}\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\mu\ge Q^{-A/(CR)}.
\]

For

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this threshold is roughly

\[
\mu\ge e^{-O(\log\log Q)}=(\log Q)^{-O(1)}.
\]

Thus a \(\lambda Q\)-dependent Wronskian might handle mildly singular packets, but not very shallow packets.

## Option C — additional singular AFE theorem

One could build an AFE theorem adapted to the smaller scale by using lower primes or modified active blocks. But if

\[
\lambda\log p
\]

is too small for all useful primes, the Wronskian still lacks rank.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{possible only for mildly singular packets; not a general cure.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Ordinary/singular split recommendation

The clean split is:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\gtrsim (\log Q)^{-C}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{use normalized Wronskian with explicit }\mu=\lambda Q\text{ losses.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{do not use Wronskian; use singular dominance or a separate local argument.}
}
\]

This prevents singular-scale rank collapse from contaminating the ordinary-scale Wronskian theorem.

---

# 9. Final classification

| Component | Ordinary scale \(\lambda Q\asymp1\) | Mild singular \(\lambda Q\ge(\log Q)^{-C}\) | Deep singular \(\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}\) |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| High-derivative \(E_2\) control | **Green feasible** | **Green feasible** | **Green feasible** |
| Gamma/smoothing losses | **\(Q^{O(1)}\)** | **\(Q^{O(1)}\)** | **\(Q^{O(1)}\)** |
| Wronskian rank | **Feasible** | **Possible with \(\mu\)-losses** | **Likely rank-degenerate** |
| Recommended treatment | Wronskian | \(\mu\)-dependent Wronskian or dominance | Singular dominance/local argument |
| Overall status | **Yellow only due to incidence theorem** | **Yellow/severe** | **Do not route through Wronskian** |

---

# 10. Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{The smoothed canonical AFE derivative theorem is Green-feasible at }
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
}
\]

A precise theorem should assert:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

after analytic smoothing and canonical main/dual decomposition.

For packet scales:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\asymp1:
\text{ Wronskian analytically feasible.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\ll1:
\text{ derivative control remains feasible, but Wronskian rank may collapse.}
}
\]

Thus the ordinary-scale Wronskian route remains analytically sound, but still Yellow overall because the core arithmetic incidence theorem is unproved:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Singular scale should not be forced through the same Wronskian unless a \(\lambda Q\)-dependent determinant theorem is explicitly proved.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:38:10)

_Thought for 11s_

## Agent 6 / F — Ordinary/singular split and canonical AFE package

The latest coordinator brief corrects the active-block picture: low-prime plateau blocks are useful for \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol sanity checks, but probably not for the packet-scale Wronskian determinant because \(x_p=\lambda\log p\ll1\) at ordinary scale. The Wronskian determinant should use packet-frequency blocks with \(\lambda\log n\asymp1\). 

---

# 1. Canonical object and required AFE package

The Wronskian route must use

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

with the fixed gamma/background term

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

The required high-derivative AFE theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}
}
\]

where

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal D=\Delta\partial_m.
\]

This is the analytic input needed before any determinant theorem can be treated as canonical.

---

# 2. Exact derivative-order budget

For the basis-normalized Wronskian, take

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^jq''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R,
\]

and column operators \(C_\ell(\mathcal D)\) of degree at most \(R+1\). Then

\[
C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_{j+1}
\]

requires derivatives of \(q''_{\can}\) up to order

\[
j+\deg C_\ell\le R+(R+1)=2R+1.
\]

Thus the exact derivative budget is:

| Object | Required normalized derivative order |
|---|---:|
| \(q''_{\can}\) | \(0\le k\le2R+1\) |
| \(q_\zeta\), since \(q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''\) | physical order \(0\le k\le2R+3\) |
| \(Z_\alpha\) | \(0\le k\le R+1\) |
| \(B_2\) | \(0\le k\le2R+1\) |
| \(P_2\) | \(0\le k\le2R+1\) |
| \(D_2\) | \(0\le k\le2R+1\) |
| \(E_2\) | \(0\le k\le2R+1\) |

A theorem controlling only \(E_2\) at order zero is insufficient. The Wronskian needs uniform high-derivative error control through \(2R+1\).

---

# 3. Ordinary-scale theorem

Let

\[
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

For ordinary packet scale,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

Then packet-frequency blocks satisfy

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

so the determinant should use frequencies with

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

A suitable ordinary-scale AFE theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
&q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),\\
&\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}\max_{k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|\le Q^{-C_E},\\
&\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}\max_{k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kB_2(m)|\le Q^{C_B},
\end{aligned}
}
\]

with \(P_2,D_2\) smoothed and differentiated termwise through order \(2R+1\), incurring only \(Q^{O(1)}\) loss.

The proof mechanism is Cauchy plus analytic smoothing. If \(E_2\) is analytic in a tube of radius \(\asymp Q^{-1}\), then

\[
|\partial_m^kE_2|
\le k!Q^kQ^{-A_0}.
\]

Multiplying by \(\lambda^k\) gives

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le k!(\lambda Q)^kQ^{-A_0}
\le k!C^kQ^{-A_0}.
\]

For

\[
k\le2R+1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

\[
k!C^k
=
e^{O(k\log k)}
=
Q^{O(1)}.
\]

So choosing \(A_0\) large enough gives the desired \(Q^{-C_E}\) bound.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary scale }(\lambda Q\asymp1):
\text{ Green feasible analytically.}
}
\]

The remaining obstruction is not AFE differentiability; it is the arithmetic incidence theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

---

# 4. Mildly singular theorem with \(\mu=\lambda Q\) losses

For mildly singular packets,

\[
\mu=\lambda Q<1
\]

but not too small. Cauchy gives

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le
k!\mu^kQ^{-A_0}.
\]

So the \(E_2\)-error is no harder; it is easier.

The difficulty is determinant rank. On packet-frequency nodes,

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n,
\]

the active node spread scales with \(\mu\). A basis-normalized determinant may lose powers like

\[
\mu^{-CR}
\]

or, depending on the basis/minor theorem,

\[
\mu^{-CR^2}.
\]

A feasible mildly singular theorem would need a determinant package of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_\mu}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{basis-conditioning and minor losses remain }Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

If losses are \(\mu^{-CR}\), then

\[
\mu^{-CR}
\le
(\log Q)^{C C_\mu R}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(
\frac{\log Q\log\log\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\right)
\right)
=
Q^{o(1)},
\]

which is acceptable.

If losses are \(\mu^{-CR^2}\), then

\[
\mu^{-CR^2}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(
\frac{(\log Q)^2\log\log\log Q}{(\log\log Q)^2}
\right)
\right),
\]

which is not fixed-polynomial in \(Q\). So the mildly singular route is feasible only if the basis-normalized construction keeps \(\mu\)-loss essentially linear in \(R\), not quadratic.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mild singular }(\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}):
\text{ Yellow; feasible only with explicit }\mu\text{-loss control.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Deep singular exclusion from Wronskian route

For deep singular packets,

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

Then

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

collapses for the AFE frequencies, and the rows generated by

\[
1,x_n,x_n^2,\ldots,x_n^R
\]

or their basis-normalized analogues become effectively rank-deficient unless one pays unacceptable \(\mu^{-CR}\) or \(\mu^{-CR^2}\) losses.

The AFE derivative theorem may still be true, but the determinant cannot be expected to retain stable packet-scale rank.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{do not route through Wronskian.}
}
\]

Deep singular packets should be handled by one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular dominance/local packet argument}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{separate singular-scale Gate 1/Gate 2 lemma.}
}
\]

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular scale: Red for ordinary Wronskian; handle separately.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Loss accounting

The analytic package is acceptable only if all high-derivative losses are bounded by

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}.
\]

At the safe depth,

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

we have

\[
R\log R=O(\log Q),
\]

hence

\[
\boxed{
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)}.
}
\]

Allowed losses:

\[
C^k k!,
\qquad
e^{O(k\log k)},
\qquad
Q^{O(1)}e^{O(k\log k)}.
\]

Dangerous losses:

\[
e^{O(k^2)},
\qquad
Q^{O(k)},
\qquad
\mu^{-O(k^2)}
\]

unless separately normalized away.

This is why \(R=O(\log Q)\) remains unsafe:

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}
=
Q^{O(\log\log Q)}.
\]

---

# 7. Canonical route classification

| Regime | AFE derivative control | Wronskian rank | Route classification |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| Ordinary: \(\lambda Q\asymp1\) | Green feasible | Green feasible, assuming packet-frequency blocks | **Green feasible analytically; Yellow overall due to incidence theorem** |
| Mild singular: \(\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}\) | Green feasible | Yellow, depends on explicit \(\mu\)-loss | **Yellow** |
| Deep singular: \(\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}\) | Green feasible | rank-degenerate | **Do not use ordinary Wronskian** |

---

# 8. Final deliverable theorem package

The route should be formalized as three separate analytic statements.

## Ordinary canonical AFE theorem

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\asymp1,\quad
R\le c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\Rightarrow
\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-C_E}.
}
\]

## Mild singular canonical AFE theorem

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q=\mu\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C},
\quad
R\le c\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\Rightarrow
\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-C_E},
}
\]

with a separate determinant-conditioning theorem carrying explicit \(\mu\)-loss.

## Deep singular exclusion

\[
\boxed{
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{exclude from Wronskian route and use singular dominance/local analysis.}
}
\]

---

# Bottom line

The canonical analytic package is **not** the current blocker.

At ordinary packet scale, the smoothed high-derivative AFE theorem is Green-feasible:

\[
\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-C_E}.
\]

At mild singular scale, it remains analytically feasible but determinant rank must pay explicit \(\mu=\lambda Q\) losses.

At deep singular scale, the Wronskian should be abandoned in favor of singular dominance/local packet arguments.

Thus the corrected route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian}
+
\text{canonical high-derivative AFE}
+
\text{actual arithmetic incidence theorem}.
}
\]

The only remaining Green-blocking theorem is still:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]
