_Thought for 6s_

## Agent 6 / F — Singular branch separation and ordinary-route formal package

The latest instruction correctly narrows the ordinary Wronskian route to **packet-frequency blocks** with

\[
\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

not low-prime plateau blocks. The unresolved blocker is still the actual arithmetic incidence theorem at \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros, while the ordinary-scale analytic package remains feasible. 

---

# 1. Ordinary-scale theorem package

Work in the ordinary packet regime

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\]

with safe jet depth

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Use the normalized derivative

\[
\mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m
\]

or equivalently \(\Delta\partial_m\), provided \(\Delta Q\asymp1\).

The canonical object must be

\[
q''_{\can}
=
B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

where

\[
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
\]

The required high-derivative AFE theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}
\max_{0\le k\le2R+1}
|\mathcal D^kE_2(m)|
\le Q^{-C_E}.
}
\]

Derivative-order budget:

\[
q''_{\can}:\quad 0\le k\le2R+1,
\]

\[
q_\zeta:\quad 0\le k\le2R+3,
\]

\[
Z_\alpha:\quad 0\le k\le R+1,
\]

\[
B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2:\quad 0\le k\le2R+1.
\]

At this depth,

\[
e^{O(R\log R)}=Q^{O(1)},
\]

so Cauchy estimates, smoothing-weight derivatives, gamma/Stirling derivatives, and determinant perturbation constants remain inside fixed-polynomial bookkeeping.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary-scale analytic package: Green feasible.}
}
\]

The open part is not the \(E_2\) derivative package; it is arithmetic incidence.

---

# 2. Ordinary packet-frequency active block theorem

The active determinant block should be

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
=
\left\{
n:
cQ\le\log n\le cQ+\frac{Q}{R}
\right\},
\qquad 0<c<\frac12.
}
\]

Then

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp1,
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)
=
\lambda\cdot\frac{Q}{R}
\asymp
\frac1R.
\]

This gives enough normalized node spread for a rank-\(R\) basis-normalized determinant, unlike low-prime blocks where \(x_n\asymp(\log Q)/Q\ll1\).

The active-block theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\exists\mathcal B_{\rm pf}
\text{ with }
|\mathcal B_{\rm pf}|\gg R,
\quad
x_n\asymp1,
\quad
\operatorname{diam}(x_n)\gtrsim R^{-1},
}
\]

and the corresponding AFE coefficients \(c_n^\pm\) are non-negligible in aggregate. A single subset coefficient may be tiny, so the determinant must be treated through **basis-normalized aggregate minors**, not single-subset dominance.

---

# 3. Conditional basis-normalized Wronskian theorem

Define

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,
\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^jq''_{\can},
\quad 0\le j\le R.
\]

Use stable basis-normalized column operators

\[
C_0(\mathcal D),\ldots,C_{R+1}(\mathcal D),
\]

not raw monomial derivatives. The Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)
=
\det
\bigl(
C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)
\bigr)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1}.
\]

The ordinary route reduces to the following conditional theorem.

## Conditional ordinary Wronskian theorem

Assume:

### A. Two-branch symbol residual

For packet-frequency main and folded-dual branches,

\[
x_n^+=\lambda\log n,
\qquad
x_n^-=\lambda\log\frac{m}{2\pi n}
\]

or the exact convention-dependent dual node, and

\[
r_n^\pm=\frac{z_n^\pm}{c_n^\pm},
\]

we have

\[
\boxed{
\inf_{P\in\mathcal P_{\le R}}
\max_\pm\max_{n\in\mathcal B_\pm}
|r_n^\pm-P(x_n^\pm)|
\ge Q^{-C_{\rm sym}}.
}
\]

### B. Minor-vector lower bound

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero, expanding along the \(Z_\alpha\)-row gives

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\sum_{\ell=1}^{R+1}
(-1)^\ell
C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)\,
M_\ell(m_0).
\]

Let

\[
\mathbf M(m_0)=(M_1,\ldots,M_{R+1}).
\]

Assume

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-C_M}.
}
\]

### C. Angle/nonalignment

Let

\[
\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)
=
\bigl(
(-1)^\ell C_\ell(\mathcal D)Z_\alpha(m_0)
\bigr)_{\ell=1}^{R+1}.
\]

Assume

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-C_\angle}
|\mathbf z'|\,|\mathbf M|.
}
\]

### D. Derivative size for \(Z_\alpha\)

Assume

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-C_Z}.
}
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This implies finite-jet anti-design and hence Gate 1, after the already-needed finite-jet-to-interval-energy transfer.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary route: Green feasible if A--D are proved.}
}
\]

Currently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A is plausible; B, C, D remain arithmetic. C is the hardest.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Mild singular route with \(\mu=\lambda Q\)

Let

\[
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

The mild singular regime is

\[
(\log Q)^{-C_0}\lesssim \mu <1.
\]

The AFE derivative error estimate remains feasible, because Cauchy gives

\[
|\mathcal D^kE_2|
\le
k!\mu^kQ^{-A_0},
\]

which is no worse than the ordinary case.

The issue is determinant conditioning and rank. Normalized nodes shrink:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\sim \mu
\]

on conductor-scale frequencies.

A mildly singular Wronskian theorem is acceptable only if all additional determinant/basis losses are at most fixed-polynomial in \(Q\).

Two possible loss models:

### Acceptable

\[
\mu^{-CR}.
\]

If

\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then

\[
\mu^{-CR}
\le
(\log Q)^{C C_0R}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(
\frac{\log Q\log\log\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\right)
\right)
=
Q^{o(1)}.
\]

This is acceptable.

### Dangerous

\[
\mu^{-CR^2}.
\]

Then

\[
\mu^{-CR^2}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(
\frac{(\log Q)^2\log\log\log Q}{(\log\log Q)^2}
\right)
\right),
\]

which is not \(Q^{O(1)}\).

Thus the mild singular route is viable only under a basis-normalized determinant theorem with essentially linear-in-\(R\) \(\mu\)-loss.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mild singular route: Yellow.}
}
\]

Open theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{basis-normalized packet-frequency Wronskian with }\mu^{-O(R)}
\text{ loss, not }\mu^{-O(R^2)}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Deep singular route: exclude from ordinary Wronskian

Deep singular scale is

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Then

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

collapses too strongly, and the determinant is expected to lose effective rank. The ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian should not be used there.

The replacement should be a singular dominance/local lemma.

A plausible required lemma is:

## Deep singular dominance lemma

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then either:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

holds by direct singular-packet dominance, or source-flattening forces a same-scale cancellation configuration that is handled by a separate local singular anti-design theorem.

More concretely, near a shallow packet at scale \(c=\lambda\),

\[
q''_{\can}\sim c^{-3}Q''_{\rm loc},
\]

so unless same-scale singular jets cancel,

\[
|q''_{\can}|^2
\]

has mass far above the Gate 1 threshold. The deep singular branch should prove that cancellation either cannot persist canonically or reduces to a separate singular anti-design problem.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{deep singular route: Red for ordinary Wronskian; use dominance/local lemma.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Route classification summary

| Regime | Scale | Active block | Analytic AFE package | Determinant rank | Remaining open theorem |
|---|---:|---|---:|---:|---|
| Ordinary | \(\lambda Q\asymp1\) | \(\log n\asymp Q\), width \(Q/R\) | Green feasible | Green feasible conditionally | Incidence \(Z_\alpha=0\Rightarrow |\widetilde W_R|\ge Q^{-A}\) |
| Mild singular | \(\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}\) | \(\lambda\log n\asymp\mu\) or adjusted packet-frequency block | Green feasible | Yellow with \(\mu\)-loss | \(\mu^{-O(R)}\) determinant theorem |
| Deep singular | \(\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}\) | ordinary determinant block rank-collapses | Green feasible but irrelevant | Red for Wronskian | singular dominance/local anti-design |

---

# 7. Exact open theorem list

## Ordinary route

The remaining open theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

for packet-frequency basis-normalized Wronskians built from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

This decomposes into:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-branch symbol residual;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A};
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|;
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

## Mild singular route

Need:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same theorem with explicit }\mu=\lambda Q\text{ loss no worse than }\mu^{-O(R)}.
}
\]

## Deep singular route

Need:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular dominance/local Gate 1 lemma replacing Wronskian.}
}
\]

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary route: analytically Green feasible, arithmetically Yellow.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mild singular route: Yellow with explicit }\mu\text{-loss requirement.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular route: do not use ordinary Wronskian.}
}
\]

The active-block issue is now resolved for ordinary scale by packet-frequency blocks

\[
\log n\asymp Q,
\qquad
\lambda\log n\asymp1.
\]

The single Green-blocking theorem remains the arithmetic incidence bound:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

## Agent 6 / F — Deep singular branch: dominance/local anti-design replacement

The ordinary Wronskian route should **not** be forced into the deep singular regime. The attached coordinator brief explicitly separates the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route from the branch

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

and assigns this branch to a dominance/local anti-design replacement rather than to the ordinary determinant theorem. 

---

# 1. Deep singular regime

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

The deep singular branch is

\[
\boxed{
\mu=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\lambda\ll Q^{-1}(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

This is much smaller than the ordinary packet scale

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1.
\]

In this regime, the packet-frequency Wronskian loses rank because

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n
\]

is small even for conductor-scale frequencies \(\log n\asymp Q\). Hence

\[
x_n\asymp\lambda Q=\mu\ll1.
\]

Rows generated by powers or stable basis functions of \(x_n\) become compressed, and a rank-\(R\) Wronskian pays unacceptable \(\mu\)-losses.

So the replacement target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove Gate 1 directly by local singular dominance,}
}
\]

unless singular packets cancel in a precise same-scale anti-design configuration.

---

# 2. Local singular scaling

Let the singular scale be

\[
c=\lambda.
\]

In normalized local coordinates,

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\]

a single singular packet has the form

\[
q(m)=c^{-1}Q_{\rm loc}(x),
\]

so derivatives scale as

\[
q'(m)=c^{-2}Q'_{\rm loc}(x),
\]

\[
q''(m)=c^{-3}Q''_{\rm loc}(x),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}(m)=c^{-5}Q_{\rm loc}^{(4)}(x).
\]

Therefore the local \(L^2\)-mass of the curvature over an interval \(I_\rho=\gamma+cX\) is

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
=
\int_X
|c^{-3}Q_{\rm loc}''(x)|^2c\,dx
=
c^{-5}
\int_X|Q_{\rm loc}''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Gate 1 only asks for

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
=
Q^{-B}c|X|.
\]

So dominance is enormous if

\[
\int_X|Q_{\rm loc}''(x)|^2\,dx
\gg Q^{-B}c^6|X|.
\]

Since \(c=\lambda\ll Q^{-1}\), the right side is extremely small:

\[
Q^{-B}c^6\ll Q^{-B-6}.
\]

Thus a single uncancelled singular packet is far above the Gate 1 threshold.

---

# 3. Dominance theorem candidate

## Theorem: deep singular dominance unless local normalized cancellation

Let

\[
I_\rho=\gamma+cX,
\qquad cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Suppose the canonical source curvature admits a local decomposition

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}
\left(
Q_0''(x)+\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal S}a_\nu Q_\nu''(x)
\right)
+
R_{\rm far}(x),
\]

where:

1. \(Q_0''\) is the dominant singular kernel from the packet centered at \(\gamma\);
2. \(\mathcal S\) consists of same-scale neighboring singular packets;
3. \(R_{\rm far}\) contains background, far zeros, and smooth AFE/tail terms;
4. the far term satisfies

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12 c^{-5/2}Q^{-A};
\]

5. the normalized local packet aggregate satisfies

\[
\left\|
Q_0''+\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal S}a_\nu Q_\nu''
\right\|_{L^2(X)}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

for some \(B=B(A)\).

### Proof sketch

By the scaling above,

\[
\left\|
c^{-3}
\left(
Q_0''+\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal S}a_\nu Q_\nu''
\right)
\right\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
=
c^{-5/2}
\left\|
Q_0''+\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal S}a_\nu Q_\nu''
\right\|_{L^2(X)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge
c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
-
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
=
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Squaring,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2
\ge
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}.
\]

Since

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp c,
\]

Gate 1 follows if

\[
c^{-5}Q^{-2A}
\ge
Q^{-B}c,
\]

i.e.

\[
c^{-6}\ge Q^{2A-B}.
\]

Because \(cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}\), we have \(c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}\). Hence the inequality holds after choosing

\[
B\ge 2A+6+O(1).
\]

So in the deep singular branch, the only obstruction is not smallness of a single singular packet, but **same-scale cancellation** among local singular kernels.

---

# 4. Same-scale cancellation branch

If the dominance hypothesis fails, then

\[
\left\|
Q_0''+\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal S}a_\nu Q_\nu''
\right\|_{L^2(X)}
<
Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the singular anti-design event.

The local kernels have the normalized form

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta},
\]

with derivatives at the origin satisfying

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)
=
n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus finite-jet flattening of curvature corresponds to moment cancellation

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

This is the same normalized quadrature obstruction already seen in local packet geometry.

Therefore, in the deep singular branch, the proof reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either singular dominance holds, or actual zeta forbids same-scale singular anti-design.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Singular anti-design theorem required

The replacement theorem should be stated directly in normalized local coordinates.

## Theorem needed: canonical singular anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Let the same-scale singular packet aggregate be

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)
+
Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

where \(Q_{\rm bg}\) is the normalized contribution of background, far zeros, gamma term, and AFE tail.

Assume the packet is admissible, i.e. it arises from actual zeta zeros and the canonical completed phase. Then there exist constants \(A,R\), with

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

such that

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_x^rQ_{\rm sing}''(x_\ast)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\int_X|Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

After scaling back, this gives

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
c^{-5}Q^{-A}
\gg
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

### What this theorem must use

It cannot follow from local positive geometry alone, because deterministic positive quadrature can force

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3.
\]

So the theorem must use actual-zeta constraints, such as:

\[
\text{zero-prime explicit formula compatibility,}
\]

\[
\text{local zero-spacing restrictions beyond pair correlation,}
\]

\[
\text{completed AFE consistency,}
\]

or

\[
\text{prime-side obstruction to same-scale quadrature.}
\]

---

# 6. Does singular cancellation reduce to the old quadrature obstruction?

Yes.

The singular branch does **not** produce a fundamentally new analytic obstruction. It reduces to the same normalized anti-design mechanism:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0
}
\]

for a range of \(k\).

The difference is scale:

- Ordinary Wronskian branch: use packet-frequency prime/AFE blocks with \(\lambda Q\asymp1\).
- Deep singular branch: local singular dominance already wins unless same-scale local singular packets form an anti-design.

Thus the deep singular theorem should not be a Wronskian determinant theorem. It should be a **singular anti-design exclusion theorem**.

---

# 7. Branch classification

| Branch | Condition | Recommended proof route | Status |
|---|---:|---|---:|
| Ordinary | \(\lambda Q\asymp1\) | packet-frequency Wronskian | Yellow; arithmetic incidence open |
| Mild singular | \(\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}\) | Wronskian with explicit \(\mu\)-loss or dominance | Yellow |
| Deep singular | \(\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}\) | dominance unless singular anti-design | Green-feasible modulo anti-design exclusion |
| Exact same-scale cancellation | normalized moments vanish | actual-zeta singular anti-design theorem | Open |

---

# 8. Final replacement package

The deep singular branch should be formalized as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Deep Singular Gate 1 Lemma.}
}
\]

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then either:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

by singular dominance, or the normalized same-scale packet aggregate satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rQ_{\rm sing}''(x_\ast)|
\le Q^{-A},
}
\]

equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

The remaining theorem in the exceptional case is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion.}
}
\]

That is the singular replacement for the ordinary Wronskian incidence theorem.

So the deep singular branch is not fatal, but it is not solved for free: it reduces to an actual-zeta anti-design theorem rather than to the ordinary Wronskian determinant.

## Agent 6 / F — Deep singular anti-design theorem

The instruction is to keep the branch

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

out of the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route and replace it with a direct singular dominance/local anti-design theorem. That is the right split: the ordinary route now lives on packet-frequency blocks, while the deep singular branch has a different scaling and should not be forced through the same determinant. 

---

# 1. Deep singular regime

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
\mu=\lambda Q.
\]

The deep singular regime is

\[
\boxed{
\mu=\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
}
\]

Write

\[
\lambda=c.
\]

Then the local coordinate is

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
I_\rho=\gamma+cX.
\]

The ordinary Wronskian is inappropriate here because packet-frequency nodes satisfy

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n.
\]

Even at conductor scale \(\log n\asymp Q\),

\[
x_n\asymp \lambda Q=\mu\ll1.
\]

So rank in the normalized derivative system collapses unless one pays severe \(\mu\)-losses. The replacement theorem should use local singular dominance.

---

# 2. Exact scaling

Assume the local singular packet contribution has normalized form

\[
q_{\rm sing}(\gamma+cx)=c^{-1}Q_{\rm sing}(x).
\]

Then

\[
q_{\rm sing}'(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-2}Q_{\rm sing}'(x),
\]

\[
q_{\rm sing}''(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x),
\]

and, more generally,

\[
q_{\rm sing}^{(4)}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-5}Q_{\rm sing}^{(4)}(x).
\]

The \(L^2\)-mass rescales as

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q_{\rm sing}''(m)|^2\,dm
=
\int_X
|c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2c\,dx
=
c^{-5}
\int_X|Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Gate 1 asks for

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\asymp Q^{-B}c|X|.
\]

Thus if

\[
\int_X|Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q_{\rm sing}''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge c^{-5}Q^{-A}.
\]

Since \(cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}\), we have \(c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}\). Therefore

\[
c^{-5}Q^{-A}
=
c\cdot c^{-6}Q^{-A}
\gg
cQ^{-A+6}.
\]

So for \(B\ge A+6+O(1)\),

\[
c^{-5}Q^{-A}
\ge
Q^{-B}c.
\]

This proves the scaling dominance implication.

---

# 3. Deep singular dominance lemma

## Lemma candidate

Let

\[
I_\rho=\gamma+cX,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Assume the canonical source curvature decomposes on \(I_\rho\) as

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)
+
R_{\rm far}(\gamma+cx),
\]

where \(Q_{\rm sing}\) is the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate and \(R_{\rm far}\) contains background, far zeros, regularized tail, and AFE residual terms.

Suppose

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

for some \(B=B(A)\).

## Proof

By scaling,

\[
\|c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
=
c^{-5/2}\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}
\ge
c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Thus

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge
c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
-
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
=
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Squaring gives

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}.
\]

Since \(|I_\rho|\asymp c\),

\[
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}
=
\frac14c^{-6}Q^{-2A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Because \(c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}\), this implies

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

for \(B\ge 2A+6+O(1)\).

So deep singular Gate 1 is automatic unless the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate is \(Q^{-A}\)-small.

---

# 4. Exceptional singular anti-design event

The only obstruction is

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the singular anti-design event.

The normalized singular aggregate should have the form

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_{j=1}^{N}w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)
+
Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

where

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta},
\]

and \(Q_{\rm bg}\) is the normalized smooth contribution of \(B_2\), far zeros, and residual canonical terms.

The local kernel identity is

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus finite-jet flattening of \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) implies moment cancellation

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

where \(\mathcal B_k\) denotes the contribution of \(Q_{\rm bg}\).

Ignoring \(Q_{\rm bg}\), the pure same-scale cancellation condition is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

This is exactly the previously identified same-scale quadrature obstruction.

---

# 5. Singular anti-design theorem required

The replacement theorem should be stated as follows.

## Singular anti-design exclusion theorem

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(Q_{\rm sing}\) be the actual canonical normalized singular packet aggregate on \(X\), including:

\[
B_2,
\qquad
\text{far zero regularized tail},
\qquad
\text{critical-line zero convention},
\qquad
\text{AFE residual transfer}.
\]

Then either

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}
}
\]

or the actual zeta zeros realize a same-scale anti-design:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

The theorem needed to close the branch is the exclusion of the second alternative:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta cannot realize same-scale singular anti-design to depth }R.
}
\]

If this exclusion is proved, then the deep singular branch of Gate 1 follows by the dominance lemma.

---

# 6. Does this reduce to the old quadrature obstruction?

Yes.

The deep singular branch reduces to the same local anti-design mechanism:

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0.
\]

Local geometry alone cannot rule it out. Deterministic positive quadrature can force exact cancellations of the form

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0
\]

over a finite range of \(k\).

Therefore the singular theorem must use actual-zeta arithmetic, not just local kernel algebra. Possible required inputs:

\[
\text{explicit formula compatibility,}
\]

\[
\text{zero-prime coupling,}
\]

\[
\text{constraints on same-scale zero packet configurations,}
\]

\[
\text{canonical AFE consistency,}
\]

or

\[
\text{a prime-side obstruction to positive sine quadrature.}
\]

So the singular branch is not closed for free. It is separated cleanly into:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dominance, unless actual-zeta singular anti-design occurs.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Required far-term control

The dominance lemma assumes

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

This should be easier than ordinary Wronskian error control because the singular leading scale is enormous:

\[
c^{-5/2}.
\]

The required canonical decomposition is:

\[
q''_{\can}
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)
+
R_{\rm far}.
\]

The far term contains:

1. \(B_2\), whose size is smooth and much smaller than \(c^{-3}\) in the deep singular regime;
2. far zero contributions, regularized/symmetrized;
3. AFE residual \(E_2\);
4. non-same-scale packets.

A sufficient condition is

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le Q^C|I_\rho|^{1/2}
\]

provided

\[
Q^Cc^{1/2}
\ll c^{-5/2}Q^{-A},
\]

i.e.

\[
Q^C\ll c^{-3}Q^{-A}.
\]

Since \(c\ll Q^{-1}(\log Q)^{-C_0}\),

\[
c^{-3}\gg Q^3(\log Q)^{3C_0},
\]

so this holds after adjusting exponents if the far terms are polynomially bounded. Thus canonical far-term control is not expected to be the main obstruction.

---

# 8. Final deep singular package

The branch should be formalized as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Deep Singular Gate 1 Lemma.}
}
\]

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then either:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

by singular dominance, or:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual canonical same-scale packet aggregate.

The remaining theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Route classification

| Branch | Condition | Recommended theorem | Status |
|---|---:|---|---:|
| Ordinary | \(\lambda Q\asymp1\) | packet-frequency Wronskian incidence | Yellow/open |
| Mild singular | \(\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}\) | Wronskian with explicit \(\mu\)-loss or dominance | Yellow |
| Deep singular | \(\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}\) | dominance unless singular anti-design | Green-feasible modulo anti-design exclusion |
| Exceptional singular cancellation | same-scale moment cancellation | actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion | Open |

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular Gate 1 is won by scaling dominance unless normalized same-scale cancellation occurs.}
}
\]

The exceptional cancellation is exactly a singular anti-design event:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

Thus the deep singular branch does **not** require the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian. It requires a separate actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion theorem.

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design exclusion branch

The deep singular branch remains cleanly separated from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. In this branch,

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

the ordinary Wronskian should not be used. The correct replacement is: **prove Gate 1 by singular dominance unless the actual zeta zeros realize a same-scale singular anti-design.** This is exactly the branch requested in the coordinator prompt. 

---

# 1. Deep singular dominance lemma

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),\qquad \lambda=c,\qquad cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Work on

\[
I_\rho=\gamma+cX,\qquad m=\gamma+cx.
\]

Assume the canonical curvature decomposes as

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)+R_{\rm far}(\gamma+cx),
\]

where \(Q_{\rm sing}\) is the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate and \(R_{\rm far}\) consists of smooth background, far zeros, non-same-scale packets, regularized tails, and AFE residual terms.

## Lemma

If

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12 c^{-5/2}Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

for some \(B=B(A)\).

---

# 2. Scaling calculation

The local singular scaling is

\[
q(\gamma+cx)=c^{-1}Q_{\rm loc}(x),
\]

so

\[
q''(\gamma+cx)=c^{-3}Q_{\rm loc}''(x).
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
=
\int_X|c^{-3}Q_{\rm loc}''(x)|^2c\,dx
=
c^{-5}\int_X|Q_{\rm loc}''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

In norm form,

\[
\|c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
=
c^{-5/2}\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}.
\]

Hence

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge
c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
-
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}
=
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Squaring,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}.
\]

Since \(|I_\rho|\asymp c\),

\[
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}
=
\frac14c^{-6}Q^{-2A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Because

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

we have

\[
c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

after taking, for instance,

\[
B\ge 2A+6+O(1).
\]

So deep singular Gate 1 is automatic unless the normalized local curvature nearly cancels.

---

# 3. Exceptional singular anti-design event

The exceptional event is

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The local singular aggregate has the form

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_j w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

where

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

The key local identity is

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus if \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) is flat to depth \(R\), then for

\[
3\le k\le R+3
\]

one obtains moment cancellations of the form

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
}
\]

where \(\mathcal B_k\) is the contribution of \(Q_{\rm bg}\).

In the pure packet model, this is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

This is exactly the finite same-scale quadrature obstruction.

---

# 4. Singular anti-design exclusion theorem needed

The theorem needed to close the deep singular branch is:

## Actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(Q_{\rm sing}\) be the canonical normalized same-scale singular aggregate, including the completed-phase convention, \(B_2\), regularized far-zero tail, and AFE residual transfer.

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, actual zeta zeros cannot satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

on a deep singular same-scale packet.

If this theorem holds, the deep singular branch of Gate 1 follows immediately from the dominance lemma.

---

# 5. Can actual zeta constraints forbid singular anti-design more easily?

Current verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Not from local geometry alone.}
}
\]

The deterministic quadrature adversary already shows that positive local packets can force

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0
\]

over a finite range of \(k\). Therefore, the exclusion theorem must use actual-zeta arithmetic.

Potential inputs that might distinguish actual zeta packets from arbitrary quadrature packets:

\[
\text{explicit formula compatibility,}
\]

\[
\text{prime-side response to same-scale zero clustering,}
\]

\[
\text{constraints on consecutive zero spacings beyond local positivity,}
\]

\[
\text{completed AFE consistency,}
\]

\[
\text{zero-prime phase coupling.}
\]

But absent such an input, the singular anti-design exclusion is not proven.

---

# 6. Comparison with ordinary Gate 1 obstruction

The singular branch reduces to the same type of obstruction as ordinary Gate 1, but in a different coordinate system.

Ordinary branch:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\]

uses packet-frequency Wronskians and must prove arithmetic incidence:

\[
Z_\alpha(m)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Deep singular branch:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

uses local dominance and must exclude same-scale singular anti-design:

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Thus the singular branch is **not killed by the Wronskian rank collapse**. It bypasses Wronskians. But it still needs actual-zeta arithmetic if same-scale cancellation occurs.

---

# 7. Final branch theorem package

The deep singular branch should be recorded as:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Deep Singular Gate 1 Alternative.}
}
\]

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then either

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

by singular dominance, or

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A}
}
\]

for the actual canonical same-scale singular packet aggregate.

The remaining theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion.}
}
\]

---

# Bottom line

The deep singular branch is **Green-feasible up to one precise exception**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale singular anti-design.}
}
\]

If that anti-design is excluded using actual zeta arithmetic, then Gate 1 follows in the deep singular regime by scaling dominance. If not, the singular branch reduces to the same fundamental arithmetic obstruction already seen elsewhere: actual zeta must forbid finite-depth source-flattening quadrature.

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design exclusion theorem

The deep singular branch is excluded from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. The task is to isolate the replacement theorem: **dominance wins unless actual zeta realizes a same-scale singular anti-design**. This matches the current route split in the coordinator brief. 

---

# 1. Deep singular dominance lemma

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
\lambda=c,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Work on

\[
I_\rho=\gamma+cX,
\qquad
m=\gamma+cx.
\]

Assume the canonical curvature decomposes as

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)+R_{\rm far}(\gamma+cx),
\]

where \(Q_{\rm sing}\) is the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate and \(R_{\rm far}\) contains all far/background/canonical residual terms.

## Lemma

If

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

for some \(B=B(A)\).

Proof:

\[
q''_{\rm sing}(\gamma+cx)=c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x),
\]

so

\[
\|q''_{\rm sing}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
=
c^{-5/2}\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}
\ge c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Squaring gives

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}.
\]

Since \(|I_\rho|\asymp c\),

\[
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}
=
\frac14c^{-6}Q^{-2A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Because

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

we have

\[
c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}.
\]

Hence, after increasing \(B\),

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

So the deep singular branch fails only if the normalized singular aggregate is very small.

---

# 2. Exceptional anti-design event

The exceptional event is

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, after finite-jet reduction,

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\partial_x^rQ_{\rm sing}''(x_\ast)|
\le Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

The normalized singular aggregate has the local form

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_j w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

with

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

Using

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta),
\]

the flatness of \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) to order \(R\) becomes

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal B_k
\]

is the contribution from \(Q_{\rm bg}\), namely canonical background, far-tail, and residual terms.

In the pure local packet model,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

This is exactly the same finite same-scale quadrature obstruction already identified in the ordinary Gate 1 analysis.

---

# 3. Singular-specific constraints

The singular setting gives some extra structure, but none of it is currently enough by itself.

## 3.1 Zero spacing

A deep singular packet means zeros are close at scale \(c\ll Q^{-1}\). Local zero-spacing facts can show the packet is atypical relative to average spacing, but they do not forbid finite clusters. A spacing bound would need to be strong enough to prevent an \(O(R)\)-node same-scale design.

Needed theorem:

\[
\#\{\gamma_j:\ |\gamma_j-\gamma|\le Cc\}
< R+O(1)
\]

or a stronger weighted spacing obstruction. Standard local density alone does not give this at the required deterministic level.

## 3.2 Multiplicity

Multiplicity restrictions do not solve the anti-design problem. The quadrature adversary can use distinct nearby nodes. Simplicity only rules out repeated angles, not the sine-moment cancellation

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0.
\]

## 3.3 Packet asymmetry

Asymmetry may break exact quadrature if the weights \(w_j\) are canonical and not freely chosen. But this requires a theorem that actual singular weights cannot match the positive quadrature weights to depth \(R\). Local kernel geometry alone does not provide this.

Needed theorem:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
(w_j,\theta_j)_{\rm actual},
\mathcal Q_R
\right)
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where \(\mathcal Q_R\) is the finite sine-quadrature design variety.

## 3.4 Canonical tail

The canonical background/tail enters as

\[
\mathcal B_k.
\]

It may break cancellation if \(\mathcal B_k\) is not itself compatible with the local packet moments. But the tail is smooth on the singular scale and likely low-complexity. It can shift the target moments, but does not automatically prevent solving

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx-\mathcal B_k.
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
-(\mathcal B_k)_{k=3}^{R+3},
\operatorname{MomentImage}_{R}(\text{actual same-scale packets})
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## 3.5 Prime / explicit formula compatibility

This is the most plausible singular-specific arithmetic input. A same-scale zero anti-design imposes many local zero-side moment cancellations. Through the explicit formula, this should produce a structured prime-side packet response. A viable theorem would be:

\[
\text{same-scale singular anti-design to depth }R
\Longrightarrow
\text{prime-side imbalance or AFE incompatibility}.
\]

This is the singular analogue of the ordinary actual-zeta incidence theorem.

---

# 4. Singular anti-design exclusion theorem candidate

The theorem needed to close the branch is:

## Theorem: actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_jw_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x)
\]

be the actual canonical normalized singular packet aggregate, including:

\[
B_2,
\qquad
\text{regularized far-zero tail},
\qquad
\text{critical-line convention},
\qquad
\text{AFE residual transfer}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for some \(A'\).

This theorem cannot be proved from local positivity or local kernel identities alone. It requires actual-zeta arithmetic.

---

# 5. Reduction theorem

A clean way to package the branch is:

## Deep Singular Gate 1 Alternative

Assume

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Then either:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

or the actual zeta singular packet satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Thus the deep singular branch is reduced to the singular anti-design exclusion theorem.

---

# 6. Verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular dominance is solid.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The only exceptional case is same-scale singular anti-design.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{That exceptional case reduces to the same actual-zeta anti-design arithmetic as ordinary Gate 1.}
}
\]

So the deep singular branch is not a Wronskian problem. It is a local singular dominance problem plus one arithmetic exclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta cannot realize finite-depth sine-moment anti-design at singular scale.}
}
\]

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design exclusion

The deep singular branch remains separate from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. In this branch,

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

Gate 1 is won by singular dominance unless the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate realizes a finite-depth sine-moment anti-design. The attached brief frames this as one of the remaining actual-zeta arithmetic blockers. 

---

# 1. Dominance alternative

Let

\[
Q=\log(3+|m_0|),
\qquad
\lambda=c,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

and write

\[
I_\rho=\gamma+cX,
\qquad
m=\gamma+cx.
\]

Assume

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x)+R_{\rm far}(\gamma+cx),
\]

where \(Q_{\rm sing}\) is the normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate.

If

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A}
\]

and

\[
\|R_{\rm far}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\le
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A},
\]

then

\[
\|q''_{\can}\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\ge
\frac12c^{-5/2}Q^{-A}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
\frac14c^{-5}Q^{-2A}.
\]

Since

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp c,
\]

this is

\[
\frac14c^{-6}Q^{-2A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Because

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

we have

\[
c^{-6}\gg Q^6(\log Q)^{6C_0}.
\]

Thus

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

after increasing \(B\). So deep singular Gate 1 fails only on the exceptional branch

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Exceptional branch and moment cancellation

In normalized coordinates, write

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_j w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

where

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

The key identity is

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Flatness of \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) to depth \(R\) gives, for

\[
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

the moment conditions

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
}
\]

where \(\mathcal B_k\) is the background/tail contribution from \(Q_{\rm bg}\).

In the pure local model,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

This is the same same-scale quadrature obstruction already found in the ordinary analysis.

---

# 3. Do singular scales add extra constraints?

## Extreme zero clustering

A deep singular packet means zeros are packed on scale

\[
c\ll Q^{-1}(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

well below the usual \(1/Q\)-scale. This looks arithmetically rare, but rarity is not enough for a deterministic proof.

A usable theorem would need something like:

\[
\#\{\gamma_j:\ |\gamma_j-\gamma|\le Cc\}\le R_0
\]

with \(R_0<R+3\), or a stronger weighted restriction preventing the \(O(R)\)-node quadrature design. Standard zero-density or average spacing information does not give this deterministic local exclusion.

## Multiplicity and simplicity

Simplicity is insufficient. The quadrature adversary can use distinct nearby nodes, so multiplicity bounds do not rule out

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0.
\]

## Packet asymmetry

Actual packets may have non-free weights \(w_j\), unlike deterministic quadrature where weights are designed. This is promising, but it requires a theorem of the form

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\bigl((w_j,\theta_j)_{\rm actual},\mathcal Q_R\bigr)
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

where \(\mathcal Q_R\) is the finite sine-moment anti-design variety.

No local kernel argument supplies this.

## Canonical tail incompatibility

The background terms \(\mathcal B_k\) shift the target moments. They may help, but they do not automatically exclude cancellation, because the local packet moments could solve

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx-\mathcal B_k.
\]

A useful theorem would need:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
-(\mathcal B_k)_{k=3}^{R+3},
\operatorname{MomentImage}_{R}(\text{actual singular packets})
\right)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Explicit formula stress

This is the most plausible actual-zeta input. A deep same-scale singular anti-design imposes many zero-side moment constraints at a scale far below \(1/Q\). Through the explicit formula, this should create a structured prime-side packet response.

A candidate theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale singular anti-design to depth }R
\Rightarrow
\text{prime/AFE imbalance}
}
\]

or more concretely,

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\mathcal P_{\rm sing}(m_0)\ge Q^{A'}
}
\]

for some explicit prime-side statistic \(\mathcal P_{\rm sing}\) that is known to be polynomially bounded. This would close the branch.

At present this is a theorem target, not a proof.

---

# 4. Singular anti-design exclusion theorem candidate

The needed theorem is:

## Theorem candidate: actual-zeta singular anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)=\sum_jw_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x)
\]

be the actual canonical same-scale singular packet aggregate, including:

\[
B_2,
\qquad
\text{critical-line convention},
\qquad
\text{regularized far-zero tail},
\qquad
\text{AFE residual transfer}.
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

Combined with the dominance lemma, this proves Gate 1 in the deep singular branch.

---

# 5. Current reduction status

The singular branch reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{dominance unless actual zeta realizes a finite-depth sine anti-design.}
}
\]

Local geometry alone cannot exclude this because deterministic positive quadrature can realize the same moment cancellations. Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the deep singular branch requires actual-zeta anti-design arithmetic.}
}
\]

It is not the ordinary Wronskian incidence theorem, but it is morally the same class of missing input: actual zeta must forbid source-flattening quadrature.

---

# 6. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular dominance: solid.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exceptional anti-design: open.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No singular-specific local argument currently excludes the anti-design.}
}
\]

The best theorem target is an explicit-formula obstruction to

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

for actual zeta singular packets.

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design exclusion via explicit formula

The deep singular branch is separate from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. In this branch,

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

dominance proves Gate 1 unless the same-scale singular packet aggregate realizes finite sine-moment cancellation. The assigned task is to test whether the explicit formula gives an exclusion theorem for that exceptional event. 

---

# 1. Singular anti-design event in normalized coordinates

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad
c=\lambda,
\qquad
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0}.
\]

Let the canonical normalized same-scale singular packet aggregate be

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_{j=1}^{N} w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

with

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

The singular anti-design event is

\[
\boxed{
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, after finite-jet reduction at a basepoint, it implies

\[
\boxed{
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
=
O(Q^{-A}),
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
}
\]

where

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

and \(\mathcal B_k\) denotes the normalized background/far-tail/canonical residual moment.

This is the same finite same-scale quadrature obstruction, but now localized in a deep singular packet.

---

# 2. Zero-side test function encoding the moments

Choose a finite-mode test function

\[
h_R(x)
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3} a_k h_k(x),
\]

where \(h_k\) is chosen so that its zero-side pairing with a local packet recovers

\[
\langle h_k,K_{\theta_j}\rangle_{\rm zero}
=
\sin(k\theta_j)
\]

up to a controlled normalization.

Then the anti-design condition implies

\[
\boxed{
\left|
\sum_j w_j\langle h_R,K_{\theta_j}\rangle
+
\langle h_R,Q_{\rm bg}\rangle
\right|
\le
Q^{-A}\|a\|_1.
}
\]

Equivalently, the zero-side distribution has small projection onto the finite-dimensional packet-mode space

\[
\mathcal H_R=\operatorname{span}\{h_3,\ldots,h_{R+3}\}.
\]

A natural robust choice is to take \(a\) as the normalized coefficient vector of the residual direction:

\[
a_k
=
\overline{
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
},
\]

so that the zero-side statistic becomes

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z_R
=
\sum_{k=3}^{R+3}
\left|
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|^2.
}
\]

The anti-design event is

\[
\mathcal Z_R\le Q^{-A}.
\]

---

# 3. Explicit-formula translation

Push each \(h_k\) through the explicit formula. Schematically,

\[
\sum_\rho h_k\!\left(\frac{\rho-\gamma}{c}\right)
=
\mathcal G_k
-
\mathcal P_k
+
\mathcal T_k,
\]

where:

\[
\mathcal G_k
\]

is the gamma/background contribution,

\[
\mathcal T_k
\]

is the regularized tail and endpoint contribution, and

\[
\mathcal P_k
\]

is the prime-side statistic

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n)
}
\]

up to the precise completed-normalization constants.

Thus the singular anti-design condition becomes a prime-side vector constraint:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
\mathcal G_k+\mathcal T_k+O(Q^{-A}),
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

Or in vector form,

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
=
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)+\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)+O(Q^{-A}).
}
\]

So an explicit-formula exclusion theorem would need to show

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_{\ell^2(3\le k\le R+3)}
\ge Q^{-A'}
}
\]

for actual zeta in the deep singular regime.

---

# 4. What frequencies does the singular explicit formula see?

Because

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

the Fourier weights are evaluated at

\[
c\log n.
\]

The modes \(h_k\) have complexity \(k\le R+3\), so their transforms \(\widehat h_k(\xi)\) are concentrated on \(|\xi|\lesssim R\) in the natural scale. Thus the relevant prime lengths satisfy roughly

\[
c\log n\lesssim R,
\]

or

\[
\log n\lesssim \frac{R}{c}.
\]

Since \(c\ll Q^{-1}\), this can be much larger than the ordinary conductor scale:

\[
\frac{R}{c}\gg RQ.
\]

This is the key issue.

The singular explicit-formula statistic probes very long prime ranges unless the test functions are designed with additional smoothing to suppress high \(\xi\). Therefore an exclusion theorem would need either:

1. a strong prime-side bound for \(\mathbf P_R\) over very long ranges; or  
2. a band-limited test family whose \(\widehat h_k(c\log n)\) stays inside a controlled AFE range; or  
3. an argument showing that the long-prime contribution cannot match the required finite vector \(\mathbf G_R+\mathbf T_R\).

None of these is currently automatic.

---

# 5. Does same-scale singular anti-design force abnormal prime response?

It forces a **structured prime response**, but not yet a contradiction.

The forced response is:

\[
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
\approx
\mathbf G_R+\mathbf T_R.
\]

This is abnormal only if one can prove that the actual prime vector \(\mathbf P_R\) cannot enter a \(Q^{-A}\)-ball around that target.

A candidate theorem would be:

## Candidate explicit-formula singular exclusion theorem

Let

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

For a band-limited packet-mode test family \(h_k\), \(3\le k\le R+3\), define

\[
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n).
\]

Then actual zeta satisfies

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
(\mathcal P_k-\mathcal G_k-\mathcal T_k)_{k=3}^{R+3}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This would exclude singular anti-design and close the deep singular branch via dominance.

But this theorem is not presently implied by standard AFE estimates. It is a new actual-prime nonrecurrence statement.

---

# 6. Are standard zeta/AFE estimates enough?

Current verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No, not in the required deterministic form.}
}
\]

Standard estimates may give average control or upper bounds for prime sums, but the exclusion needs a pointwise lower bound away from a specified target vector:

\[
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)\not\approx \mathbf G_R+\mathbf T_R.
\]

This is a nonrecurrence/anti-concentration theorem for a fixed actual prime vector. It is analogous to the ordinary Wronskian incidence obstruction.

Moreover, because \(c\) is deep singular, the explicit-formula test may involve prime frequencies beyond the clean ordinary packet-frequency AFE window unless one carefully bandlimits \(h_k\). That makes the theorem harder, not easier.

---

# 7. No-go diagnosis

The explicit formula gives an exact translation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular anti-design}
\Longrightarrow
\text{prime-side vector hits a prescribed small target.}
}
\]

But it does **not** by itself prove that this cannot happen.

Thus the branch reduces to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual-prime vector nonrecurrence for singular packet-mode statistics.}
}
\]

This is the same class of arithmetic input as ordinary Gate 1, though in a different basis and scale.

---

# 8. Final answer for Agent 6

The deep singular branch can be packaged as:

## Deep Singular Gate 1 Alternative

If

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

then either

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

by singular dominance, or the explicit formula forces

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right\|_2
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The remaining theorem needed is the exclusion of the second alternative:

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A'}.
}
\]

No standard local kernel argument or ordinary AFE estimate currently proves this. The singular branch therefore reduces to an actual-zeta anti-design/nonrecurrence theorem, not to ordinary Wronskian algebra.

## Agent 6 / F — Explicit-formula singular anti-design obstruction

The deep singular branch is:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},\qquad c=\lambda,
\]

and is separate from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. The assigned task is to push the explicit-formula translation of singular anti-design further, specifically whether

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx 0,\qquad 3\le k\le R+3
\]

can be excluded by a prime-side obstruction. 

---

# 1. Zero-side test functions for the singular moments

The local kernel is

\[
K_\theta(x)=\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta},
\]

with the identity

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus the \(k\)-th singular moment is naturally obtained by applying a local derivative functional of order \(k-1\):

\[
\mathcal L_k[f]
=
\frac{1}{(k-1)!}f^{(k-1)}(0),
\]

so that

\[
\mathcal L_k[K_\theta]=\sin(k\theta).
\]

For explicit-formula purposes, point-derivative functionals must be regularized. A workable family is:

\[
h_{k,\sigma}(x)
=
\frac{(-1)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}\partial_x^{k-1}\varphi_\sigma(x),
\]

where \(\varphi_\sigma\) is an even analytic bump approximating \(\delta_0\), with width \(\sigma\). Then

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O_k(\sigma)
\]

provided the packet lies in a fixed compact normalized region and \(\sigma\) is sufficiently small.

A convenient analytic model is the Gaussian:

\[
\varphi_\sigma(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi}\sigma}e^{-x^2/(2\sigma^2)}.
\]

Then

\[
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(\xi)
=
\frac{(i\xi)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}e^{-\sigma^2\xi^2/2}.
\]

This is the cleanest explicit-formula test family.

---

# 2. Prime-side statistic

For

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\]

the explicit formula sends each \(h_{k,\sigma}\) to a prime statistic of the schematic form

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(c\log n),
\]

plus gamma/background and regularized-tail terms:

\[
\mathcal Z_{k,\sigma}
=
\mathcal G_{k,\sigma}
-
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}
+
\mathcal T_{k,\sigma}.
\]

Therefore singular anti-design implies a vector constraint

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
\mathcal G_{k,\sigma}+\mathcal T_{k,\sigma}+O(Q^{-A}),
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf G_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf T_{R,\sigma}
\right\|_2
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

So the singular exclusion problem becomes a prime-vector nonrecurrence theorem.

---

# 3. Prime-length range

For the Gaussian derivative tests,

\[
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(c\log n)
=
\frac{(ic\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
e^{-\sigma^2c^2(\log n)^2/2}.
\]

The transform is significant when

\[
c\log n\lesssim \sigma^{-1}\sqrt{k}.
\]

Since \(k\le R+3\), the prime length range is roughly

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{\sqrt R}{\sigma c}.
}
\]

For sharper approximate-derivative tests, one typically needs \(\sigma\lesssim R^{-C}\), giving

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C+1/2}}{c}.
}
\]

In the deep singular regime,

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

so

\[
\frac{1}{c}\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}.
\]

Hence the required prime range is at least

\[
\log n\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0},
\]

and often larger by powers of \(R\).

This exceeds the ordinary packet-frequency window

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

So the singular explicit-formula tests naturally probe primes much longer than the ordinary Wronskian/AFE scale.

---

# 4. Can we band-limit while still detecting \(\sin(k\theta)\)?

A true band-limited \(h_k\) with

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat h_k\subset[-L,L]
\]

can only resolve features at normalized spatial scale

\[
\gtrsim L^{-1}.
\]

To recover the derivative-type moment

\[
K_\theta^{(k-1)}(0)/(k-1)!
\]

uniformly to depth \(k\le R+3\), the test family needs effective bandwidth at least polynomial in \(R\):

\[
L\gtrsim R^C.
\]

Then the prime range is

\[
c\log n\lesssim L,
\]

hence

\[
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^C}{c}.
\]

Again, because \(1/c\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}\), this usually exceeds the canonical conductor-scale window.

Thus there is a tradeoff:

\[
\boxed{
\text{moment accuracy to depth }R
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{bandwidth }L\gtrsim R^C
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\log n\lesssim R^C/c.
}
\]

Deep singular anti-design is therefore not naturally visible inside the ordinary AFE range.

---

# 5. Candidate exclusion theorem

A possible theorem would be:

## Singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(h_{k,\sigma}\), \(3\le k\le R+3\), be an analytic derivative-test family with bandwidth

\[
L\asymp R^C.
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(c\log n).
\]

Then actual zeta should satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_{R,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_{R,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

If true, this excludes

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

and closes the deep singular branch via dominance.

---

# 6. Obstruction

The above theorem is not currently derivable from standard AFE estimates.

The obstruction is that the prime-side vector

\[
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}
\]

uses frequencies with

\[
\log n\lesssim R^C/c,
\]

which may be far beyond the ordinary conductor-scale range. Standard estimates give upper bounds or averaged behavior, but the needed statement is a deterministic lower bound away from a prescribed target vector:

\[
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}
\not\approx
\mathbf G_{R,\sigma}+\mathbf T_{R,\sigma}.
\]

This is an actual-prime nonrecurrence theorem.

So the explicit formula translates the singular anti-design into prime-side language, but does not by itself exclude it.

---

# 7. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular dominance is solid.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The exceptional singular anti-design event translates to a prime-vector target condition.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Excluding that target condition requires a new actual-prime nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

In short:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular anti-design exclusion remains open.}
}
\]

The best current theorem target is:

\[
\left\|
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf G_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf T_{R,\sigma}
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A},
\]

with carefully chosen analytic, band-limited derivative tests \(h_{k,\sigma}\). Without such a theorem, the deep singular branch reduces to the same kind of actual-zeta anti-design arithmetic as ordinary Gate 1.

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design: band-limited explicit-formula probes

The deep singular branch remains separate from the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian route. In this branch, dominance proves Gate 1 unless the same-scale singular packet realizes finite sine-moment cancellation. The assigned task is to determine whether band-limited explicit-formula probes can exclude that anti-design. 

---

# 1. Target singular anti-design event

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,\qquad c=\lambda,\qquad cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

and let

\[
Q_{\rm sing}(x)
=
\sum_j w_jK_{\theta_j}(x)+Q_{\rm bg}(x),
\]

where

\[
K_\theta(x)=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

The local identity is

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Thus flatness of \(Q_{\rm sing}''\) to depth \(R\) is equivalent to

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

where \(\mathcal B_k\) is the contribution of the canonical background/far-tail/residual.

The goal is to rule out

\[
\boxed{
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Analytic probe family

A direct point-derivative functional is too singular for the explicit formula, so regularize it.

Let \(\varphi_\sigma\) be an analytic approximate identity. A clean model is the Gaussian

\[
\varphi_\sigma(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi}\sigma}
e^{-x^2/(2\sigma^2)}.
\]

Define

\[
h_{k,\sigma}(x)
=
\frac{(-1)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
\partial_x^{k-1}\varphi_\sigma(x).
\]

Then

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\frac{1}{(k-1)!}
(K_\theta*\varphi_\sigma)^{(k-1)}(0).
\]

For packets away from singularities of \(K_\theta\) in the normalized complex neighborhood and for sufficiently small \(\sigma\),

\[
\boxed{
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O_k(\sigma).
}
\]

The Fourier transform is

\[
\boxed{
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(\xi)
=
\frac{(i\xi)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
e^{-\sigma^2\xi^2/2}.
}
\]

This is the natural explicit-formula probe.

---

# 3. Prime-side statistic

The explicit formula gives, schematically,

\[
\sum_\rho h_{k,\sigma}\!\left(\frac{\rho-\gamma}{c}\right)
=
\mathcal G_{k,\sigma}
-
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}
+
\mathcal T_{k,\sigma},
\]

where

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(c\log n).
}
\]

Substituting the transform,

\[
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\frac{(ic\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
e^{-\sigma^2c^2(\log n)^2/2}.
\]

Therefore singular anti-design implies the prime-vector target

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{k,\sigma}(\gamma,c)
=
\mathcal G_{k,\sigma}+\mathcal T_{k,\sigma}+O(Q^{-A})
}
\]

for

\[
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Vector form:

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf G_{R,\sigma}
-
\mathbf T_{R,\sigma}
\right\|_2
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 4. Prime range required

The factor

\[
e^{-\sigma^2c^2(\log n)^2/2}
\]

cuts off the prime sum when

\[
\sigma c\log n\gtrsim 1.
\]

The polynomial factor

\[
(c\log n)^{k-1}
\]

pushes the effective support slightly outward. For \(k\le R+3\), the main range is approximately

\[
\boxed{
c\log n\lesssim \frac{\sqrt R}{\sigma}.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{\sqrt R}{\sigma c}.
}
\]

If the probe must approximate derivatives through depth \(R\), \(\sigma\) cannot be too large. A conservative choice is

\[
\sigma\asymp R^{-C_\sigma},
\]

which gives

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C_\sigma+1/2}}{c}.
}
\]

Since this is the deep singular branch,

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

so

\[
\frac1c\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}.
\]

Therefore the required prime range is at least

\[
\boxed{
\log n\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}
}
\]

and often

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim R^{C_\sigma+1/2}Q(\log Q)^{C_0}.
}
\]

This generally exceeds the ordinary packet-frequency AFE range

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

---

# 5. Can band-limiting reduce the range?

Suppose we demand

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat h_k\subset[-L,L].
\]

Then the explicit formula only sees primes with

\[
c\log n\lesssim L,
\qquad
\log n\lesssim L/c.
\]

To recover the derivative moments

\[
\sin(k\theta)
\]

for all

\[
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

the test family must resolve oscillation/jet order \(R\). Any uniformly stable recovery of \(R\) moments requires bandwidth at least polynomial in \(R\):

\[
\boxed{
L\gtrsim R^{C_L}.
}
\]

Thus even with optimal band-limiting,

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C_L}}{c}.
}
\]

So band-limiting trades Gaussian tails for compact support, but it does **not** bring the prime range back to \(\log n\asymp Q\) in the deep singular regime. Since \(1/c\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}\), the prime side still reaches beyond the ordinary conductor-scale window.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Band-limited probes do not remove the need for long-prime control.}
}
\]

They make the explicit-formula statement cleaner, but they do not by themselves produce a contradiction.

---

# 6. Candidate theorem

A usable theorem would be:

## Singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(h_k\), \(3\le k\le R+3\), be analytic band-limited probes satisfying

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_k\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O(Q^{-A_0})
\]

uniformly for the relevant same-scale packets, with

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat h_k\subset[-R^{C_L},R^{C_L}].
\]

Define

\[
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n).
\]

Then actual zeta should satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This would imply

\[
\max_{3\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k
\right|
\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and close the deep singular branch via dominance.

---

# 7. No-go diagnosis

The explicit formula gives a precise translation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\text{prime-vector hits a prescribed target}.
}
\]

But it does not exclude that target hit.

The required prime-vector statement is a deterministic lower bound away from a target:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
\not\approx
\mathbf G_R+\mathbf T_R.
}
\]

Standard AFE estimates are not enough because they usually give upper bounds, averages, or approximations, not pointwise anti-concentration away from a specified vector.

Moreover, the prime range required is

\[
\log n\lesssim R^C/c,
\]

which in the deep singular regime is usually much larger than \(Q\). So the singular explicit-formula route requires a new actual-prime vector nonrecurrence theorem, not merely a refinement of the ordinary packet-frequency Wronskian setup.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular dominance is solid.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Singular anti-design translates cleanly to a prime-vector target condition.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Band-limited probes clarify the target but do not avoid long-prime control.}
}
\]

Thus the deep singular branch remains open in exactly one place:

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is a new actual-prime vector nonrecurrence theorem. Without it, the singular branch reduces to the same class of actual-zeta anti-design arithmetic as ordinary Gate 1.

## Agent 6 / F — Singular anti-design explicit-formula theorem

The deep singular branch remains:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

where ordinary packet-frequency Wronskians should not be used. The task is to formulate the explicit-formula theorem needed to exclude the singular anti-design event. The current shared background states that dominance wins unless

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3,
\]

and that the explicit formula converts this into a prime-vector target. 

---

# 1. Probe functions recovering \(\sin(k\theta)\)

The local singular kernel is

\[
K_\theta(x)=\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

It satisfies

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

So the formal functional

\[
\mathcal L_k[f]=\frac{f^{(k-1)}(0)}{(k-1)!}
\]

recovers

\[
\mathcal L_k[K_\theta]=\sin(k\theta).
\]

For the explicit formula, replace \(\mathcal L_k\) by an analytic regularized probe. A convenient choice is

\[
h_{k,\sigma}(x)
=
\frac{(-1)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}\partial_x^{k-1}\varphi_\sigma(x),
\]

where

\[
\varphi_\sigma(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{2\pi}\sigma}e^{-x^2/(2\sigma^2)}.
\]

Then

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\frac{1}{(k-1)!}(K_\theta*\varphi_\sigma)^{(k-1)}(0).
\]

If \(K_\theta\) is analytic in a fixed complex neighborhood of \(0\), Cauchy/Taylor smoothing gives

\[
\boxed{
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O\!\left(C^k\sigma\right)
}
\]

or, under stronger analytic separation,

\[
\boxed{
\langle K_\theta,h_{k,\sigma}\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O\!\left((Ck\sigma)^2\right).
}
\]

To make this error \(Q^{-A}\) uniformly for \(k\le R+3\), it is enough to choose

\[
\sigma\le Q^{-A'}C^{-R}
\]

for the first crude bound, or more realistically a polynomially small

\[
\sigma\le R^{-C_\sigma}
\]

if the analytic separation constants are controlled and the error is \(O((Ck\sigma)^2)\).

A band-limited alternative is to choose \(h_k\) with

\[
\operatorname{supp}\widehat h_k\subset[-L,L]
\]

and

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_k\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O(Q^{-A})
\]

on the admissible compact \(\theta\)-range. But stable recovery of derivatives/moments through \(k\le R+3\) forces

\[
\boxed{
L\gtrsim R^{C_L}.
}
\]

---

# 2. Fourier transforms and prime-side statistic

For the Gaussian derivative probes,

\[
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(\xi)
=
\frac{(i\xi)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
e^{-\sigma^2\xi^2/2}.
\]

The explicit formula produces the prime-side statistic

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_{k,\sigma}(c\log n).
}
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\frac{(ic\log n)^{k-1}}{(k-1)!}
e^{-\sigma^2c^2(\log n)^2/2}.
\]

For a band-limited probe \(h_k\), the statistic is the same expression with \(\widehat h_k(c\log n)\) compactly supported in

\[
|c\log n|\le L.
\]

The zero-side singular anti-design event then implies

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
\mathcal G_k(\gamma,c)+\mathcal T_k(\gamma,c)+O(Q^{-A})
}
\]

for

\[
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

In vector form,

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right\|_2
\le Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Here \(\mathbf G_R\) is the gamma/background vector and \(\mathbf T_R\) is the regularized tail/canonical residual vector.

---

# 3. Minimal bandwidth and prime range

For Gaussian probes, the exponential factor cuts the prime sum when

\[
\sigma c\log n\gtrsim \sqrt{k},
\]

so for \(k\le R+3\),

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{\sqrt R}{\sigma c}.
}
\]

If \(\sigma=R^{-C_\sigma}\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C_\sigma+1/2}}{c}.
}
\]

For band-limited probes with bandwidth \(L\),

\[
|c\log n|\le L,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{L}{c}.
}
\]

Since stable recovery through depth \(R\) requires

\[
L\gtrsim R^{C_L},
\]

the prime range is at least

\[
\boxed{
\log n\lesssim \frac{R^{C_L}}{c}.
}
\]

In the deep singular regime,

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\]

so

\[
\frac1c\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\log n\gtrsim Q(\log Q)^{C_0}
}
\]

even before the \(R^{C_L}\) factor. This is longer than the ordinary packet-frequency/conductor scale

\[
\log n\asymp Q.
\]

---

# 4. Can band-limiting avoid long-prime control?

No, not if the probes genuinely recover the moments

\[
\sin(k\theta),\qquad 3\le k\le R+3.
\]

The uncertainty principle is the obstruction:

\[
\text{recover \(R\) local derivative/moment modes}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{bandwidth at least polynomial in \(R\)}.
\]

Thus

\[
L\gtrsim R^{C_L}
\]

and hence

\[
\log n\lesssim R^{C_L}/c.
\]

Because \(c^{-1}\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}\), the explicit-formula prime vector necessarily involves primes beyond the ordinary \(\log n\asymp Q\) range.

Band-limiting improves formal cleanliness, but it does not remove the need for long-prime control.

---

# 5. Explicit-formula exclusion theorem needed

The clean theorem target is:

## Singular explicit-formula anti-design exclusion

Let

\[
cQ\ll(\log Q)^{-C_0},
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

Let \(h_k\), \(3\le k\le R+3\), be analytic or band-limited probes satisfying

\[
\langle K_\theta,h_k\rangle
=
\sin(k\theta)+O(Q^{-A_0})
\]

for all same-scale packets in the canonical singular cluster.

Define

\[
\mathcal P_k(\gamma,c)
=
2\Re
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac{\Lambda(n)}{\sqrt n}
n^{-i\gamma}
\widehat h_k(c\log n).
\]

Then actual zeta should satisfy

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf G_R(\gamma,c)
-
\mathbf T_R(\gamma,c)
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This excludes

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3,
\]

and therefore closes the deep singular branch via dominance.

---

# 6. No-go: long-prime control is unavoidable

The explicit formula gives a precise equivalence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\text{prime-vector hits a prescribed target.}
}
\]

But excluding that target is not available from standard local geometry or standard AFE upper bounds.

The required statement is a deterministic anti-concentration theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf P_R(\gamma,c)
\not\approx
\mathbf G_R+\mathbf T_R.
}
\]

Because the prime range is

\[
\log n\lesssim R^{C}/c,
\]

and \(1/c\gg Q(\log Q)^{C_0}\), this theorem requires control over long-prime vectors beyond the ordinary packet-frequency scale.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{deep singular exclusion requires a new actual-prime vector nonrecurrence theorem.}
}
\]

It is not a consequence of the ordinary Wronskian route, and band-limited probes do not avoid the long-prime issue.

---

# Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Deep singular dominance is proven modulo the anti-design exception.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The anti-design exception translates cleanly to an explicit-formula prime-vector target.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Excluding that target requires new long-prime actual-zeta nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

So the final theorem needed for this branch is:

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Without that, the deep singular branch remains reduced but not closed.
