}
\]

---

## Case C — Exterior coefficient mass is missing

If Agent 3 cannot prove

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then the problem is upstream of zero-set sampling.

Next allocation:

\[
\boxed{
2\text{ agents on \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbol rank,}
\quad
2\text{ on basis-normalized exterior algebra,}
\quad
1\text{ on main/dual rank,}
\quad
1\text{ on canonical audit.}
}
\]

This would mean the \(\mathbf M\)-route is not yet ready for large sieve analysis.

---

## Case D — Averaged-to-pointwise fails

If Agent 4 shows that an averaged theorem

\[
\sum_{Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}
\]

cannot imply

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

at a specified zero, then split the theorem into two inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Zero-Set Cofactor Large Sieve}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Bad-Zero Exclusion for \(\mathbf M\).}
}
\]

Next allocation:

\[
\boxed{
2\text{ agents on derivative propagation of small \(\mathbf M\),}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
2\text{ agents on local \(Z_\alpha\)-zero density/sampling,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
2\text{ agents on direct pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Roadmap from \(\mathbf M\) to final angle/incidence

Once the \(\mathbf M\) theorem is available:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

we have two factors:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The final ordinary theorem is still the nonalignment/incidence bound:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}

The next allocation after a successful \(\mathbf M\)-round should be:

\[
\boxed{
3\text{ agents on direct actual-orbit incidence,}
}

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
1\text{ agent on canonical audit/singular branch.}
}
\]

The final theorem will likely be another named actual-zeta arithmetic input unless a genuine structural nonalignment mechanism appears.

---

## Assistant (2026-04-27 07:48:07)

## Agent 6 / F — Synthesis and next allocation after this \(\mathbf M\) round

I do **not** see new substantive Agent 1–5 outputs in the attached message; the attachment contains the next-round prompts and shared background. So this is a **status synthesis from the current \(\mathbf M\)-branch setup**, not a post-result synthesis. The branch has moved correctly from the parked Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence input to the cofactor-vector theorem. 

---

# 1. Kernel status: \(K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\)

The kernel object is

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

The needed estimate is not a pointwise bound on \(K_J(\xi)\) alone, but an **operator bound** on the matrix

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\]

where

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,\qquad |S|=R+1.
\]

The desired form is

\[
\sum_{S,T}
\langle \mathbf A_S,\mathbf A_T\rangle
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{kernel theorem not proved.}
}
\]

The argument-principle representation

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]

is useful but only gives a representation. The missing input is a zero-correlation / zero-set spectral large-sieve theorem for \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros.

So the current named kernel input is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Subset-product resonance status

The relevant frequencies are

\[
\Omega_S-\Omega_T=\log(N_S/N_T),
\]

with

\[
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n.
\]

The cleanest support is likely **prime-supported and squarefree**, because then

\[
N_S=N_T
\Longleftrightarrow
S=T
\]

up to ordering. This removes exact collisions.

However, near-collisions remain:

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le \eta.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact collisions can likely be controlled by prime/squarefree support;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{near-collision bounds are still open.}
}
\]

The required theorem is a weighted multiplicative-combinatorics estimate of the form

\[
\sum_{T:\,|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le \eta}|\mathbf A_T|^2
\le Q^{A}\cdot \text{acceptable local mass}.
\]

This must be matched to the kernel regimes for \(K_J(\xi)\). Without this, even a kernel estimate may be defeated by dense clusters.

---

# 3. Exterior coefficient mass status

The diagonal term is

\[
K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
\]

The needed input is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{likely feasible, but not yet fully canonical.}
}
\]

This should follow from a basis-normalized exterior-volume lower bound for the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block, provided the packet-frequency symbol/rank inputs hold for the actual canonical model.

But it must be proved for

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2,
\]

not only a main-term or prime-only model. Because \(\mathbf M\) is multilinear in \(R+1\) source rows, mixed minors matter.

So exterior mass is probably not the deepest blocker, but it needs a canonical theorem.

---

# 4. Averaged-to-pointwise status

The averaged theorem is

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

The pointwise theorem needed for a specified admissible zero is

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{averaged does not automatically imply pointwise.}
}
\]

An averaged lower bound permits isolated bad zeros. To upgrade it, one needs a bad-zero exclusion principle, such as:

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\Longrightarrow
\text{smallness propagates to enough nearby \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros},
\]

or a direct pointwise nonrecurrence theorem.

Derivative propagation alone may be too weak if the local \(Z_\alpha\)-zero density is sparse. So this is a separate serious issue.

---

# 5. Which named theorem is next?

There are two possible named inputs:

## A. \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve

Averaged form:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
}
\]

This is the right next named theorem if the team wants to keep the large-sieve route.

## B. Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

Pointwise form:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Longrightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is stronger and closer to what Gate 1 needs.

Current recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Name the averaged input as \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve,}
}
\]

but keep the pointwise input separate as

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence / Bad-Zero Exclusion.}
}
\]

The averaged theorem alone is not enough unless paired with a pointwise upgrade.

---

# 6. Recommended next allocation

Do **not** move to angle/incidence yet. The \(\mathbf M\) branch is not reduced enough.

Recommended split:

1. **Two agents on \(K_J\).**  
   One works via the argument principle and \(Z_\alpha'/Z_\alpha\); one works on operator bounds for the kernel matrix.

2. **One agent on subset-product resonances.**  
   Focus on prime/squarefree support, exact collision removal, and near-collision cluster bounds.

3. **One agent on exterior coefficient mass.**  
   Prove the diagonal mass lower bound for canonical \(\mathbf M\).

4. **One agent on averaged-to-pointwise.**  
   Try to formulate and prove bad-zero exclusion or direct pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence.

5. **One agent on canonical audit.**  
   Ensure \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\), mixed minors, and \(E_2\)-derivative errors through \(2R+1\) remain controlled.

Keep the singular branch separate and parked unless new singular-specific information arrives.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Stay on }\mathbf M\text{ for the next round.}
}
\]

The branch is currently reduced to three linked inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve for }K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{subset-product resonance control,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{averaged-to-pointwise / cofactor-vector nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Only after these are proved or named should the project move to the final angle/incidence theorem.

## Agent 6 / F — \(\mathbf M\)-branch synthesis and next allocation

Current decision:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue the }\mathbf M\text{ branch for one more focused round. Do not move to angle/incidence yet.}
}
\]

The \(\mathbf M\)-branch is not closed, but it still has concrete substructure: the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral kernel, prime subset-product near-collisions, exterior coefficient mass, canonical transfer, and pointwise-versus-averaged conversion. The latest prompt identifies exactly those lanes as the active \(\mathbf M\)-round tasks. 

---

# 1. Status of \(K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T)\) after resonance quotienting

The key kernel is

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

The \(\mathbf M\)-large sieve needs an operator lower bound for

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\]

where

\[
\Omega_S=\log N_S,
\qquad
N_S=\prod_{n\in S}n,
\qquad
|S|=R+1.
\]

After quotienting near-resonant subset-product frequencies into clusters

\[
\mathcal C_\nu=\{S:|\Omega_S-\omega_\nu|\le \eta_0\},
\]

the desired reduced Gram matrix is

\[
G_{\nu\mu}=K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu),
\]

with target lower bound

\[
G\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Not proved.}
}
\]

The argument-principle representation

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]

is only a representation. It does not yet give the required medium-frequency cancellation or positive operator bound.

Current named input if this stalls:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Status of prime subset-product near-collision control

For prime-supported squarefree blocks,

\[
\Omega_S=\sum_{p\in S}\log p.
\]

Exact collisions are clean:

\[
\Omega_S=\Omega_T
\iff
S=T
\]

up to ordering, by unique factorization.

The remaining issue is near-collision:

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le \eta.
\]

The target is a Hamming-stratified estimate of the form

\[
\#\{T:h(S,T)=h,\ |\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le\eta\}
\le
Q^C
\left(
1+
\binom{k}{h}\binom{P-k}{h}
\frac{\eta}{hQ}
\right),
\]

with \(k=R+1\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exact collisions are manageable with prime support; near-collision bounds remain open.}
}
\]

This remains worth attacking because it is concrete multiplicative combinatorics. It should be pursued before naming the whole \(\mathbf M\) theorem as a black box.

---

# 3. Status of exterior coefficient mass

The diagonal term is

\[
K_J(0)\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2.
\]

The needed lower bound is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Green-feasible, but still needs canonical proof.}
}
\]

For a model packet-frequency block, this should follow from basis-normalized exterior algebra, essentially

\[
\sum_{|S|=R+1}|\det U_S|^2=\det(UU^\ast),
\]

provided the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows have stable rank and the normalization is controlled.

However, this must be proved for the canonical block, not a pure main-term toy.

---

# 4. Canonical transfer obstacles

The canonical object is

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The cofactor vector is multilinear in \(R+1\) source rows, so

\[
\mathbf M_{\can}
\]

contains pure \(P_2\), pure \(D_2\), mixed \(P_2/D_2\), \(B_2\)-containing, and \(E_2\)-containing minors.

Main warning:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A pure main-term or prime-only \(\mathbf M\) lower bound does not automatically transfer to \(\mathbf M_{\can}\).}
}
\]

A valid transfer theorem needs derivative error control through approximately

\[
2R+1
\]

normalized derivatives, plus a cofactor Lipschitz bound:

\[
|\mathbf M_{\can}-\mathbf M_{\model}|
\le
Q^{A_L}\varepsilon_E.
\]

To transfer a model lower bound

\[
|\mathbf M_{\model}|\ge Q^{-A_M},
\]

we need

\[
Q^{A_L}\varepsilon_E\le \frac12Q^{-A_M}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical transfer is understood structurally but not yet certified for all mixed minors.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Averaged versus pointwise status

Averaged target:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

Pointwise target:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{averaged does not imply pointwise without a separate bad-zero exclusion theorem.}
}
\]

An averaged large sieve can tolerate isolated bad zeros. For Gate 1 at a specified admissible zero, this is insufficient unless one proves:

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\text{badness propagates to nearby \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros}
\]

or proves pointwise cofactor nonrecurrence directly.

So the \(\mathbf M\)-branch may split into two named inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence / Bad-Zero Exclusion.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Decision: continue, name, or move?

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue the \(\mathbf M\)-branch for one focused round.}
}
\]

Do not move to final angle/incidence yet, because \(\mathbf M\) is not yet reduced to a single black-box theorem. There are still concrete subproblems:

1. quotient kernel estimates;
2. prime subset-product near-collision bounds;
3. exterior coefficient mass;
4. canonical mixed-minor transfer;
5. averaged-to-pointwise conversion.

If the next round again reduces all of these to unproved zero-correlation/nonrecurrence inputs, then name the \(\mathbf M\)-package and move to angle/incidence.

---

# 7. Recommended next allocation

Use this split:

1. **Agent 1 — Quotient kernel theorem.**  
   Prove or name the \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral large sieve after resonance quotienting.

2. **Agent 2 — Prime subset-product near-collision.**  
   Focus on squarefree prime subsets and Hamming-stratified near-collision estimates.

3. **Agent 3 — Exterior coefficient mass.**  
   Prove \(\sum_S|\mathbf A_S|^2\ge Q^{-A}\) in the basis-normalized packet model.

4. **Agent 4 — Pointwise \(\mathbf M\)-nonrecurrence.**  
   Decide whether bad-zero exclusion is possible or must be named separately.

5. **Agent 5 — Canonical mixed-minor audit.**  
   Ensure \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\), high derivatives, and mixed minors are handled.

6. **Agent 6 — Synthesis / stop condition.**  
   Decide after that round whether to name the \(\mathbf M\)-input or proceed to angle/incidence.

Keep the singular branch separate and parked unless a singular-specific theorem emerges.

\text{The \(\mathbf M\)-route is not yet exhausted.}
}

## Agent 6 / F — \(\mathbf M\)-round synthesis

The \(\mathbf M\) branch has now reached the same kind of boundary as the cell branch: it is structurally organized, but the decisive inputs are actual-zeta arithmetic theorems. I recommend naming the \(\mathbf M\) inputs, then moving part of the allocation to angle/incidence while retaining a small \(\mathbf M\)-audit lane.

The latest coordinator brief identifies the unresolved \(\mathbf M\)-issues as quotient zero-set kernel estimates, full-support subset-product resonance, prime-block versus canonical transfer, pointwise cofactor nonrecurrence, and canonical mixed-minor modeling. 

---

# 1. Quotient \(Z_\alpha\)-zero spectral kernel

The desired averaged theorem is controlled by

\[
K_J(\Omega_S-\Omega_T),
\qquad
K_J(\xi)=
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
w_J(m_j)e^{-im_j\xi}.
\]

After resonance quotienting, the target is a positive operator bound

\[
\boxed{
\bigl(K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\bigr)_{\nu,\mu}
\ge
Q^{-A}K_J(0)I.
}
\]

The argument-principle identity

\[
K_J(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}
\int_{\partial\Omega}
w_J(s)e^{-is\xi}
\frac{Z_\alpha'(s)}{Z_\alpha(s)}\,ds
\]

is useful only as a representation. It does not itself provide the needed medium-frequency cancellation or positive operator estimate.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not proved; should be named as an arithmetic input.}
}
\]

Suggested name:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Subset-product resonance status

For prime-supported squarefree packet blocks,

\[
\Omega_S=\sum_{p\in S}\log p,
\]

exact collisions are clean:

\[
\Omega_S=\Omega_T
\iff
S=T.
\]

So prime support removes exact collisions by unique factorization.

For full canonical support, where \(n\) ranges over AFE integers, exact subset-product collisions satisfy

\[
N_S=N_T
\iff
\mathbf E(S)=\mathbf E(T),
\]

where \(\mathbf E(S)\) is the summed prime-exponent vector of the selected integers. This suggests an exact-collision quotient by exponent vectors.

The open part is near-collision:

\[
|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le\eta.
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Hamming-stratified near-collision bounds for subset products,}
}
\]

or a weighted/operator version controlling

\[
\sum_{T:|\Omega_S-\Omega_T|\le\eta}|\mathbf A_T|^2.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact-collision structure is understood; near-collision control remains open.}
}
\]

Suggested name:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Subset-Product Resonance Bound.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Canonical support and mixed-minor status

The cofactor vector must be built from

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The safe leading model is

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf M_{\lead}
=
\mathbf M[B_2+P_2+D_2],
}
\]

with perturbation

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf M_{\can}
=
\mathbf M[B_2+P_2+D_2]
+
\mathbf M_{\pert}[E_2].
}
\]

A prime-only \(\mathbf M\) theorem is **not** canonical unless one proves a transfer theorem from the omitted non-prime terms. That transfer is not currently justified.

Key audit conclusions:

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ should remain in the leading model unless proved perturbative.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
P_2/D_2\text{ mixed minors may be leading, especially in the symmetric regime.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
E_2\text{-containing minors are perturbative only with derivative control through }2R+1.
}
\]

Required error condition:

\[
\max_{k\le2R+1}|\mathcal D^kE_2|\le Q^{-A_E}
\]

with enough slack to beat the cofactor Lipschitz amplification.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical model is clear; full transfer theorem still needed.}
}
\]

Suggested guardrail theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Cofactor Transfer Theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Pointwise status

The averaged theorem

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J)
\]

does not imply the pointwise theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

An averaged lower bound can allow isolated bad zeros.

Thus a separate pointwise input is needed unless one proves a bad-zero propagation principle:

\[
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ll Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\text{many nearby \(Z_\alpha\)-zeros also have small \(\mathbf M\)}.
\]

No such propagation theorem is currently available.

Suggested name:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence Theorem.}
}
\]

Statement:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Which theorem should be named?

Name both layers:

## Input 2A — Averaged layer

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting.}
}
\]

Averaged form:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

This depends on:

\[
K_J(\omega_\nu-\omega_\mu)\ge Q^{-A}K_J(0)I,
\]

subset-product resonance control, exterior coefficient mass, and canonical transfer.

## Input 2B — Pointwise layer

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

Pointwise form:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is what the Gate 1 route actually needs at the specified zero.

The averaged input is useful, but the pointwise input remains necessary unless averaged-to-pointwise is proved.

---

# 6. Recommended next allocation

Do **not** return to cell theorem now. It is parked.

Do **not** move fully to angle/incidence yet. The \(\mathbf M\) branch needs a final naming/audit pass and then partial transition.

Recommended split:

\[
\boxed{
2\text{ agents on }\mathbf M,\quad
3\text{ agents on angle/incidence,\quad 1 audit/singular.}
}
\]

Specifically:

1. **Agent 1 — \(\mathbf M\) averaged theorem finalization.**  
   Formalize the \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after resonance quotienting as a named input, including resonance and canonical-transfer assumptions.

2. **Agent 2 — Pointwise Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence.**  
   Try one final direct pointwise avoidance formulation; otherwise name it as Input 2B.

3. **Agent 3 — Angle/incidence direct theorem.**  
   Begin attack on
   \[
   |\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
   \ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
   \]

4. **Agent 4 — Folded main/dual angle structure.**  
   Search for nonalignment mechanisms in the full Wronskian pairing.

5. **Agent 5 — Resultant/common-small-value formulation.**  
   Treat
   \[
   Z_\alpha=0,\quad \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R\approx0
   \]
   as an actual-orbit incidence problem.

6. **Agent 6 — Canonical/singular audit.**  
   Keep the canonical \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) bookkeeping intact and keep the singular anti-design branch separate.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(\mathbf M\) is not proved, but it is now reduced to named arithmetic inputs.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Name the \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve and Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence inputs.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Begin transitioning to the final angle/incidence theorem while retaining \(\mathbf M\) audit lanes.}
}

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:14:20)

## Agent 6 / F — Synthesis and next roadmap

The ordinary route has now entered the final incidence layer. The prior two ordinary inputs are parked as named arithmetic hypotheses, and the remaining theorem is the Wronskian angle/nonalignment bound. The uploaded brief explicitly sets this as the new active target while keeping the singular branch separate. 

---

# 1. Current named ordinary-route inputs

## Input 1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

This is the parked theorem giving the first row:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It packages the multiblock cell-sum theorem:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input, not proved.}}
\]

---

## Input 2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence / \(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve

This is the parked theorem giving the cofactor vector:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

It has an averaged supporting formulation:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J),
\]

but the pointwise statement remains separately needed because isolated bad zeros can survive an averaged theorem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input, not proved.}}
\]

---

# 2. Remaining ordinary theorem

At a zero

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the Wronskian is

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0)\rangle.
\]

After Inputs 1 and 2, we know only

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The remaining theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This is the final ordinary Wronskian incidence theorem.

---

# 3. Relative difficulty

This theorem appears **harder** than the parked cell input and at least comparable to, probably harder than, the \(\mathbf M\) input.

Reason:

- The cell input is a degree-one nonrecurrence theorem for the \(Z_\alpha\)-row.
- The \(\mathbf M\) input is a norm lower bound for the cofactor vector.
- The angle theorem remains open even if both vectors have polynomial norm.

A phase-relaxed model can satisfy

\[
|\mathbf z'|\gg Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\gg Q^{-A},
\qquad
\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\approx0.
\]

So the final theorem is not a norm estimate. It is a genuine **nonalignment/incidence** theorem.

Classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{hardest ordinary-route input so far.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Can the angle theorem be decomposed further?

Yes, but likely only into equivalent actual-orbit incidence statements. The useful decompositions are the following.

---

## A. Direct common-small-value formulation

Prove:

\[
\boxed{
|Z_\alpha(m)|+
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero, this gives

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the most direct final theorem.

Likely obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{requires actual-orbit common-zero / common-small-value nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

---

## B. Exterior-angle formulation

Let \(V\) be the subspace spanned by the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet rows. The cofactor vector \(\mathbf M\) is a Hodge-dual normal to \(V\). The bad event

\[
\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle=0
\]

is equivalent to

\[
\mathbf z'\in V.
\]

Thus the theorem becomes

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This looks close to the earlier \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol-rank calculations, but it is stronger: symbol-rank shows nonredundancy in an AFE-symbol model; this theorem needs pointwise actual-orbit quantitative separation at \(m_0\).

Likely obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symbol rank is not enough; pointwise actual-zeta incidence remains.}
}
\]

---

## C. Folded main/dual nonalignment

Decompose the pairing into

\[
\text{pure main}+\text{pure dual}+\text{mixed main/dual}+B_2\text{-mixed}+E_2\text{-perturbative}.
\]

In tilted regimes,

\[
|\alpha|Q\gtrsim \log Q,
\]

branch dominance may help. But in the hard symmetric regime,

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

main/dual cancellation is again a folded subset-product actual-orbit nonrecurrence problem.

Likely obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no known sign, positivity, or commutator invariant.}
}
\]

---

## D. Actual-orbit incidence

Define the bad variety

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}
=
\{u:Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0\}.
\]

Then prove

\[
\operatorname{dist}(u(m_0),\mathcal I_{\rm bad})\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is probably the most honest formulation.

Likely obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{requires new actual-prime-log orbit avoidance theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Singular branch remains separate

The singular branch is still not part of the ordinary angle theorem.

Deep singular scale:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

is handled by dominance unless singular anti-design occurs. The remaining singular theorem is

\[
\boxed{
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

This uses long-prime explicit-formula probes with range roughly

\[
\log n\lesssim R^C/c,
\]

not the ordinary packet-frequency range. It should remain a separate branch.

---

# 6. Recommendation for next allocation

The next round should focus mostly on the final angle/incidence theorem, while retaining one canonical audit lane.

Recommended allocation:

1. **Agent 1 — Direct common-small-value theorem.**  
   Attack
   \[
   |Z_\alpha|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A}.
   \]

2. **Agent 2 — Exterior-angle theorem.**  
   Attack
   \[
   \operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)\ge Q^{-A}.
   \]

3. **Agent 3 — Folded main/dual angle structure.**  
   Search for nonalignment mechanisms in the full pairing.

4. **Agent 4 — Actual-orbit incidence/nonrecurrence.**  
   Formulate the bad variety and recurrence-cost / avoidance theorem.

5. **Agent 5 — Canonical final-Wronskian audit.**  
   Ensure the final determinant uses
   \[
   q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
   \]
   and that \(E_2\) transfer through the full determinant is controlled.

6. **Agent 6 — Synthesis / stop condition.**  
   Decide after the next round whether to:
   - prove the angle theorem,
   - name it as Input 3,
   - return to \(\mathbf M\),
   - or split off a special \(\alpha\)-regime.

---

# 7. Likely next named input

If the next round does not find a structural mechanism, the final ordinary theorem should be named:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence Theorem.}
}
\]

Statement:

\[
\boxed{
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

or equivalently, assuming Inputs 1 and 2,

\[
\boxed{
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
}
\]

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Move the main allocation to angle/incidence.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Keep one canonical audit lane and keep singular anti-design separate.}
}
\]

The ordinary route now has two named inputs parked; the active target is the final Wronskian angle/nonalignment theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:23:58)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 6 / F — Synthesis and stop condition

The final ordinary-route angle theorem is **not proved** by the current architecture, and it is no longer usefully decomposing into softer local-algebra statements. It should now be named as the third ordinary-route black-box arithmetic input.

The uploaded prompt frames this as the stop-condition round for the angle/incidence theorem: if no structural proof emerges, name the input. 

---

# 1. Status of the angle-theorem routes

## A. Common-small-value theorem

Target:

\[
|Z_\alpha(m)|+|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the cleanest direct form. At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero, it gives

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{not proved.}}
\]

It reduces to actual-orbit common-small-value nonrecurrence for two canonical exponential-polynomial/AFE objects. Phase-relaxed models can have approximate common smallness, so generic codimension is insufficient.

---

## B. Exterior-angle theorem

At

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

we have

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

Let \(V(m_0)\) be the row span of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block. Then \(\mathbf M\) is a Hodge-dual normal to \(V\), and the bad event is

\[
\mathbf z'\in V.
\]

The desired quantitative version is

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\mathbf z',V)\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{not proved.}}
\]

Earlier symbol-rank results show that \(Z_\alpha\) is not formally redundant with the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet symbols on packet-frequency blocks. They do **not** give a pointwise quantitative distance between \(\mathbf z'\) and the actual row span \(V(m_0)\).

So exterior algebra clarifies the geometry but does not provide the lower bound.

---

## C. Folded main/dual angle structure

One may decompose

\[
\mathbf z'=\mathbf z'_++\mathbf z'_-+\mathbf z'_B+\mathbf z'_E
\]

and

\[
\mathbf M=\mathbf M_+ + \mathbf M_-+\mathbf M_{\rm mix}+\mathbf M_B+\mathbf M_E.
\]

The pairing contains pure-main, pure-dual, mixed main/dual, \(B_2\)-mixed, and \(E_2\)-perturbative terms.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{not proved uniformly.}}
\]

In tilted regimes, branch dominance may simplify some terms. But in the hard symmetric regime

\[
|\alpha|Q\ll1,
\]

there is still no sign, positivity, Hermitian, skew, or commutator invariant forcing nonalignment. The problem remains folded subset-product actual-orbit nonrecurrence.

---

## D. Actual-orbit incidence formulation

Define the bad incidence variety

\[
\mathcal I_{\rm bad}
=
\{u: Z_\alpha(u)=0,\ \widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(u,\alpha)=0\}.
\]

The theorem becomes

\[
\operatorname{dist}(u(m_0),\mathcal I_{\rm bad})\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{honest formulation, not a proof.}}
\]

This is likely the most accurate mathematical description of the missing input.

---

## E. Canonical transfer

The final Wronskian matrix is

\[
\left(C_\ell(\mathcal D)G_j(m,\alpha)\right)_{0\le j,\ell\le R+1},
\]

with

\[
G_0=Z_\alpha,\qquad
G_{j+1}=\mathcal D^jq''_{\can}.
\]

and

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

The existing high-derivative budget through roughly

\[
2R+1
\]

normalized derivatives remains the right order for the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block and cofactor construction. A model Wronskian angle theorem transfers only if the determinant perturbation from \(E_2\), truncation, tails, and any model simplifications is less than the claimed lower bound.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{canonical audit is clear; it does not prove the angle theorem.}}
\]

---

# 2. Regime status

## \(|\alpha|Q\gtrsim\log Q\)

Tilted branch dominance may simplify main/dual interactions, but it does not automatically prove the full Wronskian angle unless the relevant one-branch incidence theorem is also supplied.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{partially simplified, not closed.}}
\]

## \(|\alpha|Q\ll\log Q\)

No dominance mechanism strong enough to close the theorem is known.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

## \(|\alpha|Q\ll1\)

This is the hard symmetric regime.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; actual-orbit folded incidence/nonrecurrence needed.}}
\]

---

# 3. Is the theorem meaningfully decomposable further?

Not at the current level.

The theorem can be restated as:

\[
\text{common-small-value nonrecurrence,}
\]

\[
\text{exterior-angle lower bound,}
\]

\[
\text{folded main/dual nonalignment,}
\]

or

\[
\text{actual-orbit incidence avoidance.}
\]

But these are equivalent formulations of the same missing arithmetic phenomenon. None is currently reducing to a softer local, algebraic, or analytic lemma.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Stop decomposing the ordinary route here and name the angle theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Named input

## Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence Theorem

Assume the ordinary-scale setup and the canonical Wronskian

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m,\alpha).
\]

Then for every admissible ordinary center satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

Equivalently, assuming the parked first two inputs,

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

one has

\[
\boxed{
|\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\,|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|.
}
\]

This is the third ordinary-route arithmetic input.

---

# 5. Full ordinary-route stack

The ordinary Gate 1 path is now:

## Input 1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Input 2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

## Input 3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Together these imply

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then the existing Wronskian-to-finite-jet machinery gives finite-jet anti-design, and hence Gate 1 in the ordinary regime.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 1 + Input 2 + Input 3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

# 6. Next allocation recommendation

Do **not** run another angle-decomposition round unless a genuinely new structural mechanism appears.

Recommended next move:

\[
\boxed{
\text{synthesize final proof architecture and identify all named arithmetic inputs.}
}
\]

   \]

## Agent 6 / F — Final proof-state dependency graph

The current proof state is now best understood as a **conditional architecture**, not as a completed RH proof. The ordinary Gate 1 route has been reduced to three named actual-zeta arithmetic inputs; the singular route has a separate named anti-design input; and downstream Gate 2 / row conversion still has the \(q_0\)-wall. The uploaded coordinator brief explicitly asks for this dependency map rather than another decomposition round. 

---

# 1. Ordinary Gate 1 dependency chain

For ordinary scale,

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1,
\qquad
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

the Wronskian route is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

The ordinary route now depends on three named inputs.

---

## Input 1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

Statement:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This implies:

\[
\sup_{|t|\le R}|Z_\alpha(m_0+\lambda t)|\ge Q^{-A'}
\]

and then:

\[
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A''}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named black-box input; numerically supported; not proved.}}
\]

---

## Input 2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

Statement:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Averaged support theorem:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j)|^2
\ge
Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

But averaged does not imply pointwise without a separate bad-zero exclusion.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named black-box input; structurally reduced; not proved.}}
\]

Sub-inputs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(Z_\alpha\)-Zero Spectral Large Sieve after Resonance Quotienting}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Subset-Product Resonance Bound}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical Cofactor Transfer}
}
\]

---

## Input 3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence

Statement:

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Equivalently:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named black-box input; not proved.}}
\]

No structural sign, positivity, Hodge, Hermitian, commutator, or generic transversality mechanism has closed this.

---

## Ordinary Gate 1 implication

Inputs 1–3 give:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\qquad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\]

and

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Therefore:

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then the existing Wronskian-to-finite-jet machinery gives finite-jet anti-design:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\mathcal D^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Then finite-jet anti-design plus analytic complexity/Remez–Bernstein propagation gives ordinary Gate 1:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inputs 1--3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional.}}
\]

---

# 2. Singular Gate 1 branch

Deep singular scale:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

Ordinary packet-frequency Wronskians do not apply because the normalized packet-frequency nodes collapse:

\[
x_n=\lambda\log n\asymp \lambda Q\ll1.
\]

Use local singular scaling instead:

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad c=\lambda.
\]

Then

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)
\sim c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x),
\]

and

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\sim
c^{-5}\int_X |Q_{\rm sing}''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Thus Gate 1 follows by dominance unless:

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
\]

The exceptional branch is same-scale singular anti-design:

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Explicit formula translation gives the named singular input:

---

## Input 4 — Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion

Statement:

\[
\left\|
\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R
\right\|_2
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This excludes the singular sine-moment anti-design and therefore proves singular Gate 1 by dominance.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named black-box input; not proved.}}
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Input 4}
\Rightarrow
\text{singular Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Global Gate 1

The scale split is:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp1
\quad\text{ordinary},
\]

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\quad\text{deep singular},
\]

with a mildly singular transition regime requiring either explicit \(\mu=\lambda Q\) losses or assignment to one of the two branches.

Conditional global Gate 1 statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inputs 1--3}
+
\text{Input 4}
+
\text{mild-singular transition control}
\Rightarrow
\text{global Gate 1}.
}
\]

The transition control remains a bookkeeping theorem:

\[
\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

can use Wronskian with explicit \(\mu\)-loss if the determinant conditioning loses at most \(\mu^{-O(R)}\), while

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}
\]

uses singular dominance plus Input 4.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional; mild-singular transition should be stated explicitly.}}
\]

---

# 4. Downstream Gate 2 and row conversion

Gate 1 gives source curvature mass:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Gate 2 target is roughly:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

The known row architecture has leading source-divisible rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

where

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q''_{\can})^3}{288}.
\]

Thus row conversion needs source-factor nondegeneracy:

\[
|H|\ge Q^{-C_H}|q''_{\can}|^3,
\]

which is essentially a \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy condition:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

The obstruction is the \(q_0\)-wall:

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

At \(q_0=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3=u,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can},
\]

so Gate 1 / Gate 2 mass can coexist with \(q_0\approx0\). Existing sampling does not force \(q_0\)-nondegeneracy.

Therefore downstream split:

---

## Branch A — nondegenerate \(q_0\)

Input needed:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

at a row-sampling point where Gate 2 mass is visible.

Then:

\[
|H(m_\ast)|
\ge Q^{-C}|q''_{\can}(m_\ast)|^3,
\]

and the row lower bound follows from Gate 2 and anisotropy.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional; sampling/nondegeneracy theorem still needed.}}
\]

---

## Branch B — \(q_0\)-wall

If

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C}
\]

on all relevant row-sampling points, then the known source-divisible row conversion may collapse.

Needed input:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-robust row/invariant visible at }q_0\approx0.
}
\]

or a theorem showing that \(q_0\approx0\) cannot persist on the Gate 2 mass set.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

---

| Component | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| Wronskian algebra identity \(\widetilde W=\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\) | Proved/structural | Identity-level. |

| \(q_0\)-wall | Open | Major downstream blocker. |
| Final RH contradiction | Not proved | Requires Gate 1, Gate 2, row conversion, global-to-contradiction bridge. |

## Input 3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence

Purpose:

\ge

\Rightarrow

# 2. Transition theorem between ordinary and deep singular

Ordinary route:

\[
\lambda Q\asymp 1.
\]

Deep singular route:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

The transition regime is:

\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \lambda Q\lesssim 1.
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mu=\lambda Q\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Wronskian machinery works with explicit }\mu\text{-losses.}
}
\]

A plausible acceptable loss is:

\[
\mu^{-O(R)},
\]

because for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

and

\[
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

one gets

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}=Q^{o(1)}.
\]

A dangerous loss is:

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)},
\]

which is too large for fixed-polynomial bookkeeping.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional transition theorem; not yet fully proved.}}
\]

---

# 3. Gate 2 theorem needed

Gate 1 supplies source curvature mass:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|u(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 2 target:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|u(m)|^2
\left(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2\right)
\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

The obstruction is the base-locus:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\int|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\Rightarrow
\int|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A}|I|
}
\]

under the canonical derivative/complexity package.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{partly structured; base-locus rigidity still needed.}}
\]

This is likely more tractable than the hardest ordinary arithmetic inputs, because it is a local analytic/ODE rigidity problem rather than global actual-prime nonrecurrence.

---

# 4. Row-conversion split and \(q_0\)-wall

Known row architecture:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q''_{\can})^3}{288}
=
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Thus the nondegenerate branch needs:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Then Gate 2 mass can be converted into row lower bounds, assuming correction terms are controlled.

The wall branch is:

\[
\boxed{
|q_0|<Q^{-C}.
}
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we still have

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3=u,
\]

so source and anisotropy can remain live while the known \(H\)-driven rows collapse.

Needed downstream alternatives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-robust row/invariant not divisible by }q_0\text{ or }H.
}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open and important.}}
\]

---

# 5. Component classification

| Component | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| Wronskian identity \(\widetilde W_R=\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle\) | proved/structural | Algebraic identity. |
| Packet-frequency active blocks | proved/structural | Low-prime issue resolved. |
| \(Z_\alpha\)-symbol rank | essentially settled | Does not prove pointwise nonrecurrence. |
| Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence | named black-box input | Numerically supported; actual-orbit arithmetic open. |
| Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence | named black-box input | Needs zero-set spectral large sieve / pointwise theorem. |
| Wronskian Angle Nonalignment | named black-box input | Final ordinary incidence theorem. |
| Ordinary Gate 1 from Inputs 1–3 | conditional local theorem | Dependency clear. |
| Singular dominance scaling | proved/structural | Dominance unless anti-design. |
| Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion | named black-box input | Long-prime vector nonrecurrence open. |
| Mild transition \(\lambda Q\) theorem | conditional/open | Needs \(\mu^{-O(R)}\), not \(\mu^{-O(R^2)}\). |
| Gate 2 anisotropy propagation | conditional/open | Base-locus rigidity needed. |
| Nondegenerate row conversion | conditional | Needs \(q_0\)-nondegenerate sampling and correction control. |
| \(q_0\)-wall | open/no-go under current rows | Needs source-robust row or exclusion theorem. |
| Canonical transfer \(B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\) | guardrail partly established | Must be enforced in every input. |
| Final RH contradiction | not proved | Requires all above plus global bridge. |

---

# 6. Next priority list

## Priority 1 — Gate 2 anisotropy propagation

This is the most promising next target because it is local analytic/ODE in character and may be provable without a new global actual-prime nonrecurrence theorem.

Target:

\[
\int|u|^2
\Rightarrow
\int|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Main task:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

base-locus rigidity.

---

## Priority 2 — \(q_0\)-wall / source-robust row

This is downstream but critical. Even Gate 1 + Gate 2 may not produce the final row lower bound if \(q_0\approx0\).

Two routes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove \(q_0\)-nondegenerate sampling}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{find source-robust row/invariant visible at }q_0=0.
}
\]

This should be attacked in parallel with Gate 2.

---

## Priority 3 — Mild singular transition

Formalize the \(\mu=\lambda Q\) transition theorem.

Needed:

\[
\mu\gtrsim(\log Q)^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary machinery survives with }Q^{O(1)}\text{ loss}.
\]

This is mostly conditioning/bookkeeping unless \(\mu^{-O(R^2)}\) losses appear.

---

## Priority 4 — Singular anti-design input

The singular branch remains separate and open:

\[
\|\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This is hard actual-prime vector nonrecurrence over a long-prime range. It should stay as a named input unless a new explicit-formula mechanism emerges.

---

## Priority 5 — Return to ordinary named inputs only with new ideas

Inputs 1–3 are all hard actual-zeta arithmetic. They are important, but further decomposition has plateaued. Return only if there is a new mechanism for:

\[
\text{cell nonrecurrence,}
\quad
\text{cofactor nonrecurrence,}
\quad
\text{angle incidence.}
\]

---

Use the next round on the downstream analytic bridge:

1. **Agent 1 — Gate 2 base-locus rigidity.**  
   Attack \(\Gamma_G\approx0,\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0\) under \(u\)-mass.

2. **Agent 2 — Gate 2 propagation/Remez-Bernstein.**  
   Prove mass thickening and analytic propagation from Gate 1 to Gate 2.

3. **Agent 3 — \(q_0\)-wall exclusion.**  
   Test whether Gate 2 mass forces a sample point with \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}\).

4. **Agent 4 — Source-robust row search.**  
   Search for rows/invariants not divisible by \(q_0\) or \(H\).

5. **Agent 5 — Nondegenerate row-conversion and correction control.**  
   Formalize \(A_7,A_9\) lower bound under \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}\).

6. **Agent 6 — Canonical/global audit.**  
   Keep all dependencies canonical and update the global proof map.

## Agent 6 / F — Downstream synthesis and priority map

The current downstream target is the analytic bridge after conditional Gate 1: Gate 2 anisotropy propagation, then row conversion, with the \(q_0\)-wall as the main known obstruction. The ordinary/singular Gate 1 architecture is already conditionally mapped, so the next useful work is downstream rather than another ordinary-route decomposition. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 base-locus status

Gate 2 needs:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

The base-locus obstruction is:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

Using

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

exact base-locus gives

\[
u=6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

Also,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

up to the established normalization. On the exact base-locus \(\Gamma_G=0\), this reduces formally to

\[
2q(q')^2\approx0.
\]

So exact simultaneous vanishing suggests one of:

\[
q\approx0,
\qquad
q'\approx0,
\qquad
u\approx 6q_0-2q_0^3.
\]

But this does **not yet prove** that \(u\approx0\). In particular, the \(q_0\approx0\) case gives

\[
\Gamma_G\approx u,
\]

so \(\Gamma_G\approx0\) would force \(u\approx0\), but away from \(q_0=0\), \(u\) can cancel \(6q_0-2q_0^3\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 base-locus rigidity is plausible but not proved.}
}
\]

Needed theorem:

\[
\boxed{
|u|\text{-mass cannot concentrate on }
\{\Gamma_G\approx0,\ \Gamma_{G,2}\approx0\}
}
\]

under the canonical derivative/complexity package.

---

# 2. Gate 2 propagation status

The desired implication is:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\Longrightarrow
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The intended proof structure is:

1. Gate 1 gives \(L^2\) mass of \(u\).
2. If Gate 2 fails, then on a substantial \(u\)-weighted set,

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|
\]

is small.
3. Remez/Bernstein/Cartan propagation upgrades smallness on that thick set to smallness on an interval or enough analytic control.
4. Base-locus rigidity gives a contradiction with \(u\)-mass.

The likely derivative package required is finite and local, roughly:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q_\zeta|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le k_0,
\]

with \(k_0\) probably around \(6\), because \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) contains \(\Gamma_G''\), hence derivatives of \(u=q''_{\can}\) up to roughly fourth order of \(q\), with margin for propagation.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 propagation is a promising local analytic theorem, but still open.}
}
\]

This is likely more tractable than the named actual-zeta arithmetic inputs because it is an ODE/real-analytic rigidity problem.

---

# 3. \(q_0\)-wall status

Known row conversion uses

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H=yq''_{\can}
\sim
-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

Thus if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and Gate 2 provides a point or thick set where

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then the \(A_7,A_9\) rows can be lower-bounded, modulo correction control.

But if

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C},
\]

then

\[
H\approx0
\]

even when \(u\) and \(\Gamma_G\) are live. At \(q_0=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

So Gate 1 and Gate 2 can both be live while known \(H\)-driven rows collapse.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{\(q_0\)-wall is real under current row architecture.}
}
\]

A nondegenerate sampling theorem

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast:\ |q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is **not currently justified**. Local models with \(q_0\approx0\), \(u\ne0\), and \(\Gamma_G\approx u\) are compatible with the current formulas.

---

# 4. Source-robust row search status

Known rows:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}
\]

appear to retain the common factor

\[
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

Therefore higher rows in the same tower likely do **not** escape the \(q_0\)-wall unless a correction, raw/unprojected row, or different invariant removes the \(H\)-factor.

Needed source-robust row:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no source-robust row currently certified.}
}
\]

This is now a major downstream open input.

If no such row exists, the proof architecture must include a \(q_0\)-wall exclusion theorem.

---

# 5. Nondegenerate row conversion status

In the branch

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

row conversion is plausible.

Using

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288},
\]

we get

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|
\approx
|H|\left(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\right),
\]

so if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
\]

and

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A},
\]

then a pointwise lower bound on rows follows after converting the \(u\)-powers and using vector norm to avoid cancellation between \(A_7\) and \(A_9\).

Remaining requirements:

\[
|\mathrm{Correction}|\le \frac12|\mathrm{Leading}|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nondegenerate row conversion is conditionally closeable.}
}
\]

It needs exact expansions, normalization powers, and correction bounds, but it is less conceptually blocked than the \(q_0\)-wall.

---

# 6. Priority recommendation

## Priority 1 — Gate 2 base-locus + propagation

This is the best next target.

Reason:

\[
\text{Gate 2 appears to be a local analytic/ODE rigidity problem.}
\]

It is more tractable than the named actual-zeta arithmetic inputs and must be proved before row conversion is useful.

Next work:

\[
\boxed{
\int|u|^2\Rightarrow
\int|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
}
\]

via thick-set propagation and base-locus rigidity.

---

## Priority 2 — \(q_0\)-wall row search

Run this in parallel.

Either prove:

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}\Rightarrow \exists |q_0|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

or find a source-robust row/invariant not divisible by \(q_0\) or \(H\).

The current evidence suggests the wall is real, so row search is likely necessary.

---

## Priority 3 — Nondegenerate row conversion

Formalize this branch as a theorem:

\[
\text{Gate 2}
+
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
+
\text{correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

This should be completed to isolate exactly what the \(q_0\)-wall must supply.

---

## Priority 4 — Mild transition and singular branch

Keep singular anti-design and mild transition as named/open branches, but do not prioritize them over Gate 2 and \(q_0\)-wall right now unless new information appears.

---

# Recommended next allocation

1. **Two agents on Gate 2.**  
   One on base-locus ODE rigidity, one on Remez/Bernstein propagation.

2. **Two agents on \(q_0\)-wall.**  
   One on wall exclusion, one on source-robust row/invariant search.

3. **One agent on nondegenerate row conversion.**  
   Formalize leading-row lower bound and correction control.

4. **One agent on canonical/global audit.**  
   Maintain the dependency map and ensure all objects are canonical.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next proof priority: Gate 2 base-locus rigidity and propagation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Parallel priority: resolve the }q_0\text{-wall.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Nondegenerate row conversion is likely closeable once those are handled.}
}
\]

The ordinary and singular Gate 1 branches are conditionally mapped; downstream analytic conversion is now the most productive area.

## Agent 6 / F — Downstream stop condition and next priority

The downstream picture has now sharpened substantially. Gate 2 has a credible local rigidity route, but the **measure-to-interval propagation step is still missing**. Separately, the \(q_0\)-wall is real under the known projected row architecture and requires either a source-robust row or a new wall-exclusion theorem. The uploaded coordinator brief identifies this as the current focus. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 status

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 2 needs

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The relevant identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

with the established normalization.

The exact interval base-locus theorem is now structurally available:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad
\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\text{ on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0.
}
\]

This is a real advance: it says the simultaneous anisotropy base-locus cannot carry nonzero source curvature on an interval.

But Gate 2 still needs a propagation theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 mass + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{approximate base-locus on an interval with }u\text{ non-small}.
}
\]

So Gate 2 is not proved yet.

---

# 2. Missing Gate 2 step

The missing step is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{thick-set to interval propagation.}
}
\]

The desired implication is:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

and

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|
\]

should imply existence of an interval \(J\subset I\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\text{needed derivatives}\le Q^{-C'}
\]

in a form strong enough to invoke approximate interval rigidity.

The difficulty is that weighted smallness initially gives only a thick or \(u\)-weighted set, not an interval. A Remez/Bernstein/Cartan-type lemma must convert this thick-set information into interval control using finite analytic complexity:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k}.
\]

Likely derivative order remains modest, around \(k\le6\), but this has to be pinned down because \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) already contains \(\Gamma_G''\).

---

# 3. \(q_0\)-wall status

The wall is real.

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

If

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

then

\[
H\approx0.
\]

But Gate 2 can still be live at the wall. Indeed,

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

so at

\[
q_0=0
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Thus if \(u\neq0\),

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4
\]

is nonzero, even though the \(H\)-driven rows collapse.

So the hoped-for implication

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists m_\ast:\ |q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is not justified by the current formulas and is likely false without additional structure.

---

# 4. Row search status

The known projected tower has the form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

these rows all appear to vanish at

\[
q_0=0.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the projected Gram tower does not currently rescue the \(q_0\)-wall.}
}
\]

The only plausible rescue paths are:

\[
\text{raw scattering rows,}
\]

\[
\text{ambient/unprojected rows,}
\]

\[
\text{wall-leading correction rows,}
\]

or

\[
\text{a new source-robust invariant.}
\]

The target is a row/invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) satisfying

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

No such row is currently certified.

---

# 5. Nondegenerate row conversion status

In the branch

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

row conversion is structurally close.

Assume also a pointwise Gate 2 sample:

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
(\Gamma_G(m_\ast)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m_\ast)^2)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Then the leading row vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

A lower bound follows if:

1. \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}\);
2. the Gate 2 pointwise mass gives enough \(u,\Gamma\)-size;
3. correction terms satisfy

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Vector norm avoids cancellation between \(A_7\) and \(A_9\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nondegenerate row conversion is conditionally closeable.}
}
\]

The wall branch remains the serious issue.

---

# 6. Recommended next allocation

I recommend a split, not all agents on one task:

\[
\boxed{
3\text{ agents on Gate 2 propagation,}
\quad
2\text{ agents on \(q_0\)-wall row search,}
\quad
1\text{ agent on nondegenerate row conversion/canonical audit.}
}
\]

More concretely:

1. **Agent 1 — Thick-set to interval propagation.**  
   Prove the Remez/Bernstein step from Gate 2 failure to interval approximate base-locus.

2. **Agent 2 — Approximate interval base-locus rigidity.**  
   Quantify the exact interval theorem with \(\varepsilon\)-small \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2},\Gamma_G''\).

3. **Agent 3 — Gate 2 complete theorem.**  
   Combine propagation and rigidity into
   \[
   \int|u|^2\Rightarrow\int|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
   \]

4. **Agent 4 — Raw/ambient row search at \(q_0=0\).**  
   Look outside the projected tower for wall-visible rows.

5. **Agent 5 — Correction-row wall-leading audit.**  
   Determine whether lower-order corrections become leading at \(q_0=0\).

6. **Agent 6 — Nondegenerate conversion and global dependency audit.**  
   Keep the non-wall branch clean and update the global map.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Primary next proof target: Gate 2 propagation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Parallel critical target: source-robust row or \(q_0\)-wall resolution.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not return to the ordinary arithmetic inputs unless a new mechanism appears.}
}
\]

Gate 2 now looks like the most tractable open layer; the \(q_0\)-wall is the biggest downstream structural blocker.

## Assistant (2026-04-27 08:46:49)

_Thought for 5s_

## Agent 6 / F — Downstream synthesis and stop condition

The downstream layer has now split into one promising analytic theorem and one hard structural obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is plausible but still needs thick-set-to-interval propagation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }q_0\text{-wall is real and still needs a source-robust row or new wall theorem.}
}
\]

The uploaded brief identifies exactly these as the active downstream tasks. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 status

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 2 needs

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The known identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

## 1.1 Set extraction

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, one can extract a polynomial-measure set \(E\subset I\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}.
\]

This part is structurally sound.

## 1.2 Missing step: thick-set to interval

The missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{polynomial-measure approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}.
}
\]

Positive measure alone is not enough: the bad set can be dust-like. The proof needs either a genuine thickness condition or a Remez/Bernstein/Cartan lemma showing that finite-complexity functions small on a sufficiently large set become small on a real interval.

This is now the exact Gate 2 propagation bottleneck.

## 1.3 Derivative-control gap

Approximate interval rigidity needs not only

\[
|\Gamma_G|,\ |\Gamma_{G,2}|\ll1,
\]

but also control of either

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or directly

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

So the propagation package must also show that smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) on an interval implies sufficient smallness of \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\), using analytic complexity bounds.

Likely required derivative package:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6.
\]

## 1.4 Approximate interval rigidity

The exact interval theorem is:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
u\equiv0.
\]

The quantitative version is viable if the interval propagation supplies

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Then one expects

\[
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

on a shrunken interval, contradicting the retained \(u\)-mass.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is reduced to a named propagation theorem.}
}
\]

Suggested name:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation Theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 2. \(q_0\)-wall status

The wall branch is

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Known rows satisfy

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
H=0,
\]

but also

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Therefore Gate 2 can remain live:

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4,
\]

while the known \(H\)-driven projected rows vanish.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 mass does not force }|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

The \(q_0\)-wall is not a sampling artifact; it is structurally real for the currently known row architecture.

---

# 3. Source-robust row status

## 3.1 Projected tower

The known projected rows have schematic form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Since

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

these rows remain \(q_0\)-divisible.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the projected Gram tower does not rescue }q_0=0.
}
\]

## 3.2 Raw / ambient rows

Still open. The needed search is term-by-term:

\[
R_{\rm raw}|_{q_0=0,\ u\ne0}\neq0.
\]

Candidate surviving forms would look like

\[
u^p,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

without a factor of \(q_0\) or \(H\).

No such row is certified yet.

## 3.3 Correction rows

Also open. Corrections that are lower-order off-wall may become leading when \(H=0\). The audit must classify correction terms by divisibility in

\[
(q_0),\qquad (H),\qquad (q_0u^3).
\]

Needed result:

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\neq0
\quad\text{or}\quad
C_9|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\neq0,
\]

or a no-go that all correction sectors are also wall-divisible.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-robust row search is unresolved and critical.}
}
\]

Suggested named input if unresolved:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution Theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Nondegenerate row conversion

The non-wall branch is relatively clean.

Assume

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and pointwise Gate 2 mass

\[
|u(m_\ast)|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_\ast)
\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
=
c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Leading vector:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

If

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|,
\]

then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

An additional pointwise lower bound

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

may be needed unless anisotropy has a known polynomial upper bound, since the Gate 2 product lower bound alone could come from large anisotropy and small \(u\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{nondegenerate row conversion is conditionally closeable.}
}
\]

Suggested named local theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Nondegenerate Row Conversion Theorem.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Downstream named inputs now needed

The downstream layer currently requires:

## Input D1 — Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation

\[
\int|u|^2
+
\text{Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}
\Rightarrow
u\approx0,
\]

contradicting Gate 1.

## Input D2 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Either:

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}
\Rightarrow
\exists |q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

or a row/invariant satisfying

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

The first option appears unlikely from current formulas; the second is the more promising search direction.

## Input D3 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}
+
\text{Gate 2 pointwise mass}
+
\text{correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

This is mostly formal but still needs exact expansions and correction bounds.

---

I recommend:

Specifically:

## Agent 6 / F — Downstream dependency synthesis

The downstream branch is now split into two sharply defined blockers:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1: Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2: Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

The nondegenerate row-conversion branch is largely formal once Gate 2 supplies a usable point and \(q_0\) is not too small. The uploaded prompt frames this round exactly around propagation and the \(q_0\)-wall. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 status

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 2 wants

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

The relevant identities are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

## 1.1 Set extraction

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, one can extract a polynomial-measure set \(E\subset I\) with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{structural / essentially available.}}
\]

## 1.2 Thick-set-to-interval propagation

This is still the missing step.

Positive polynomial measure alone does not guarantee interval control; \(E\) can be dust-like. The needed theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-complexity functions small on a sufficiently thick bad set}
\Rightarrow
\text{small on an actual interval}.
}
\]

The required form is something like:

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C}
\quad\text{on a thick set }E
\]

\[
\Longrightarrow
\exists J\subset I:
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C'}.
\]

This likely requires either relative density on subintervals,

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C}|J|,
\]

or a Remez/Cartan-type lemma strong enough to convert global polynomial measure plus derivative complexity into interval control.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; should be named if the next attempt does not close it.}}
\]

Suggested name:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Thick-Set-to-Interval Propagation}.
}
\]

## 1.3 Derivative propagation

Approximate interval rigidity needs more than small \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\). It needs either

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A}
\]

or direct control of

\[
\sup_J|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A}.
\]

Because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

small \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone does not separate the two terms. A derivative propagation theorem must show, under finite analytic complexity, that interval smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) gives control of \(\Gamma_G''\) on a shrunken interval, or else that the combination directly forces \(q(q')^2\) small.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open sublemma within D1.}}
\]

Likely derivative package:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le6.
\]

## 1.4 Approximate interval rigidity

The exact interval theorem is available:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0.
\]

A usable approximate theorem is conditional on interval bounds:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{plausible / essentially reduced, conditional on derivative propagation.}}
\]

---

# 2. \(q_0\)-wall status

The wall is

\[
|q_0|<Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim -\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we get

\[
H=0,
\]

but

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

Therefore Gate 2 mass can be live at the wall:

\[
|u|^2\Gamma_G^2=|u|^4,
\]

while the known \(H\)-driven rows vanish.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the \(q_0\)-wall is real.}
}
\]

Gate 2 alone does not imply a \(q_0\)-nondegenerate sampling point.

---

# 3. Row search status

## 3.1 Projected tower

Known projected rows:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Because

\[
H\sim q_0u^3,
\]

the projected tower remains wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{no rescue from known projected tower.}}
\]

## 3.2 Raw / ambient rows

Still open. The target is a row or invariant \(R_{\rm rob}\) with

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Candidate leading forms would be

\[
u^p,\quad
u^p\Gamma_G,\quad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\quad
u^p(q')^a
\]

without a \(q_0\) or \(H\) factor.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{not found yet.}}
}
\]

## 3.3 Correction rows

Also open. Corrections could become leading when \(H=0\). One must inspect

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9.
\]

If

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
\]

or

\[
C_9|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

then the wall might be rescued by correction terms.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{unresolved; requires term-level expansion audit.}}
}
\]

---

# 4. Nondegenerate branch

The nondegenerate branch is:

\[
|q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q}.

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|,
\]

then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

\boxed{\text{conditionally closeable.}}
}
\]

Named theorem:

}

# 1. Gate 2 component classification

Gate 2 target:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\qquad u=q''_{\can}.

## 1.1 Set extraction

\qquad

## 1.2 Thick-set-to-interval propagation

Current missing statement:

\[
E\text{ polynomial-measure}
\Longrightarrow
\exists J\subset I:
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C'}.

\[

}
\]

## 1.3 Remez/Cartan theorem

Needed form:

\[
|f_i|\le Q^{-A}\text{ on }E
\Rightarrow
|f_i|\le Q^{-A'}\text{ on interval }J,
\]

for

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

If the effective complexity is \(O(1)\), this may close. If it is \(N\asymp R\), generic Remez loss may be

\[
Q^{O(R)},
\]

which is too expensive unless the initial smallness is much stronger.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; likely requires a tailored low-complexity/relative-density theorem.}}
\]

## 1.4 Derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\)

Approximate interval rigidity needs control of

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or directly

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

But Gate 2 failure directly controls only

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

small \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) can hide cancellation between \(2q(q')^2\) and \(-\Gamma_G''/6\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open sublemma.}}
\]

Named candidate:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}.
}
\]

## 1.5 Approximate interval rigidity

Exact interval rigidity is available:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\Rightarrow u\equiv0.
\]

Approximate version:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|+\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional/near-Green once derivative control is available.}}

Yes.

By contrast, the \(q_0\)-wall lacks a known source-robust row. If no raw/ambient/correction row survives at \(q_0=0\), the proof needs a genuinely new invariant or wall-exclusion theorem.
