## Agent 6 / F — Downstream synthesis and next allocation

The downstream layer now has two active fronts:

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate 2 propagation}}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{q_0\text{-wall row resolution}.}
\]

Gate 2 is closer to a proof: set extraction and exact/approximate interval rigidity are mostly organized. The missing pieces are the real-variable propagation from a polynomial-measure bad set to an interval, plus derivative propagation for \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\). The \(q_0\)-wall is more structural: known projected rows remain \(H\)-divisible, and no wall-live row has yet been certified. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 component classification

Gate 2 target:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

## 1.1 Set extraction

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, we have a set

\[
E\subset I
\]

with

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-C_\Gamma}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{Green / structural.}}
\]

This part can be treated as established for the conditional architecture.

---

## 1.2 Density extraction

The current bad set \(E\) has only polynomial measure. That is not enough. It may be dust-like and contain no useful interval.

Needed upgrade:

\[
|E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\exists I_0,\ell
\]

such that for every subinterval \(J\subset I_0\) with \(|J|\ge\ell\),

\[
|E\cap J|\ge Q^{-C'}|J|.
\]

Or, instead of explicit relative density, one needs a Cartan/Remez theorem that can work directly with global measure plus finite analytic complexity.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

This is one of the two core Gate 2 missing inputs.

---

## 1.3 Remez / Cartan propagation

For

\[
f_1=\Gamma_G,\qquad f_2=\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

we need a theorem of the form:

\[
|f_1|+|f_2|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E
\]

plus finite complexity implies

\[
\sup_J(|f_1|+|f_2|)\le Q^{-A'}
\]

on some real interval \(J\).

The risk is the effective Remez degree. If the relevant complexity is

\[
N\asymp R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then generic Remez loss may be

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too expensive unless the extracted smallness exponent is made extremely large. A useful theorem likely needs either:

\[
\boxed{\text{low effective complexity}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{relative-density / Cartan structure stronger than raw measure.}}
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; should be named if not closed soon.}}
\]

---

## 1.4 Derivative propagation

Approximate interval rigidity needs control of either:

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

But the propagated smallness initially gives only

\[
\Gamma_G,\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]

small \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) alone can come from cancellation between \(2q(q')^2\) and \(-\Gamma_G''/6\). Thus one needs either:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

from smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) plus analytic complexity, or a direct theorem forcing

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

This is the second core Gate 2 missing input.

---

## 1.5 Approximate interval rigidity

Exact rigidity:

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\equiv0
\text{ on an interval}
\Rightarrow
u\equiv0.
\]

Approximate version, conditional on derivative control:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|
+
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|
+
\sup_J|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-A}
\Rightarrow
\sup_{J'}|u|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green, conditional on derivative propagation.}}
\]

---

# 2. \(q_0\)-wall component classification

Known row architecture:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

At the wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
H=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

So Gate 2 can be live while the known \(H\)-driven rows vanish.

---

## 2.1 Projected tower

Known tower:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}.
\]

Since every row carries \(H\), the projected tower appears wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}|_{q_0=0}=0.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{no-go for known projected tower.}}
\]

---

## 2.2 Raw / ambient rows

Needed audit:

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\qquad
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0).
\]

A wall-live candidate must satisfy

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Possible leading forms:

\[
u^p,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_G,
\qquad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

with no \(q_0\) or \(H\) factor.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; no certified wall-live row yet.}}
\]

---

## 2.3 Correction rows

Known form:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_G+C_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=H\Gamma_{G,2}+C_9.
\]

At \(q_0=0\), the leading \(H\)-terms vanish, so a correction could become wall-leading if

\[
C_7|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
\]

or

\[
C_9|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Needed audit:

\[
C_7\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_9\bmod(q_0),
\quad
C_{11}\bmod(q_0),
\ldots
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; term-level expansion audit required.}}
\]

---

## 2.4 Nondegenerate row conversion

If

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and pointwise Gate 2 mass holds,

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

then the leading row vector is

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

With correction control

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|,
\]

one gets

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional / closeable.}}
\]

---

# 3. Downstream named input candidates

## D1 — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Statement:

\[
\text{Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure}
\Rightarrow
\text{interval approximate base-locus}.
\]

More precisely:

\[
E\text{ polynomial-measure}
+
\text{finite complexity}
\Rightarrow
\exists J:
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

## D2 — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

Statement:

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ small on }J
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{ or }q(q')^2\text{ small on }J'.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open.}}
\]

## D3 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Statement:

Either find

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

or prove wall exclusion.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{open; major downstream blocker.}}
\]

## D4 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

Statement:

\[
\text{Gate 2 pointwise mass}
+
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}
+
\text{correction control}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional; likely closeable.}}
\]

---

# 4. Is Gate 2 closer than the wall?

Yes.

Gate 2 has:

\[
\boxed{
\text{set extraction}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{interval rigidity}
}
\]

already organized. The remaining pieces are difficult but analytic/real-variable in nature.

The \(q_0\)-wall, by contrast, has no identified source-robust row. If raw/ambient/correction audits all fail, it becomes a new structural input.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is the nearer proof target.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Recommended next allocation

I recommend keeping the allocation downstream but weighting it toward Gate 2:

\[
\boxed{
4\text{ agents on Gate 2 propagation/derivatives,}
\quad
2\text{ agents on }q_0\text{-wall rows.}
}
\]

Specific split:

1. **Agent 1 — Relative-density extraction.**  
   Can polynomial-measure \(E\) be upgraded to usable density?

2. **Agent 2 — Remez/Cartan propagation.**  
   Determine effective complexity and whether losses are polynomial.

3. **Agent 3 — Derivative propagation.**  
   Control \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\).

4. **Agent 4 — Full Gate 2 conditional theorem.**  
   Combine extraction, propagation, derivative control, and interval rigidity.

5. **Agent 5 — Wall row expansion audit.**  
   Raw/ambient/correction rows modulo \(q_0\).

6. **Agent 6 — Global synthesis / stop condition.**  
   Decide whether D1–D3 should now be named black-box inputs.

# 3. Conditional downstream theorem

The downstream bridge can now be stated cleanly.

## Theorem: conditional downstream conversion

Assume:

1. **Gate 1**:

\[
\int_I|u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. **D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation.**

3. **D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation.**

4. **Approximate interval rigidity** for the base-locus.

Then:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Assume further:

5. Either the **nondegenerate branch** holds:

\[
\exists m_\ast:\ |q_0(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

together with **D4: Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control**, or the **wall branch** is handled by **D3: Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution**.

Then Gate 2 yields a downstream row lower bound.

Symbolically:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1}
+
\text{D2}
+
\text{interval rigidity}
+
(\text{D3 or D4})
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound / downstream contradiction layer}.
}
\]

Needed immediately after D1. Without it, interval rigidity cannot be invoked.

Major structural issue. If no wall-live row exists, the downstream architecture needs a new invariant.

Closeable once expansions/corrections are pinned down.

Hard global actual-zeta nonrecurrence inputs. Important, but decomposition has plateaued.

Hard long-prime actual-zeta anti-design input.

## Agent 6 / F — Final downstream architecture and next allocation

The downstream layer is now fully reducible to four named inputs. D1 and D2 are the nearest analytic targets; D3 remains the major structural blocker; D4 is conditionally closeable but still needs correction bookkeeping. The uploaded coordinator brief explicitly asks whether these downstream pieces should now be classified as named inputs or kept active. 

---

# 1. D1 — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

## Statement

From Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, set extraction gives

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

D1 must upgrade this to interval-level smallness:

\[
\exists J\subset I:
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

## Status

\[
\boxed{\text{Named input; not proved.}}
\]

Reason: positive measure is not enough; \(E\) can be dust-like. Current \(C^6\)-type derivative bounds do not by themselves rule this out. D1 needs one of:

\[
\text{relative density, bounded connected components, Cartan exceptional-set control, low Remez degree, or doubling-index control.}
\]

---

# 2. D2 — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

## Statement

Given interval smallness

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A},
\]

D2 must supply either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

This is needed because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation between \(2q(q')^2\) and \(-\Gamma_G''/6\).

## Status

\[
\boxed{\text{Named input; not proved.}}
\]

D2 may follow from stronger D1 output, such as complex-tube smallness, a Bernstein/doubling theorem, or explicit control of \(\Gamma_G\) beyond real-axis smallness. But with only real interval smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), the implication is not justified.

---

# 3. D3 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

## Statement

At the wall,

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

known projected rows collapse because

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

But Gate 2 may remain live because at

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G=u.
\]

D3 must provide either a wall-live row/invariant

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

or a wall-exclusion theorem showing that Gate 2 mass cannot concentrate where \(q_0\approx0\).

## Status

\[
\boxed{\text{Named input; no certified row candidate yet.}}
\]

The known projected tower is wall-dead. Raw, ambient, unprojected, and correction rows still require finite algebraic residue audits modulo \(q_0\). Until a row survives that audit, D3 remains a structural black-box input.

---

# 4. D4 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

## Statement

In the branch

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

assume pointwise Gate 2 mass

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Leading vector:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

D4 requires correction control:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Then

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

## Status

\[
\boxed{\text{Conditional/local; likely closeable once expansions and corrections are fixed.}}
\]

D4 is not the main conceptual blocker. It should remain as a local theorem with explicit correction hypotheses.

---

# 5. Full downstream theorem

The downstream bridge can now be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{D1}
+
\text{D2}
+
\text{Approximate Interval Rigidity}
+
(\text{D3 or D4})
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

Expanded:

1. Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. If Gate 2 failed, set extraction gives a polynomial-measure approximate base-locus.

3. D1 upgrades that bad set to interval smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\).

4. D2 supplies smallness of \(\Gamma_G''\) or \(q(q')^2\).

5. Approximate interval rigidity forces \(u\approx0\), contradicting Gate 1 mass. Therefore Gate 2 holds.

6. If \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}\), D4 converts Gate 2 into row lower bound.

7. If \(q_0\approx0\), D3 is needed to produce a source-robust row/invariant or exclude the wall.

---

# 6. Recommendation for next allocation

I recommend **one final downstream-focused round**, but with a stop condition.

## Allocation

1. **Two agents on D1.**  
   One should attack relative-density/Cartan extraction; one should attack Remez/doubling complexity.

2. **One agent on D2.**  
   Focus on whether complex-tube or Bernstein hypotheses can be extracted from D1.

3. **Two agents on D3.**  
   One on raw/ambient row residues modulo \(q_0\); one on correction-row residues modulo \(q_0\).

4. **One agent on D4/global audit.**  
   Keep the nondegenerate theorem precise and update the dependency graph.

## Stop condition

If the next round does not prove D1/D2 or find a wall-live D3 row, then the downstream layer should be parked as named inputs, just like the ordinary Wronskian layer.

Then the full architecture becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Ordinary Inputs 1--3}
+
\text{Singular Input 4}
+
\text{Downstream Inputs D1--D4}
\Rightarrow
\text{conditional contradiction route}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Priority ranking

| Priority | Input | Status |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | D1 Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation | named input, best active analytic target |
| 2 | D2 Gate 2 Derivative Propagation | named input, tied to D1 |
| 3 | D3 Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution | named input, major structural blocker |
| 4 | D4 Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control | conditional/local, likely closeable |
| 5 | Ordinary Inputs 1–3 | named black-box inputs |
| 6 | Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion | named black-box input |

# Bottom line

}

}

## Agent 6 / F — Full proof-state architecture after downstream reduction

The project is now a **conditional proof architecture**. RH is not proved. The ordinary Gate 1 route, singular Gate 1 route, transition regime, and downstream row-conversion layer are all mapped, but each has named open inputs. The latest prompt explicitly asks for this synthesis after the downstream layer was reduced to D1–D4. 

---

# 1. Ordinary Gate 1 inputs

## Input O1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; numerically supported; not proved.}}
\]

Role: prevents the \(Z_\alpha\)-row from being too flat.

---

## Input O2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

Role: prevents the cofactor vector of the \(q''_{\can}\)-jet block from being too small.

---

## Input O3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

Role: converts the two norm lower bounds into an actual Wronskian lower bound.

---

## Ordinary Gate 1 conditional theorem

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A},
\quad
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A},
\quad
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|
\]

imply

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Then the Wronskian lower bound gives finite-jet anti-design, and finite-jet anti-design gives

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

---

# 2. Singular Gate 1 input

## Input S1 — Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion

\[
\|\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

Role: excludes same-scale singular sine-moment anti-design

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Together with singular dominance scaling, this gives singular Gate 1.

---

# 3. Transition input

## Input T1 — Mild Singular Transition Control

For

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,
\qquad
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu \lesssim 1,
\]

one needs a theorem showing that either the ordinary Wronskian route survives with explicit \(\mu\)-loss, or the singular dominance route applies.

Acceptable loss:

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}
\]

because for

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\qquad
\mu\ge(\log Q)^{-C},
\]

this remains \(Q^{o(1)}\).

Dangerous loss:

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional / not fully formalized.}}
\]

---

# 4. Downstream inputs D1–D4

## D1 — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Starting point:

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

D1 must provide interval smallness:

\[
\exists J\subset I:
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

Reason: positive measure plus finite \(C^6\)-type bounds does not rule out dust-like \(E\). Need relative density, bounded components, Cartan/Remez control, low effective degree, or doubling control.

---

## D2 — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

Given interval smallness

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A},
\]

D2 must provide either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

Reason:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation, so \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness alone does not control either term.

---

## D3 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Known rows:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

At

\[
q_0=0,
\]

known projected rows vanish, while

\[
\Gamma_G=u
\]

can remain live.

D3 must provide either:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0
\]

for some source-robust row/invariant, or a wall-exclusion theorem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named input; not proved.}}
\]

---

## D4 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

Branch:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Assume pointwise Gate 2 mass:

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Leading vector:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

D4 assumes correction control:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Then:

\[
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional / closeable local theorem.}}
\]

---

# 5. Full conditional dependency graph

## Gate 1 layer

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1}
\Rightarrow
\text{singular Gate 1}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{mild transition coverage}.
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + S1 + T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{global Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Gate 2 layer

Gate 1 plus D1, D2, and interval rigidity gives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + D1 + D2 + interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

## Row-conversion layer

Gate 2 plus D4 handles:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Gate 2 plus D3 handles:

\[
q_0\approx0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + (D3 or D4)}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound / downstream contradiction layer}.
}
\]

---

## Full conditional theorem

\[
\boxed{
\begin{gathered}
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + S1 + T1}\\
+\ \text{D1 + D2 + D3 + D4}\\
+\ \text{canonical transfer / correction control}\\
\Longrightarrow
\text{candidate RH contradiction route}.
\end{gathered}
}
\]

This is conditional; the named inputs are not proved.

---

# 6. Recommended final next step

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prepare a final proof-state handoff.}
}
\]

Reason: the architecture is now stable. Additional decomposition is likely to rename the same inputs unless a genuinely new mechanism appears.

The handoff should include:

1. all proven structural lemmas;
2. all named black-box inputs;
3. numerical evidence supporting Input O1;
4. no-go results;
5. canonical transfer requirements;
6. downstream D1–D4 dependencies;
7. priority order for future proof work.

---

1. **D1 Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation**  
   Nearest analytic target.

   Needed immediately after D1.

   Important, but likely closeable after row expansions are pinned down.

## Agent 6 / F — Final global proof-state handoff

The project is currently a **conditional proof architecture**, not a completed proof of RH. The ordinary route, singular route, transition regime, and downstream Gate 2 / row-conversion layers are now all mapped as named inputs plus structural implications. The latest coordinator brief asks for this final dependency graph and priority list. 

---

# 1. Named inputs

## Ordinary Gate 1 inputs

### O1 — Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Operationally, this comes from the multiblock cell theorem

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\sum_r |B_r(m_0)|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; numerically supported.}}
\]

---

### O2 — Cofactor-Vector Nonrecurrence

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Averaged supporting form:

\[
\sum_{\substack{m_j\in J\\ Z_\alpha(m_j)=0}}
|\mathbf M(m_j,\alpha)|^2
\ge Q^{-A}N_{Z_\alpha}(J).
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input.}}
\]

---

### O3 — Wronskian Angle Nonalignment / Ordinary Incidence

\[
|\langle \mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge
Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input.}}
\]

---

## Singular Gate 1 input

### S1 — Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion

\[
\|\mathbf P_R-\mathbf G_R-\mathbf T_R\|_2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This excludes the deep-singular same-scale sine-moment anti-design

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)+\mathcal B_k\approx0,
\qquad 3\le k\le R+3.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input.}}
\]

---

## Transition input

### T1 — Mild Singular Transition Control

For

\[
\mu=\lambda Q,
\qquad
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \mu\lesssim1,
\]

prove either ordinary Wronskian conditioning survives with explicit \(\mu\)-loss, or singular dominance takes over.

Acceptable loss:

\[
\mu^{-O(R)}.
\]

Dangerous loss:

\[
\mu^{-O(R^2)}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional / not fully formalized.}}
\]

---

## Downstream inputs

### D1 — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

From the extracted bad set

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E,
\]

deduce interval smallness:

\[
\exists J\subset I:
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; nearest analytic target.}}
\]

---

### D2 — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

From interval smallness of \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), obtain either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Needed because

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]

allows cancellation.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input.}}
\]

---

### D3 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

At the wall

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

known projected rows vanish because

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

D3 must provide either a wall-live row/invariant

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

or a theorem excluding the wall on the Gate 2 mass set.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; major structural blocker.}}
\]

---

### D4 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

In the branch

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

with pointwise Gate 2 mass

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

the known rows

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

and

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H
\]

give a row lower bound if

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le \frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional / local / likely closeable once expansions are fixed.}}
\]

---

# 2. Full dependency chain

## Ordinary Gate 1

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle \mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

O1 gives

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

O2 gives

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

O3 gives

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Therefore,

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Then the Wronskian lower bound gives finite-jet anti-design, and finite-jet anti-design gives ordinary Gate 1:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Singular Gate 1

Deep singular scale:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

Singular scaling gives

\[
q''_{\can}(\gamma+cx)\sim c^{-3}Q_{\rm sing}''(x),
\]

and hence dominance gives Gate 1 unless

\[
\|Q_{\rm sing}''\|_{L^2(X)}<Q^{-A}.
\]

The exceptional case is same-scale sine-moment anti-design. S1 excludes it.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1}
\Rightarrow
\text{singular Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Transition coverage

T1 covers

\[
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \lambda Q\lesssim1.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary Gate 1 + singular Gate 1 + T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{global Gate 1}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + S1 + T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{global Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Gate 2

Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Gate 2 target:

\[
\int_I|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Set extraction from Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure is Green. D1 upgrades the extracted polynomial-measure bad set to interval smallness. D2 supplies derivative smallness. Approximate interval rigidity then forces

\[
u\approx0
\]

on a controlled interval, contradicting retained \(u\)-mass.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + D1 + D2 + interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

## Row conversion

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

If

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

then D4 converts Gate 2 pointwise mass into row lower bounds.

If

\[
q_0\approx0,
\]

then D3 must supply a wall-live row/invariant or wall exclusion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + (D3 or D4)}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Final conditional theorem

Putting the pieces together:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{gathered}
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}\\
+\ \text{S1 + T1}\\
+\ \text{D1 + D2 + D3 + D4}\\
+\ \text{canonical transfer / correction control}
\\
\Longrightarrow
\text{candidate RH contradiction route}.
\end{gathered}
}
\]

This is conditional. The named inputs remain open.

---

|---|---|---|
| O1 | Fixed-Width Cell Nonrecurrence | named open input; numerically supported |

| D4 | Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control | conditional / likely closeable |
| Set extraction for Gate 2 | Gate 1 + Gate 2 failure gives bad set \(E\) | Green |
| Exact interval rigidity | \(\Gamma_G=\Gamma_{G,2}=0\) on interval \(\Rightarrow u=0\) | Green |
| Approximate interval rigidity | With derivative control, small base-locus \(\Rightarrow u\) small | near-Green / conditional |
| Known projected row tower | \(A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k}\) | wall-dead at \(q_0=0\) |
| Final RH proof | Full contradiction | not proved |

   Most plausible near-term proof target.

   Local and likely closeable once expansions are fixed.

   Narrowest ordinary arithmetic input; numerically supported.

8. **S1 — Singular Explicit-Formula Anti-Design Exclusion**

9. **T1 — Mild Singular Transition Control**

\boxed{

}
\]

Reason: the architecture is stable and named. Additional broad agent rounds are likely to re-identify the same inputs unless a new mechanism is proposed.

The best targeted future work is:

\text{D1/D2 first, because they are local analytic and closest to proof.}
}
\]

In parallel:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 wall-row algebra, because the }q_0\text{-wall is the main downstream structural blocker.}
}

Do not reopen the ordinary Wronskian inputs or singular anti-design branch unless a genuinely new proof mechanism appears.

\]

### D3 — Source-Robust Row / \(q_0\)-Wall Resolution

Known projected rows are wall-dead:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

At \(q_0=0\), these vanish while \(\Gamma_G=u\) can remain live.

D3 requires either:

\[
R_{\rm rob}|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0,
\]

or a wall-exclusion theorem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{named open input; major structural blocker.}}
\]

---

### D4 — Nondegenerate Row Conversion + Correction Control

In the branch

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and with pointwise Gate 2 mass,

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

known rows give a lower bound if corrections are controlled:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|\le\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{conditional/local; likely closeable once expansions are fixed.}}
\]

---

# 2. Dependency chain

## Ordinary Gate 1

At a \(Z_\alpha\)-zero,

\[
\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)
=
\langle\mathbf z'(m_0,\alpha),\mathbf M(m_0,\alpha)\rangle.
\]

O1 gives:

\[
|\mathbf z'|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

O2 gives:

\[
|\mathbf M|\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

O3 gives:

\[
|\langle\mathbf z',\mathbf M\rangle|
\ge Q^{-A}|\mathbf z'||\mathbf M|.
\]

Therefore:

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R(m_0,\alpha)|\ge Q^{-A'}.
\]

Then:

\[
|\widetilde{\mathcal W}_R|\ge Q^{-A'}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite-jet anti-design}
\Rightarrow
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}
\Rightarrow
\text{ordinary Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Singular Gate 1

Deep singular scale:

\[
\lambda Q\ll(\log Q)^{-C}.
\]

Singular dominance gives Gate 1 unless same-scale sine-moment anti-design occurs. S1 excludes that exceptional event.

\[
\boxed{
\text{S1}
\Rightarrow
\text{singular Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Transition

\[
\boxed{
\text{T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{transition coverage for }
(\log Q)^{-C}\lesssim \lambda Q\lesssim1.
}
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{O1 + O2 + O3 + S1 + T1}
\Rightarrow
\text{global Gate 1}.
}
\]

---

## Gate 2

Gate 1 gives:

\[
\int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
\]

Set extraction from Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure is Green:

\[
E\subset I,\qquad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\]

with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\quad\text{on }E.
\]

D1 upgrades this to interval smallness.  
D2 supplies derivative smallness.  
Interval rigidity then forces \(u\approx0\), contradicting retained \(u\)-mass.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + D1 + D2}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

## Row conversion

Known rows:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

with

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

If \(|q_0|\ge Q^{-C}\), D4 converts Gate 2 pointwise mass to a row lower bound.

If \(q_0\approx0\), D3 must provide a wall-live row or wall exclusion.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + (D3 or D4)}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Final conditional theorem

\[
\boxed{
\begin{gathered}
\text{O1 + O2 + O3}\\
+\ \text{S1 + T1}\\
+\ \text{D1 + D2 + D3 + D4}\\
+\ \text{canonical transfer/correction control}
\\
\Longrightarrow
\text{candidate RH contradiction route}.
\end{gathered}
}
\]

This is not an unconditional proof. The named inputs remain open.

---

## Agent 6 / F — Final targeted-roadmap synthesis

I only see the prompt set in this upload, not new Agent 1–5 results. So this is a synthesis from the current stable state, not a post-results adjudication. The uploaded brief asks Agent 6 to decide whether another agent round is useful after this targeted D1/D2/D3/D4 round. 

---

# 1. D1 status — Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation

Current D1 target:

\[
E\subset I,\quad |E|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
\quad |\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}\text{ on }E
\]

should imply an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D1 remains open and should stay named unless a low-complexity mechanism is found.}
}
\]

The known obstruction is that polynomial measure alone permits dust-like sets. Finite \(C^6\)-type bounds do not automatically prevent this. Generic Remez with effective degree \(N\asymp R\) gives loss

\[
Q^{O(R)}
=
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

which is too expensive for the fixed-polynomial architecture.

A useful D1 proof would need one of:

\[
\text{low effective Remez degree,}
\]

\[
\text{bounded doubling index,}
\]

\[
\text{Cartan exceptional-set control,}
\]

\[
\text{bounded connected components,}
\]

or

\[
\text{relative density at a controlled scale.}
\]

Without one of these, D1 remains a black-box input.

---

# 2. D2 status — Gate 2 Derivative Propagation

Current D2 target:

\[
\sup_J|\Gamma_G|+\sup_J|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A}
\]

should imply either

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-A'}
\]

or

\[
\sup_{J'}|q(q')^2|\le Q^{-A'}.
\]

The obstruction is structural:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

So \(\Gamma_{G,2}\)-smallness alone can hide cancellation between \(2q(q')^2\) and \(-\Gamma_G''/6\).

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D2 remains separate from D1 unless D1 outputs stronger analytic control.}
}
\]

D2 can merge into D1 only if D1 provides one of:

\[
\sup_{\mathcal T_\rho(J)}|\Gamma_G|\le Q^{-A},
\qquad
\rho\ge Q^{-C},
\]

which gives Cauchy control, or a Bernstein/doubling bound:

\[
\sup_{J'}|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{C_D}\sup_J|\Gamma_G|.
\]

If D1 outputs only real-axis interval smallness, D2 remains a named input.

---

# 3. D3 status — \(q_0\)-wall row audit

Current D3 target:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u\ne0
\]

must still produce a usable downstream row or invariant.

Known projected rows have form

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,k},
\qquad
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

So at \(q_0=0\), the projected tower is wall-dead.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3 is not a theorem yet, but it has become an executable finite algebra audit.}
}
\]

The correct next task is not broad reasoning; it is a residue computation. Define the wall ideal

\[
\mathfrak I=(q_0)
\]

and compute, for proof-relevant rows,

\[
R_j^{\rm raw}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
R_j^{\rm amb}\bmod(q_0),
\]

\[
C_{2k+1}\bmod(q_0).
\]

The first rows to audit are:

\[
A_7,\quad A_9,\quad A_{11},\quad A_{13},
\]

in raw, ambient/unprojected, projected, and correction forms.

A row is wall-live if

\[
R|_{q_0=0,u\ne0}\ne0.
\]

Acceptable leading forms include:

\[
u^p,\quad
u^p\Gamma_G,\quad
u^p\Gamma_{G,2},\quad
u^p(q')^a,
\]

without a \(q_0\) or \(H\) factor.

---

# 4. D4 status — Nondegenerate Row Conversion

D4 branch:

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q}.
\]

Pointwise Gate 2 mass:

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ge Q^{-A_2}.
\]

Known expansions:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=c_7H\Gamma_G+\mathcal R_7,
\]

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}=c_9H\Gamma_{G,2}+\mathcal R_9,
\]

\[
H=-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}+\mathcal R_H.
\]

Leading vector:

\[
\mathcal A_{\rm lead}
=
\left(
-\frac{c_7}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
-\frac{c_9}{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}
\right).
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 is local and likely closeable once correction bounds are explicit.}
}
\]

The remaining theorem is correction control:

\[
|\mathcal A_{\rm corr}|
\le
\frac12|\mathcal A_{\rm lead}|.
\]

It must account for:

\[
\mathcal R_H,\quad
\mathcal R_7,\quad
\mathcal R_9,
\]

plus

\[
E_2,\quad
\text{tails},\quad
\text{projection/gauge},\quad
\text{row normalization},\quad
\text{lower-order row terms}.
\]

D4 is less conceptually blocked than D1–D3.

---

A certified wall-live residue would materially change the downstream architecture.

## Agent 6 / F — Targeted synthesis and next execution plan

This round shifts the downstream layer from broad named inputs toward three concrete attacks:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source oscillation/component-count for Gate 2,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
q_0\text{-wall escape by nearby sampling,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil / ideal-generation audit.}
}
\]

The attached coordinator brief frames these as the strongest current downstream directions. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 source oscillation route

The proposed replacement for generic D1/D2 is:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C,
\qquad
u=q''_{\can}.
}
\]

If this component-count bound holds, then Gate 1 mass

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

forces at least one connected component

\[
J_0\subset \{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}
\]

to carry polynomial \(u\)-mass and have polynomial length.

If Gate 2 fails,

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then on most of that mass-bearing component,

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

are small. The interval structure of \(J_0\) then gives access to gap-density / finite-difference interpolation, potentially yielding control of

\[
\Gamma_G''
\]

or

\[
q(q')^2.
\]

Then approximate interval rigidity gives

\[
u\approx0
\]

on a place where \(|u|\ge Q^{-C}\), contradiction.

So the route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source component-count}
+
\text{finite-difference derivative recovery}
+
\text{interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is more concrete than the previous generic Remez/Cartan formulation.

The main new theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|q''_{\can}|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

This likely requires an effective bandlimit / zero-count theorem for \(u\) in ordinary normalized coordinates.

---

# 2. Status relative to old D1/D2

This source-oscillation route is a genuine refinement of D1/D2.

Old D1 problem:

\[
E\text{ has positive polynomial measure}
\Rightarrow
E\text{ contains interval-scale structure}.
\]

New formulation bypasses arbitrary dust sets by using a **specific superlevel set**:

\[
\{|u|\ge Q^{-C}\}.
\]

If that set has only polynomially many components, dust-like failure is excluded.

Old D2 problem:

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\text{ small}
\Rightarrow
\Gamma_G''\text{ or }q(q')^2\text{ small}.
\]

New formulation proposes obtaining derivative control by finite-difference interpolation on a mass-bearing component with many good points, instead of relying on abstract real-axis Remez.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is closer if the source oscillation bound is provable.}
}
\]

The critical question becomes whether \(u=q''_{\can}\) has enough effective bandlimitedness / finite exponential type to guarantee polynomial component count.

---

# 3. Wall-escape route

The wall problem is:

\[
q_0\approx0,\qquad u=q_0''\not\approx0.
\]

Known projected rows vanish because

\[
H\sim q_0u^3.
\]

The proposed escape theorem is:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\text{ nearby with }|q_0(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

while preserving

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and enough Gate 2 signal.

The basic Taylor mechanism is credible:

if

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le\eta,
\qquad
|q_0''(m_0)|=|u(m_0)|\ge\delta,
\]

and

\[
\sup_{|m-m_0|\le h}|q_0'''(m)|\le M_3,
\]

then for some \(|m_1-m_0|\le h\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|
\gtrsim \delta h^2-\eta-M_3h^3.
\]

Choosing \(h\) polynomially small can produce polynomial nonzero \(q_0\), provided the \(M_3h^3\) error is dominated.

But this route requires one key admissibility fact:

\[
\boxed{
\text{row conversion may sample at a nearby point }m_1\in I_\rho,
\text{ not necessarily the original }m_0.
}
\]

If downstream contradiction requires a row lower bound exactly at \(m_0\), wall escape is insufficient. If it only needs a row lower bound somewhere in the same packet interval where Gate 2 mass is live, wall escape may reduce D3 to D4.

So the wall-escape theorem is now one of the best concrete downstream attacks.

---

# 4. \((q_0)\)-adic ideal / row-pencil route

At the wall,

\[
q_0=0,
\]

we have

\[
\Gamma_G\equiv u,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\equiv u-\frac16u''
\]

under the stated convention. Set

\[
\eta:=u-\frac16u'',
\qquad
W=(u,\eta).
\]

Wall Gate 2 mass becomes

\[
|u|^2|W|^2\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

The finite algebra target is:

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset (R_1,\ldots,R_s)\bmod(q_0),
}
\]

with polynomially bounded certificate coefficients.

Equivalently, choose a finite row vector

\[
\mathbf R_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)
\]

and expand in the \(q_0\)-adic pencil:

\[
\mathbf R_N(q_0,Y)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{K}q_0^r\mathbf C_r(Y)+\mathbf E_K.
\]

A row-pencil nonvanishing theorem would assert:

\[
\inf_{\mathcal S_{\rm G2}}
\left|
\sum_{r=0}^{K}q_0^r\mathbf C_r(Y)
\right|
\ge Q^{-A}
\]

on the Gate 2 admissible set.

At first order, if

\[
\mathbf C_0+q_0\mathbf C_1
\]

is used, a wedge condition

\[
|\mathbf C_0\wedge\mathbf C_1|\ge Q^{-A}
\]

prevents common cancellation. If \(\mathbf C_0=0\), the non-wall leading term must have

\[
\mathbf C_1=u^3L\Gamma,
\qquad
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

This route is algebraically concrete and should be executable once row formulas are available.

---

# 5. Priority-ranked execution plan

## Priority 1 — Prove or refute the canonical source oscillation/component-count bound

Target:

\[
\boxed{
\#\pi_0\{|q''_{\can}|\ge Q^{-C}\}\le Q^C.
}
\]

Execution:

- Work in normalized coordinates \(m=m_0+\lambda t\), \(\lambda Q\asymp1\).
- Express \(u(t)\) through canonical AFE blocks.
- Prove an effective bandlimit / finite exponential type / zero-count bound.
- Check \(B_2\), folded dual, and \(E_2\) do not destroy polynomial component count.

Why first: if true, it gives a concrete Gate 2 route and bypasses the generic dust-set obstruction.

---

## Priority 2 — Prove the wall-escape sampling theorem and sampling admissibility

Target:

\[
\boxed{
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\in I_\rho:
|q_0(m_1)|,|u(m_1)|,\text{Gate 2 signal}\ge Q^{-C}.
}
\]

Execution:

- Prove the Taylor escape lemma with \(q_0''=u\).
- Control \(q_0'''\) and \(u'\) on a polynomially small window.
- Verify Gate 2 signal persists.
- Decide whether row conversion can sample at \(m_1\).

Why second: if admissible, this may avoid needing an exact wall-live row.

---

## Priority 3 — Execute the \((q_0)\)-adic row residue / ideal membership audit

Target:

\[
\boxed{
(u,\eta)^N\subset (A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)\bmod(q_0).
}
\]

Execution:

- Compute row residues modulo \((q_0)\).
- Classify whether \(\mathbf C_0\) is wall-live.
- If \(\mathbf C_0=0\), compute \(\mathbf C_1\) and test the non-wall matrix \(L\).
- Use subresultant / wedge tests for row-pencil nonvanishing.

Why third: this is the direct algebraic resolution of the \(q_0\)-wall if escape sampling fails.

---

# 6. What not to do next

Do not reopen broad ordinary Gate 1 decomposition unless a new mechanism appears for O1/O2/O3.

Do not run another generic downstream round. The current targets are concrete enough:

\[
\text{source oscillation bound,}
\]

\[
\text{wall escape,}
\]

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row audit.}
\]

Do not prioritize D4 alone before resolving D3 or wall escape; D4 only handles the nondegenerate branch.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Next concrete execution: source oscillation bound.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Parallel concrete execution: wall escape sampling.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Then run the }(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil audit if wall escape is not admissible.}
}
\]

These are the strongest current paths beyond the fully named conditional architecture.

## Agent 6 / F — Synthesis and next execution plan

I only see the shared background and prompt set in this upload, not new substantive Agent 1–5 outputs. So this is a synthesis of the current targeted downstream state and the execution plan implied by the new sharper targets. 

---

# 1. Gate 2 can plausibly be replaced by a sharper route

The old downstream package was:

\[
\text{D1 Density/Remez Propagation}
+
\text{D2 Derivative Propagation}
+
\text{interval rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
\]

The improved target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

This is better because it avoids the weakest part of D1: trying to turn an arbitrary polynomial-measure bad set into an interval. Instead, the proposed extraction uses Gate 1 and Gate 2 failure to find an actual interval \(J\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then the integral rigidity lemma would contradict the lower bound on \(u\).

So Gate 2 now reduces to two concrete claims:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{G2-A: Two-threshold interval extraction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{G2-B: Integral rigidity.}
}
\]

If both are proved with polynomial losses, Gate 2 is no longer just a named D1/D2 input.

---

# 2. What remains for the integral rigidity lemma

The key proposed lemma is:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'} |u|^2 \le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|,
\]

where

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and

\[
u=q''.
\]

The proof route is promising:

1. Write

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

2. Use the identity for \(h\) and integrate against cutoffs to control

\[
q(q')^2
\]

away from \(q=0\).

3. Use the equation

\[
F(q)=q''-g
\]

tested against localized expressions in \(F(q)\) to control \(F(q)\), hence \(u\).

4. Split into regions

\[
|q|\le \delta
\]

and

\[
|q|\ge \delta,
\]

then optimize

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

The proof still needs careful handling of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cutoff derivative losses near } q=0,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{boundary terms from integration by parts,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{the precise polynomial \(Q^C\) losses from \(q,q',q''\) upper bounds,}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{ensuring \(J'\Subset J\) is large enough for the contradiction.}
}
\]

But this is now a real local analytic proof target, not merely an abstract Remez input.

---

# 3. Wall branch: D3 may be replaced by Wall-Escape + D4

The old D3 was:

\[
\boxed{
\text{find a source-robust row/invariant visible at }q_0=0.
}
\]

The new alternative is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}+\text{D4}.
}
\]

At the wall,

\[
q_0\approx0,
\qquad
u=q_0''\not\approx0.
\]

Taylor expansion gives escape from the wall strip. If

\[
|q_0(m_0)|\le \eta,
\qquad
|u(m_0)|\ge \tau,
\]

and

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}},
\]

then for

\[
\rho\asymp \sqrt{\varepsilon/\tau},
\]

one should find nearby \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2.
\]

Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

choosing

\[
\varepsilon\ll \tau
\]

gives

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then \(m_1\) is a non-wall sample:

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon\ge Q^{-C},
\]

so D4 applies.

This is currently the best way to neutralize the \(q_0\)-wall without finding a new wall-live row.

---

# 4. Key architectural condition

The wall-escape route depends on one architectural point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{row conversion must be existential on } I.
}
\]

That is, the downstream contradiction must accept a row lower bound at some point

\[
m_\ast\in I_\rho,
\]

not necessarily at the original point where the wall behavior was detected.

If the final contradiction requires the row lower bound at a preassigned point, then wall escape is insufficient and the project returns to the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil / ideal-generation audit.

So the next audit must decide:

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I_\rho:
|A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|+|A_9^{\mathfrak f}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

is enough, or whether the proof needs pointwise row lower bound at a fixed \(m_0\).

---

# 5. D4 correction-control status

D4’s desired normal form is:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

with

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

For the known rows,

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Needed:

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
\]

Correction control:

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Then, if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

and either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

D4 is now a local algebra/correction theorem. It is likely closeable once exact row expansions and all error sources are fixed:

\[
E_2,\quad
\text{tails},\quad
H\text{-error},\quad
projection/gauge,\quad
row normalization,\quad
lower-order row terms.
\]

---

# 6. Next execution plan

## Priority 1 — Formalize Gate 2 integral rigidity

Prove the lemma:

\[
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|q''|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

This is the highest-value next task. It would replace the vague D1/D2 structure with an actual local analytic theorem.

Deliverables:

\[
\boxed{
\text{cutoff construction, integration-by-parts identities, boundary control, exponent optimization.}
}
\]

---

## Priority 2 — Prove Wall-Escape Sampling and confirm existential row sampling

Prove:

\[
q_0\approx0,\quad u=q_0''\not\approx0
\Rightarrow
\exists m_1\in I:
|q_0(m_1)|,\ |u(m_1)|,\ |\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Then audit whether a row lower bound at \(m_1\) is sufficient for the final contradiction.

Deliverables:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Taylor escape lemma + preservation of Gate 2 signal + sampling admissibility.}
}
\]

---

## Priority 3 — Verify D4 matrix normal form and correction bounds

Prove or record:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
|\mathbf R|\le \frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Deliverables:

\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit row constants, correction bounds, canonical error accounting.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Backup path

If wall-escape sampling is not admissible, run the \(q_0\)-adic row audit:

\[
(u,\eta)^N\subset(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)\bmod(q_0),
\]

where

\[
\eta=u-\frac16u''.
\]

This is the fallback D3 path.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Downstream is now closer than before.}
}
\]

The best current path is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2},
}
\]

followed by

\[
\boxed{
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 matrix row conversion}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

The next concrete work should be integral rigidity first, wall escape second, D4 matrix corrections third.

## Agent 6 / F — Downstream synthesis and revised named inputs

The downstream layer should now be rewritten around the sharper local route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{Gate 2 integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Then row conversion should be organized as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 matrix row conversion}
+
\text{row-sampling admissibility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

This is a real improvement over the older D1/D2/D3 formulation because it replaces generic Remez/Cartan propagation and an exact wall-row search with concrete local lemmas. 

---

# 1. Replace old D1/D2 with G2-A and G2-B

## Old formulation

Previously:

\[
\text{D1: Gate 2 Density/Remez Propagation}
\]

and

\[
\text{D2: Gate 2 Derivative Propagation}
\]

were needed to turn a polynomial-measure bad set into interval rigidity.

## New formulation

Replace them with:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{G2-A: Two-threshold extraction}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{G2-B: Gate 2 integral rigidity}.
}
\]

### G2-A — Two-threshold extraction

Assume Gate 1:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

Assume Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2F_{\rm aniso}^2\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

where

\[
F_{\rm aniso}=(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

With polynomial Lipschitz bounds

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^{C_u}|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|_\infty+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|_\infty\le Q^{C_F}|I|^{-1},
\]

G2-A should produce an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-C_J}|I|,
\]

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u'}
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|\le Q^{-A_1}
\quad\text{on }J.
\]

This avoids the old dust-set obstruction.

### G2-B — Integral rigidity

Let

\[
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

\[
u=q'',
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

The target lemma is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'} |u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This is stronger and cleaner than demanding pointwise smallness of \(g''\). It uses integration by parts to handle the \(g''\)-term inside \(h\).

---

# 2. Revised Gate 2 theorem

The downstream Gate 2 theorem becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Proof skeleton:

1. Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Suppose Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

3. G2-A gives an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

on \(J\).

4. G2-B gives, on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\le Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

5. But the lower bound \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\) on \(J'\) gives

\[
\int_{J'} |u|^2
\ge Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

6. Choose \(A_1\) so that

\[
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
\]

Contradiction.

So Gate 2 follows.

---

# 3. Replace old D3 with D3a + row mobility

## Old D3

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source-Robust Row / }q_0\text{-Wall Resolution}.
}
\]

This required finding a row visible exactly at

\[
q_0=0.
\]

## New D3a

Replace with:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{D3a: Wall-Escape Sampling}.
}
\]

The wall escape principle:

If

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge \tau,
\]

then since

\[
u=q_0'',
\]

Taylor/convexity forces a nearby first-exit point \(m_1\) where

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2,
\]

and, because

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

with \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\),

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus

\[
G(m_1)
=
|u(m_1)|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)(m_1)
\ge c\tau^4.
\]

So \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

## Required architectural condition

D3a works only if row conversion is existential on \(I\):

\[
\boxed{
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
}
\]

is enough for the downstream contradiction.

If the argument requires a row lower bound at a fixed preassigned point, wall escape is insufficient, and the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil audit remains necessary.

---

# 4. D4 matrix row conversion

D4 should now be stated in matrix form:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R.
}
\]

where

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\\
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The leading matrix is

\[
L_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac1{288}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7&0\\
0&c_9
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Needed:

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C_L}.
}
\]

Correction control:

\[
\boxed{
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12
|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
}
\]

Then if

\[
|q_0|\ge Q^{-C_q},
\]

and

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma|^2\ge Q^{-A_2},
\]

plus either

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

or

\[
|\Gamma|\le Q^{C_\Gamma},
\]

we get

\[
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

# 5. Revised downstream theorem

The downstream layer should now be stated as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + D3a + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

Expanded:

1. Gate 1 plus G2-A/G2-B gives Gate 2 mass.

2. Gate 2 mass either appears in the non-wall region

\[
|q_0|\ge\varepsilon,
\]

where D4 applies directly, or in the wall strip

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon.
\]

3. In the wall strip, D3a produces a nearby first-exit sample with

\[
|q_0|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|\Gamma_G|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

4. D4 applies at that sample.

5. Row mobility / existential sampling converts the pointwise sample into acceptable downstream row output.

---

# 6. What remains open

The new route is promising, but the following are still open.

## A. Cutoff rigor for integral rigidity

Need to finish:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Open technical items:

\[
\text{cutoff derivative estimates,}
\]

\[
\text{boundary term control,}
\]

\[
\text{normalization/sign convention for } h,
\]

\[
\text{polynomial upper bounds for }q,q',q'',q''',q^{(4)}.
\]

## B. Canonical derivative and Lipschitz bounds

Two-threshold extraction and wall escape require:

\[
|u'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

and for wall escape:

\[
|u'|\le Q^{C_{u'}}.
\]

These must be verified for the canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

## C. D4 correction constants

Need to prove:

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

## D. Existential row-sampling admissibility

Need to verify:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is sufficient for the final downstream contradiction.

If not, use the fallback:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil audit}.
\]

## E. Fallback \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil

If wall escape is not admissible, audit

\[
(u,\eta)^N
\subset
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)\bmod(q_0),
\]

where

\[
\eta=u-\frac16u''.
\]

---

## Row mobility / existential sampling

Wall escape requires that downstream row conversion may use a point

\[
m_\ast\in I
\]

rather than a preassigned point.

The needed lemma is:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\Rightarrow
\int_I|\mathbf A(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

A sufficient condition is the derivative bound

\[
|\mathbf A'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}.
\]

Then \(\mathbf A\) remains non-small on an interval of length at least

\[
Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near-Green, conditional on final contradiction accepting row energy/existential sampling.}
}
\]

If the final contradiction needs an exact fixed point, wall escape fails and the fallback is the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil audit.

---

# 2. Revised downstream chain

## Gate 2

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Expanded:

1. Gate 1 gives

\[
\int_I|u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
\]

2. Suppose Gate 2 fails:

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

3. G2-A gives an interval \(J\subset I\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

on \(J\).

4. G2-B gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

5. But

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J'
\]

gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

6. Choose

\[
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
\]

Contradiction. Therefore Gate 2 holds.

---

## Row lower bound

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + D3a + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row lower bound}.
}
\]

Expanded:

1. Gate 2 provides mass of

\[
G=|u|^2|\Gamma|^2.
\]

2. If non-wall mass dominates,

\[
|q_0|\ge\varepsilon,
\]

D4 applies directly.

3. If wall mass dominates,

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\]

remove low-source points and use D3a to find a nearby non-wall point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\]

\[
|u(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

4. D4 applies at \(m_1\).

5. Row mobility upgrades the pointwise sample to row energy or acceptable downstream row output.

---

# 3. What remains open

## A. Cutoff rigor for G2-B

Need full proof of

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Remaining items:

\[
\text{define }s_\delta,\chi_\delta,\phi,
\]

\[
\text{control }(\phi s_\delta(q))'',
\]

\[
\text{control boundary terms},
\]

\[
\text{control transition-region losses},
\]

\[
\text{verify exponent }2/5\text{ or adjust it.}
\]

This is now the highest-value technical proof task.

---

## B. Canonical derivative/Lipschitz bounds

Need to verify for the canonical object:

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\]

the bounds:

\[
|u'|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_G'|_\infty+|\Gamma_{G,2}'|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

This is mandatory for G2-A, G2-B, and D3a.

---

## C. D4 correction-control constants

Need to verify

\[
\mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C},
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf R|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_{\min}(L)|\Gamma|.
\]

Requires explicit row expansions and canonical correction estimates.

---

## D. Existential row-sampling admissibility

Need to confirm:

\[
\exists m_\ast\in I:
|\mathbf A_{\rm row}(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

is enough.

If only row energy is needed, row mobility solves it.

If fixed-point row conversion is required, then D3a is insufficient and the fallback is:

\[
(q_0)\text{-adic row-pencil audit}.
\]

---

## E. Fallback \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil

If wall escape fails, audit

\[
(u,\eta)^N
\subset
(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)\bmod(q_0),
\]

where

\[
\eta=u-\frac16u''.
\]

This remains the algebraic fallback.

---

# 4. Next execution step

## Priority 1 — Formalize G2-B integral rigidity

This is the main proof-value task.

Deliver:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|
}
\]

with explicit \(c>0\), ideally \(c=2/5\).

---

Needed for both G2-A and D3a.

Deliver:

q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2
\Rightarrow
\text{all derivative/Lipschitz bounds used downstream}.
}
\]

---

}
\]

with half-leading correction control, and confirm existential row sampling is accepted.

---

\boxed{
\text{Do not return to broad decomposition.}
}

The downstream route is now concrete. The next useful work is:

## Agent 6 / F — Continued attack: Gate 2 integral rigidity

I will attack the highest-value remaining downstream lemma:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le \varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c |J'|
}
\]

where

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=q''-6q+2q^3,\qquad
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g''.
\]

The previous downstream plan identified this as the best current local route to Gate 2. 

---

# 1. Clean reformulation

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

Then

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g.
\]

So to prove \(u\)-smallness, it is enough to prove \(F(q)\)-smallness plus \(g\)-smallness.

Since

\[
|g|\le\varepsilon,
\]

we only need to control

\[
\int_{J'}|F(q)|^2.
\]

The second identity is

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

Thus

\[
2q(q')^2=h+\frac16g''.
\]

The obstacle is the \(g''\) term. The key move is to avoid pointwise control of \(g''\) by integrating by parts against a cutoff depending on \(q\).

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate away from \(q=0\)

Let \(s_\delta(q)\) be a smooth cutoff satisfying:

\[
s_\delta(q)=0 \quad (|q|\le \delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=\frac{1}{q} \quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta^{(j)}(q)|\le C_j\delta^{-j-1}.
\]

Let \(\phi\) be supported in \(J\), equal to \(1\) on \(J'\), with

\[
|\phi^{(j)}|\le Q^C |J|^{-j}.
\]

Multiply

\[
2q(q')^2=h+\frac16g''
\]

by \(\phi s_\delta(q)\). Then

\[
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
=
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
+
\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge 2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=1,
\]

so the left side controls

\[
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2.
\]

For the \(h\)-term:

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le
\varepsilon\int |\phi|\,|s_\delta(q)|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term, integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g\,(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Expand:

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta(q)
+
2\phi' s_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

Using \(|g|\le \varepsilon\), polynomial derivative bounds, and the cutoff estimates, the dangerous term is

\[
\varepsilon\int \phi |s_\delta''(q)|(q')^2
\le
C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\int_{\delta\le |q|\le 2\delta}\phi(q')^2.
\]

This term is localized to the transition annulus \(\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\). It can be absorbed into the left side if the left side is taken over \(|q|\ge\delta\), or bounded separately using the same argument at a slightly smaller cutoff. This produces the estimate

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

The exponent \(\delta^{-3}\) is plausible and matches the earlier heuristic.

---

# 3. Potential estimate away from \(q=0\)

Now test

\[
q''=F(q)+g
\]

against

\[
\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q),
\]

where \(\chi_\delta(q)=0\) for \(|q|\le2\delta\) and \(\chi_\delta(q)=1\) for \(|q|\ge3\delta\).

Then

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is bounded by

\[
Q^C\varepsilon |J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
=
-\int
\bigl(\phi\chi_\delta F(q)\bigr)'q'.
\]

Expanding gives terms of the form:

\[
-\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
-\int \phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2,
\]

\[
-\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'.
\]

Now

\[
F'(q)=6-6q^2.
\]

This term is not sign-definite globally, so it cannot simply be discarded. But it is bounded by the kinetic estimate:

\[
\left|
\int \phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2
\right|
\le
Q^C
\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

For the transition term, on \(2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,
\qquad
|\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1}.
\]

So

\[
|\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)|\le C,
\]

and the kinetic estimate again gives

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

For the boundary cutoff term,

\[
\int \phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q',
\]

use Cauchy–Schwarz and \(|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi\):

\[
\left|\int \phi'\chi_\delta Fq'\right|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}(q')^2.
\]

Absorb the first term into the left side and use the kinetic bound for the second.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}}|F(q)|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(q\) region

On

\[
|q|\le 3\delta,
\]

we have

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

and \(|g|\le\varepsilon\),

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Therefore

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Combine and optimize

On \(|q|\ge3\delta\),

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

so

\[
|u|^2\le 2|F(q)|^2+2\varepsilon^2.
\]

Hence

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\left(
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}+\delta^2+\varepsilon^2
\right)|J'|.
\]

Optimize by setting

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\delta^2.
\]

Thus

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5},
\qquad
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

So we obtain:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This proves the desired integral rigidity lemma, modulo the cutoff absorption and normalization details above.

---

# 6. Gate 2 conclusion

From two-threshold extraction, Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Apply integral rigidity with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then on \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

But since \(|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}\),

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Remaining technical obligations

This attack materially advances Gate 2. The remaining tasks are not conceptual; they are technical verification:

1. **Cutoff absorption:** formalize the transition-annulus term in the kinetic estimate so it does not circularly depend on itself.

2. **Boundary control:** choose \(\phi=\psi^2\) with

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi
\]

and similarly controlled \(\phi''\).

3. **Derivative convention:** verify the exact normalization in

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

4. **Polynomial bounds:** establish

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C
\]

on the local interval.

5. **Canonical transfer:** ensure these bounds hold for the canonical object

\[
q''_{\can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2.
\]

---

# 8. Current verdict

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now close to a proof modulo technical cutoff and canonical-bound bookkeeping.}
}
\]

The next execution should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{formalize the integral rigidity lemma in full detail.}
}
\]

In parallel:

\[
\boxed{
\text{verify two-threshold extraction Lipschitz bounds and D4 row correction control.}
}
\]

This is the strongest concrete progress in the downstream layer so far.

## Agent 6 / F — Continued attack: rigorous Gate 2 integral-rigidity core

The downstream route is now:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{two-threshold extraction}
+
\text{integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2},
\]

followed by wall escape and D4 row conversion. The current highest-value task is to make the integral-rigidity lemma proof-level. 

---

# 1. Target lemma

Let

\[
u=q'',\qquad
g=\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,\qquad
h=\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16 g''.
\]

Let

\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,
\qquad
u=F(q)+g.
\]

Assume on \(J\):

\[
\|g\|_{L^\infty(J)}+\|h\|_{L^\infty(J)}\le \varepsilon,
\]

and polynomial derivative bounds

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

Then for \(J'\Subset J\),

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This is the needed G2-B lemma.

---

# 2. Kinetic estimate away from \(q=0\)

Choose a smooth cutoff \(s_\delta(q)\) with

\[
s_\delta(q)=0 \quad (|q|\le \delta),
\]

\[
s_\delta(q)=\frac1q \quad (|q|\ge 2\delta),
\]

and

\[
|s_\delta^{(j)}(q)|\le C_j\delta^{-j-1}.
\]

Let \(\phi\) be supported in \(J\), equal to \(1\) on \(J'\), with

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi,\qquad |\phi''|\le Q^C.
\]

From

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

multiply by \(\phi s_\delta(q)\):

\[
2\int \phi s_\delta(q)q(q')^2
=
\int \phi s_\delta(q)h
+
\frac16\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''.
\]

On \(|q|\ge2\delta\),

\[
s_\delta(q)q=1.
\]

Thus the left side controls

\[
K_\delta:=\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2.
\]

The \(h\)-term obeys

\[
\left|\int \phi s_\delta(q)h\right|
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

For the \(g''\)-term, integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int \phi s_\delta(q)g''
=
\int g(\phi s_\delta(q))''.
\]

Now

\[
(\phi s_\delta(q))''
=
\phi''s_\delta
+
2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'
+
\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2
+
\phi s_\delta'(q)q''.
\]

The terms are bounded as follows.

First,

\[
\int |g\phi''s_\delta|
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-1}|J|.
\]

Second, by Cauchy–Schwarz / Young,

\[
\int |g\,2\phi's_\delta'(q)q'|
\le
\frac18K_\delta
+
Q^C\varepsilon^2\delta^{-4}|J|.
\]

Third,

\[
\int |g\,\phi s_\delta''(q)(q')^2|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
\int_{\{\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2.
\]

This is the only dangerous term. It is absorbed because we choose

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}\ll1.
\]

The final term uses

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

On the transition zone \(\delta\le |q|\le2\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,\qquad |g|\le\varepsilon.
\]

Hence

\[
\int |g\,\phi s_\delta'(q)q''|
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-2}(\delta+\varepsilon)|J|
\le
Q^C(\varepsilon\delta^{-1}+\varepsilon^2\delta^{-2})|J|.
\]

Therefore, after absorption,

\[
\boxed{
K_\delta
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

This is the kinetic estimate.

---

# 3. Potential estimate away from \(q=0\)

Let \(\chi_\delta(q)\) be smooth with

\[
\chi_\delta=0\quad(|q|\le2\delta),
\qquad
\chi_\delta=1\quad(|q|\ge3\delta),
\]

and

\[
|\chi_\delta^{(j)}|\le C_j\delta^{-j}.
\]

Use

\[
q''=F(q)+g.
\]

Multiply by \(\phi\chi_\delta(q)F(q)\):

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)^2
=
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)q''
-
\int \phi\chi_\delta F(q)g.
\]

The \(g\)-term is bounded by

\[
\left|\int \phi\chi_\delta Fg\right|
\le
\eta\int \phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta\varepsilon^2|J|.
\]

For the \(q''\)-term, integrate by parts:

\[
\int \phi\chi_\delta Fq''
=
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F)'q'.
\]

Expanding,

\[
-\int(\phi\chi_\delta F)'q'
=
-\int\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2
-\int\phi\chi_\delta'(q)F(q)(q')^2
-\int\phi'\chi_\delta F(q)q'.
\]

The first term is controlled by the kinetic estimate:

\[
\left|\int\phi\chi_\delta F'(q)(q')^2\right|
\le Q^C K_\delta
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

For the transition term, on \(2\delta\le |q|\le3\delta\),

\[
|F(q)|\le C\delta,\qquad |\chi_\delta'(q)|\le C\delta^{-1},
\]

so

\[
|\chi_\delta'F|\le C.
\]

Thus

\[
\left|\int\phi\chi_\delta'F(q)(q')^2\right|
\le Q^C K_\delta
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

For the boundary-cutoff term, use \(\phi=\psi^2\), so

\[
|\phi'|^2\le Q^C\phi.
\]

Then

\[
\left|\int\phi'\chi_\delta Fq'\right|
\le
\eta\int\phi\chi_\delta F^2
+
C_\eta Q^C\int_{\{|q|\ge2\delta\}}\phi(q')^2.
\]

Again use the kinetic estimate.

After absorbing the \(\eta\)-terms,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\ge3\delta\}} |F(q)|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
}
\]

---

# 4. Small-\(q\) region

On

\[
|q|\le3\delta,
\]

\[
|F(q)|=|6q-2q^3|\le C\delta.
\]

Since

\[
u=F(q)+g,
\]

\[
|u|\le C\delta+\varepsilon.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'\cap\{|q|\le3\delta\}}|u|^2
\le
Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
}
\]

---

# 5. Optimization

Combining large-\(q\) and small-\(q\) regions,

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C
\left(
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}
+\delta^2
+\varepsilon^2
\right)
|J'|.
\]

Choose

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

Then

\[
\varepsilon\delta^{-3}=\varepsilon^{2/5},
\qquad
\delta^2=\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

Therefore,

\[
\boxed{
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

This proves G2-B modulo the stated cutoff and derivative bounds.

---

# 6. Gate 2 implication

G2-A gives an interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Apply G2-B with

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-A_1}.
\]

Then

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}Q^{-2A_1/5}|J'|.
\]

But

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C_u}
\quad\text{on }J'
\]

gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge
Q^{-2C_u}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
\boxed{
\frac{2A_1}{5}-C_R>2C_u.
}
\]

So

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 7. Remaining checks

The remaining work is now technical rather than conceptual:

1. **Cutoff absorption:** formalize the absorption of the transition-annulus kinetic term

\[
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}K_\delta.
\]

With \(\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}\), this coefficient is

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}.
\]

So choose the smallness exponent \(A_1\) large enough that

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}\ll1.
\]

2. **Boundary margin:** ensure \(J'\Subset J\) with margin polynomially comparable to \(|J|\), so \(\phi\)-derivatives cost only \(Q^C\).

3. **Derivative bounds:** verify

\[
|q|+|q'|+|q''|+|q'''|+|q^{(4)}|\le Q^C.
\]

4. **Convention check:** confirm the sign and coefficient in

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''.
\]

5. **Canonical transfer:** verify these are for the canonical object, not a proxy.

---

# Bottom line

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 is now close to a proof.}
}
\]

The core analytic lemma is viable:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_J(|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|q''_{\can}|^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

The next execution should be a formal write-up of this lemma with cutoff definitions, margin constants, and canonical derivative bounds.

Current downstream picture:

\[

+

+
\text{G2-B integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{Wall-Escape Sampling}
+
\text{D4 matrix row conversion}
+

\Rightarrow

Key updates absorbed:

1. **Old D1/D2 are effectively replaced** by the local Gate 2 package:
   \[
   \text{two-threshold extraction}+\text{integral rigidity}.
   \]
   The generic Remez/Cartan problem is no longer the main route.

2. **Integral rigidity is the central Gate 2 lemma.** It uses
   \[
   g=q''-6q+2q^3,\qquad
   h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
   \]
   and proves a bound of the form
   \[
   \sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
   \Rightarrow
   \int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^c|J'|
   \]
   for some fixed \(c>0\). The exact exponent may be \(1/2\), \(2/5\), or a conservative \(1/3\), but any fixed positive exponent is sufficient for Gate 2. 

3. **Canonical derivative bookkeeping is now low-order.** For Gate 2, the needed local package is roughly derivative control for \(q\) through order \(5\) or \(6\), enough to bound \(u'\), \(g'\), and \(h'\), plus the local bounds used in cutoff estimates. 

4. **The \(q_0\)-wall is no longer necessarily a structural blocker** if row conversion can be existential or energetic over the packet interval. Wall escape moves from \(q_0\approx0\), \(u\neq0\) to a nearby non-wall point where D4 applies. Row mobility then thickens the pointwise row lower bound to row energy. 

5. **D4 is now finite row algebra.** The goal is to verify a normal form
   \[
   \mathbf A_{\rm row}=q_0u^3L\Gamma+\mathbf R,
   \qquad
   \Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
   \]
   with \(\sigma_{\min}(L)\ge Q^{-C}\) and half-leading remainder control. The main finite check is that the row symbols, likely \(A_7,A_9\), observe both anisotropy directions. 

6. **Remaining finite tasks** are now:
   - formalize the integral-rigidity lemma cleanly;
   - verify canonical derivative/local complexity bounds;
   - compute D4 row-symbol coefficients and determinant/minors;
   - prove D4 remainder half-leading bounds;
   - confirm the final architecture accepts row energy or existential sampling rather than exact-point row conversion.
