## Agent 6 / F — Downstream synthesis and exact next execution plan

I only see the new assignment prompt and shared background in this upload, not fresh Agent 1–5 results. So this is a synthesis of the **current downstream proof state**, not a post-result adjudication. The current assignment explicitly frames the downstream route as Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B implying Gate 2, then Gate 2 + D3a + D4 + row mobility implying row energy / row lower bound. 

---

# 1. Revised downstream chain

The correct current downstream architecture is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + G2-A + G2-B}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

where:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A = targeted two-threshold interval extraction}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B = integral rigidity with exponent }c>0.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 + D3a + D4 + row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy / row lower bound}.
}
\]

where:

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a = Wall-Escape Sampling / wall-to-annulus sampling}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4 = principal-symbol rank + projected-residual correction control}.
}
\]

This should replace the older downstream labels D1/D2/D3 as the active proof route. The old labels can remain as historical fallback commentary, but they are no longer the best formulation.

---

# 2. Module classification

## G2-A — Target-smallness two-threshold extraction

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green}}
\]

Reason: from Gate 1 plus Gate 2 failure, and using Lipschitz bounds for \(u,g,h\), one can extract an actual interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C}
\]

and

\[
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-S}.
\]

The important correction is to use a **target smallness exponent \(S\)** rather than tying the extracted smallness directly to the failure exponent \(A\). This avoids making the interval too small in a way that could destroy the cutoff constants.

Needs:

\[
|u'|_\infty,\ |g'|_\infty,\ |h'|_\infty \le Q^C |I|^{-1}.
\]

---

## G2-B — Integral rigidity

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green, with safe exponent }c=\frac13}
\]

The robust version is:

\[
\sup_J(|g|+|h|)\le\varepsilon
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2\le Q^C\varepsilon^{1/3}|J'|.
\]

The sharper exponent

\[
c=\frac25
\]

should be treated as optional until the transition kinetic estimate is sharpened. The safe exponent \(1/3\) is enough for the Gate 2 contradiction, provided the target smallness \(S\) is chosen large enough.

The proof uses

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

and avoids pointwise control of \(g''\) by integrating by parts.

---

## Ordinary zero-separated local complexity

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite audit / near-Green under ordinary zero-separated transfer}}
\]

Needed bounds:

\[
\sup_{J\subset I^\ast,\ |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I^\ast|}
\sup_J |J|^k|\partial^k q|
\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6
\]

or in normalized coordinates,

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le 6/7.
\]

At minimum, Gate 2 needs \(k\le5\), because

\[
h=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
\]

and

\[
h'=(1-q^2)q'''-2qq'q''-\frac16q^{(5)}.
\]

This package should follow from ordinary zero-separated completed-log-derivative transfer plus either direct formulas for \(q,q'\) or basepoint normalization.

Remaining audit items:

\[
\boxed{
\text{meromorphic formula, pole set, local zero count, }E_2\text{ transfer, and primitive/basepoint normalization.}
}
\]

---

## D3a — Wall escape / wall-to-annulus

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green, conditional on row-energy/existential sampling}}
\]

The wall split is:

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q_0|\ge\varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If wall mass dominates, remove low-source points \(|u|<\tau\). On the live wall strip,

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,\qquad |u|\ge\tau,
\]

the identity \(u=q_0''\) forces first-exit from the wall strip. At a first-exit point \(m_1\),

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge \tau/2,
\]

and, since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

with \(\varepsilon\ll \tau\),

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

Thus \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

D3a replaces the old “source-robust wall row” requirement **if** the final row layer accepts an existential sample or row-energy output.

---

## D4 — Principal-symbol rank

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite audit}}
\]

The target normal form is:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

where

\[
\Gamma=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Need:

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

For \(A_7,A_9\), expected leading behavior is:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

So the expected leading matrix is diagonal and full rank. But this must be verified as a principal-symbol statement after projection.

If \(A_7,A_9\) do not suffice, enlarge to:

\[
\mathbf A_N=(A_7,A_9,A_{11},A_{13},\ldots)^T.
\]

Rank check:

\[
\max_{i<j}
|\ell_{i,1}\ell_{j,2}-\ell_{i,2}\ell_{j,1}|
\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

---

## D4 — Projected-residual correction control

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite audit}}
\]

Need:

\[
|P_L\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12 |q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

The instruction correctly notes that **projected residual control** is enough: residual components orthogonal to \(\operatorname{im}L_N\) cannot cancel the leading vector.

Residuals should be split into:

\[
\mathbf R_{\rm high},\quad
\mathbf R_{\rm can},\quad
\mathbf R_{\rm proj},\quad
\mathbf R_{\rm norm}.
\]

All non-perturbative \(\Gamma\)-linear terms must be absorbed into \(L_{\rm eff}\), not treated as error.

---

## Row mobility / existential sampling

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green}}
\]

If

\[
|\mathbf A(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1},
\]

then row mobility gives an interval \(J_\ast\subset I\) with polynomial length and

\[
|\mathbf A(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]

on \(J_\ast\), hence

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

So D3a is admissible if the downstream contradiction uses row energy or existential row output. If exact-point row conversion is required, the fallback is the \(q_0\)-adic row-pencil audit.

---

# 3. Safe exponent policy

Record the safe Gate 2 exponent as:

\[
\boxed{c=\frac13.}
\]

The sharper exponent

\[
\boxed{c=\frac25}
\]

should be listed as an optional improvement conditional on closing the stronger kinetic estimate:

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}.
\]

The proof should not depend on \(2/5\).

---

# 4. Replace old labels or keep them?

I recommend formally replacing the active downstream labels:

\[
D1,D2,D3
\]

with:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A, G2-B, D3a}.
}
\]

Keep the old labels only in a historical note:

\[
D1/D2
\quad\text{were replaced by}\quad
\text{two-threshold extraction + integral rigidity}.
\]

\[
D3
\quad\text{was replaced by}\quad
\text{wall escape + row mobility},
\]

unless exact-point row conversion is required.

D4 remains active, but sharpened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{principal-symbol rank + projected-residual correction control}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Exact remaining proof obligations

The remaining obligations are now finite and local.

## Gate 2 obligations

1. **Ordinary local complexity / zero-separated transfer**

\[
\sup |\mathcal D^kq|\le Q^{C_k},\qquad 0\le k\le6/7.
\]

2. **Primitive or basepoint bounds for \(q,q'\)**

Either direct meromorphic formulas, or

\[
|q(x_0)|+|q'(x_0)|\le Q^C.
\]

3. **G2-B cutoff proof**

Use safe exponent \(1/3\), with all cutoff and transition terms explicit.

4. **Target-smallness exponent hierarchy**

Choose \(S\) so that:

\[
cS-C_R(S)>2C_1.
\]

Under scale-invariant derivative bounds, \(C_R(S)=O(1)\), so large fixed \(S\) suffices.

---

## Wall / row obligations

5. **Wall escape**

Complete first-exit proof, boundary-layer removal, and live-source extraction.

6. **Row-energy admissibility**

Confirm final contradiction accepts row energy or existential row output.

7. **D4 principal-symbol rank**

Compute principal symbols of \(A_7,A_9\) first:

\[
\operatorname{gr}_5(A_7),\quad \operatorname{gr}_5(A_9).
\]

Expected:

\[
-\frac1{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_G,
\qquad
-\frac1{288}q_0u^3\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

8. **Projection regularity**

Projection must act by regular row operations, with no denominators:

\[
1/q_0,\quad 1/u,\quad 1/\Gamma_G,\quad 1/\Gamma_{G,2},\quad 1/|\Gamma|.
\]

9. **Projected-residual correction control**

Bound projected residual half-leading.

---

# 6. Next execution plan

No more than three next tasks:

## Task 1 — Finalize Gate 2 proof package

Write G2-A + G2-B as a theorem using safe exponent \(c=1/3\), with target-smallness \(S\), and specify the ordinary local complexity hypotheses.

This has highest proof value because it replaces old D1/D2.

---

## Task 2 — Execute D4 principal-symbol rank audit for \(A_7,A_9\)

Compute:

\[
\operatorname{gr}_5(A_7^{\rm raw}),\qquad
\operatorname{gr}_5(A_9^{\rm raw})
\]

and verify projection preserves the two anisotropy directions.

If successful, D4 reduces to correction estimates.

---

## Task 3 — Prove row mobility / existential row-energy admissibility

Formalize:

\[
|\mathbf A(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C}
\Rightarrow
\int_I|\mathbf A|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

Then wall escape is admissible.

---

# 7. Final downstream status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Downstream is now substantially more local and closer to proof.}
}
\]

The remaining blockers are not broad arithmetic inputs. They are:

\[

}
\]

The main architectural replacement is:

\[

\quad\leadsto\quad

## Assistant (2026-04-27 12:31:18)

_Thought for 12s_

## Agent 6 / F — Synthesis after new Gate 2 route

The downstream architecture should now be updated. The active route is no longer the old pointwise target-smallness path. The strongest current downstream chain is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}
+
\text{source-large interval extraction}
+
L^2\text{-input integral rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2}
+
\text{D3a wall escape}
+
\text{D4 row-span conversion}
+
\text{row mobility}
\Rightarrow
\text{row energy}.
}
\]

This supersedes the prior D1/D2/D3 framing and should be treated as the active proof path. 

---

# 1. Demote the older pointwise route

The older route was:

\[
\text{target-smallness pointwise extraction}
+
\text{pointwise G2-B integral rigidity}.
\]

That route extracted an interval \(J\) where

\[
|u|\ge Q^{-C},
\qquad
|g|+|h|\le Q^{-A_1}
\]

pointwise. It was useful, but it introduced a hidden problem: the interval length can shrink with the anisotropy-smallness exponent. That shrinkage can feed back into cutoff losses.

The new route avoids that issue. It extracts a **source-large interval** whose length depends on the source threshold, then uses Gate 2 failure to obtain **average anisotropy smallness** on that interval. So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{old pointwise extraction route = fallback / historical route only.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Active Gate 2 package

## G2-A′ — Source-large interval extraction

From Gate 1,

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|,
\]

and local source bounds

\[
|u|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
|u'|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

choose a threshold

\[
\tau=Q^{-T}.
\]

Then extract an interval \(J\subset I\) such that

\[
|u|\ge \tau
\quad\text{on }J,
\]

and

\[
|J|\ge Q^{-T-C_u-O(1)}|I|.
\]

If Gate 2 fails,

\[
\int_I |u|^2(g^2+h^2)\,dm\le Q^{-A}|I|,
\]

then on some such source-large interval,

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
\]

So set

\[
\varepsilon^2
=
Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green.}}
\]

It depends only on \(u,u'\), not on Remez/Cartan or pointwise anisotropy extraction.

---

## G2-B′ — \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

The new rigidity input is:

\[
\boxed{
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
}
\]

Here

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,
\qquad
F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

This is stronger than the prior pointwise lemma because it accepts exactly the kind of average anisotropy smallness that Gate 2 failure naturally supplies. The proof uses the multiplier

\[
q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

against

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

to obtain the kinetic bound

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|.
\]

Optimizing at

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}
\]

gives exponent

\[
\boxed{c=\frac25}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green, pending final cutoff proof.}}
\]

Use \(2/5\) for this \(L^2\)-input lemma if Agent 2’s repaired multiplier proof holds.

---

## Gate 2 conclusion

On \(J'\subset J\), source-large extraction gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2\ge \tau^2|J'|.
\]

The \(L^2\)-input rigidity gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}<\tau^2.
\]

With

\[
\varepsilon^2=Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)},
\]

a sufficient condition is schematically

\[
A>12T+C_U+O(C).
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 + source-large extraction + \(L^2\)-input rigidity}
\Rightarrow
\text{Gate 2}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Module classification

| Module | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| Source-large interval extraction | near-Green | Needs \(|u|_\infty, |u'|_\infty\). |
| \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity | near-Green | Main remaining Gate 2 proof; target exponent \(2/5\). |
| Ordinary zero-separated local complexity | near-Green / finite audit | Needs \(u,u'\), plus \(q,q'\) or basepoint normalization. |
| D3a wall escape | near-Green | Works for row-energy/existential architecture. |
| Row mobility | Green / near-Green | Needs row derivative bound. |
| D4 raw principal rank | finite audit | Expected \(A_7,A_9\) principal directions. |
| D4 projection coercivity | finite audit | Only needed if projected rows are required. |
| D4 projected residual control | finite audit | Control residual in leading row-image only. |
| Old D1/D2/D3 | fallback | Keep only as historical fallback labels. |

---

# 4. Remaining Gate 2 proof obligations

## 4.1 Source interval extraction

Need to formalize the covering/pigeonhole argument:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

plus

\[
|u|_\infty\le Q^C,\qquad |u'|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1}
\]

implies existence of a source-large interval \(J\) with

\[
|u|\ge\tau
\]

and controlled length.

Then Gate 2 failure must imply

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\le Q^{-A+2T+C_U+O(1)}.
\]

## 4.2 \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof

Need the exact cutoff proof using:

\[
q\chi_\delta(q)
\]

as multiplier, not the older sign-cutoff-only argument.

The required estimates are:

\[
\int_{|q|\ge2\delta}\phi(q')^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J|,
\]

\[
\int_{J'\cap |q|\ge3\delta}F(q)^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon\delta^{-3}|J'|,
\]

\[
\int_{J'\cap |q|\le3\delta}|u|^2
\le Q^C(\delta^2+\varepsilon^2)|J'|.
\]

Then optimize:

\[
\delta=\varepsilon^{1/5}.
\]

## 4.3 Canonical bounds

The new Gate 2 route needs less than the prior package:

\[
|u|_\infty\le Q^C,
\qquad
|u'|_\infty\le Q^C|I|^{-1},
\]

plus polynomial control of

\[
q,\quad q',\quad q''
\]

for the \(L^2\)-rigidity proof.

Still, the safe canonical theorem remains:

\[
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D^k q|\le Q^{C_k},
\qquad 0\le k\le7.
\]

This should follow under ordinary zero-separated tube hypotheses, provided \(q,q'\) are covered by direct canonical formulas or basepoint normalization.

## 4.4 Residual version

If the identities are approximate,

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3+r_g,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g''+r_h,
\]

then require

\[
\|r_g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|r_h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}.
\]

---

# 5. Row-conversion layer

## D3a wall escape

D3a remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 wall mass}
\Rightarrow
\text{nearby non-wall D4 sample}.
}
\]

The wall split is:

\[
I_{\rm nd}=\{|q_0|\ge\varepsilon\},
\qquad
I_{\rm wall}=\{|q_0|<\varepsilon\}.
\]

If wall mass dominates, remove low-source points \(|u|<\tau\). On the live wall strip,

\[
|q_0|<\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u|\ge\tau,
\]

the identity

\[
u=q_0''
\]

forces first exit to a point \(m_1\) with

\[
|q_0(m_1)|=\varepsilon,
\qquad
|u(m_1)|\ge\tau/2.
\]

Then

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3
\]

and \(\varepsilon\ll\tau\) give

\[
|\Gamma_G(m_1)|\ge c\tau.
\]

So \(m_1\) is a non-wall D4 sample.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green if row-energy/existential output is allowed.}}
\]

---

## Row mobility

If

\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]

and

\[
|\mathbf A_N'|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1},
\]

then

\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N|^2\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{Green / near-Green.}}
\]

This validates wall escape if the final contradiction uses row energy rather than exact-point row lower bounds.

---

## D4 principal-symbol rank

D4 target:

\[
\mathbf A_N=q_0u^3L_N\Gamma+\mathbf R_N,
\]

\[
\Gamma=(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})^T,
\]

with

\[
\sigma_2(L_N)\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Expected principal rows:

\[
A_7\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\]

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]

So expected directional responses are:

\[
v_1\sim -\frac1{288}e_7,
\qquad
v_2\sim -\frac1{288}e_9.
\]

D4 should be audited through raw principal-symbol rank first:

\[
|v_1\wedge v_2|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

If projected rows are needed, verify projection coercivity on the anisotropy plane:

\[
|P_{\mathfrak f}v_1\wedge P_{\mathfrak f}v_2|\ge Q^{-C}.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite audit.}}
\]

---

## D4 projected residual control

Do not require full residual norm unless necessary. It is enough to control the residual projected to the leading row image:

\[
|P_L\mathbf R_N|
\le
\frac12|q_0||u|^3\sigma_2(L_N)|\Gamma|.
\]

All non-perturbative \(\Gamma\)-linear terms should be absorbed into an effective matrix \(L_{\rm eff}\).

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite audit.}}
\]

---

# 6. Architecture update

The active downstream labels should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-A′: Source-large interval extraction}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{G2-B′: \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity}
}

\[
\boxed{
\text{D3a: Wall escape / wall-to-annulus row sampling}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{D4: Row-span principal rank + projected-residual control}
}
\]

The old labels

# 2. Module classification

## \(|u'|_\infty\) source thickening

Status:

\[

Thus there is some point \(m_\ast\in I\) with

This is cleaner than the previous dyadic/Vitali extraction.

## \(L^2\)-input integral rigidity

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{near-Green; central Gate 2 lemma}}
\]

The target lemma is:

\[
\|g\|_{L^2(J)}+\|h\|_{L^2(J)}
\le
\varepsilon |J|^{1/2}
\Rightarrow
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^C\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

Here

\[
g=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
h=2q(q')^2-\frac16g'',
\]

\[
u=q''=F(q)+g,\qquad F(q)=6q-2q^3.
\]

The currently preferred proof uses the multiplier

\[
a_\delta(q)=q\chi_\delta(q),
\]

with

\[
a_\delta'(q)=O(1),
\qquad
a_\delta''(q)=O(\delta^{-1}),
\]

against \(h\). This avoids the worse transition loss from sign-cutoff methods and supports the exponent

\[
\boxed{c=\frac25.}
\]

---

Status:

\qquad

These should follow from ordinary zero-separated canonical transfer for

\[

The ordinary zero-separated hypothesis is:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(

\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge
\lambda Q^{-C_0}.
\]

The proof should use completed meromorphic/log-derivative estimates, not AFE \(\ell^1\) bounds.

For now, the clean formal path should keep primitive admissibility / direct formulas as an explicit hypothesis.

Split:

# 3. Gate 2 exponent flow

From source thickening:

\[
\tau\asymp Q^{-B/2}.
\]

Gate 2 failure gives on the thickened interval \(J\):

\[
\frac1{|J|}\int_J(g^2+h^2)\,dm
\le
Q^{-A+\frac32B+C_u+O(1)}.
\]

Thus

\[
\varepsilon
=
Q^{-A/2+\frac34B+\frac12C_u+O(1)}.
\]

The \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\le
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}|J'|.
\]

But source thickness gives

\[
\int_{J'}|u|^2
\ge Q^{-B-O(1)}|J'|.
\]

Contradiction if

\[
Q^{C_R}\varepsilon^{2/5}<Q^{-B-O(1)}.
\]

A sufficient condition is:

\[
\boxed{
A>\frac{13}{2}B+C_u+5C_R+O(1).
}
\]

So Gate 2 is locally proved once the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma and the \(u'\)-bound are formalized.

and the \(L^2\)-input rigidity lemma is written cleanly with exponent \(2/5\).

The exponent flow is stable:

So old \(D1/D2\) are effectively replaced by the Gate 2 theorem once the real-normal-form and \(L^2\)-rigidity proof are finalized.

# 3. D4 status

\[
\boxed{
\text{Main remaining downstream blocker.}
}
\]

The exact blocker is no longer generic “row formulas missing.” It is the order-9 correction/cross-channel package.

Known positives:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}T_7^{(1)}=-2yBr\,I\sim H\Gamma_G,
\]

and the clean order-9 channel:

\[

=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}I
\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

But the actual corrected order-9 \(I\)-sector row is:

\[
(A_9^{\mathfrak f})_I
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
+
R_9^I.
\]

Define:

\[
F_9^I
=
R_9^I+
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

The current unresolved incidence wall is:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm cc}^{(9)}
=
\{F_9^I=0,\ yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\}.
\]

D4 is not closed until \(R_9^I\) is fully computed and classified as zero, \(H\)-divisible, quotient/nuisance, harmless, or genuinely cross-channel with quantitative avoidance.

_Thought for 1m 46s_

## Verdict

\[
\boxed{\text{carrier quotient row energy admissible}}
\]

## 1. Row-output classification

The needed post-D4 row-output statement is **carrier quotient row energy**, not collapsed scalar \(I\)-coordinate energy.

The relevant row object is the pre-collapse carrier class

\[
[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}]\in \mathcal Q_{\rm car}
=
\mathcal M_{\rm car}/\mathcal C_{\rm car},
\]

with nuisance carriers killed before applying scalar collapse. The current criterion explicitly says carrier quotient lower bounds are admissible when the downstream obstruction is stated in the full row algebra/module or quotient row algebra, rather than only after applying \(S_I\). 

---

## 2. Is the carrier quotient lower bound admissible?

Yes. A lower bound of the form

\[
\int_I
|[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}(m)]|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I|
\]

is admissible for the current downstream row-energy architecture.

The reason is that D4 is now formulated as a row-span / quotient row-energy obstruction. In \(\mathcal Q_{\rm car}\), the clean order-9 carrier survives as

\[
[\mathcal A_9^{\rm car}]
=
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}
[\mathsf C_{Y12}],
\]

while the \(N_7,N_5\), line, background, core, and normalization carriers are quotiented as nuisance directions. 

---

## 3. Exact map to downstream row obstruction

The map is:

\[
\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}
\longmapsto
[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}]
\in
\mathcal Q_{\rm car}.
\]

D4 supplies a pointwise lower bound for the carrier quotient class. Row mobility then upgrades this to row energy:

\[
|[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}(m_\ast)]|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}\ge Q^{-C}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_I |[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}(m)]|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C'}|I|.
\]

This is the admissible downstream obstruction: the row class is nonzero in the quotient module before scalar carrier collapse.

---

## 4. Is the proof forced to use \(S_I(\mathcal A_N)\)?

No, not under the current row-energy formulation.

The scalar wall

\[
F_9^I=0
\]

is relevant only if the final downstream theorem insists on the collapsed scalar coordinate

\[
S_I(\mathcal A_N).
\]

That scalar collapse can cancel independent carrier directions, so carrier quotient energy would not imply scalar \(I\)-coordinate energy in that stricter architecture. The files state this exact fork: if carrier/quotient row energy is accepted, D4 can close through order 9; if scalar \(I\)-coordinate energy is mandatory, the cross-channel wall remains. 

\[
\boxed{\text{carrier quotient row energy admissible}}
\]

## Edit 1 — Add canonical real-normal-form / zero-separated source transfer

**Where:** Immediately after `\end{proof}` of Lemma `\ref{lem:differentiated-form-second-gate-two-anisotropy}`, before the paragraph beginning `For two nearby points around a center $T$...`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Ordinary zero-separated real-canonical packet]
\label{def:ordinary-zero-separated-real-canonical-packet}
Let \(I^\ast\) be an ordinary packet interval, let \(\lambda Q\asymp1\), and
write
\[
        \mathcal D=\lambda\partial_m .
\]
For \(\rho\ge Q^{-C_\rho}\), set
\[
\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast)
:=
\{m+iy:m\in I^\ast,\ |y|\le \rho\lambda\}.
\]
We say that \(I^\ast\) is an ordinary zero-separated real-canonical packet if
\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
\frac12+i\mathcal T_\rho(I^\ast),
\mathcal Z_\Xi
\right)
\ge \lambda Q^{-C_0},
\]
and if the local source curvature is the completed critical-line curvature
\[
q''_{\can}
=
\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\!\left(\frac12+im\right),
\]
where \(\mathfrak C_2\) is the fixed completed meromorphic curvature operator.
In particular \(q''_{\can}\) is the full real-canonical object, not a one-sided
AFE branch or a truncated proxy.

The only allowed poles of \(\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) in the ordinary tube are
poles inherited from completed logarithmic derivatives of \(\Xi\), hence from
zeros of \(\Xi\).  No denominator of the form
\[
\frac1q,\qquad
\frac1{q''_{\can}},\qquad
\frac1{\Gamma_G},\qquad
\frac1{\Gamma_{G,2}},\qquad
\frac1{|\Gamma|}
\]
is part of the definition of \(q''_{\can}\).
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Ordinary completed-log-derivative source transfer]
\label{lem:ordinary-completed-log-derivative-source-transfer}
On an ordinary zero-separated real-canonical packet,
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{I^\ast}|q''_{\can}|
+
\sup_{I^\ast}|\mathcal D q''_{\can}|
\le Q^C .
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let
\[
L(s)=\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}(s).
\]
For fixed \(r\), completed logarithmic derivatives have the local meromorphic
form
\[
L^{(r)}(s)
=
(-1)^r r!\sum_{\rho\in\mathcal Z_\Xi}
\frac{1}{(s-\rho)^{r+1}}
+
\text{regular completed background}.
\]
On the zero-separated tube, every zero has distance at least
\[
\delta:=\lambda Q^{-C_0}
\]
from the tube.  Decompose the zeros into dyadic annuli around the tube:
\[
2^j\delta\le \operatorname{dist}(s,\rho)<2^{j+1}\delta .
\]
The standard local zero-count bound gives a polynomial number of zeros in each
annulus after the harmless dyadic factor is included.  Hence, for each fixed
\(r\),
\[
\sum_\rho |s-\rho|^{-(r+1)}
\le Q^{C_r}.
\]
The completed gamma/background terms and their fixed derivatives are also
polynomially bounded on ordinary packets.  Since
\(\mathfrak C_2[\Xi]\) is a fixed finite expression in these completed
logarithmic derivatives and regular background terms, this proves
\[
|q''_{\can}|\le Q^C.
\]
Applying one normalized derivative \(\mathcal D\) only raises the finite
completed-log-derivative order by one, so the same estimate gives
\[
|\mathcal D q''_{\can}|\le Q^C.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Real normal form and primitive policy]
\label{rem:real-normal-form-and-primitive-policy}
The \(L^2\)-input rigidity proof below is a real scalar argument.  It applies
only in a real completed critical-line gauge, i.e. a gauge in which
\[
q,\quad q''_{\can},\quad \Gamma_G,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}
\]
are real on the packet.  This is automatic if \(q\) is constructed from a real
critical-line scalar such as \(\Xi(t)=\xi(1/2+it)\) or Hardy's \(Z(t)\), with
real coefficients and safe chart denominators.

For the safe Gate--2 theorem we assume the primitive bounds needed by
Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}.  Equivalently, it is enough to
assume a basepoint normalization
\[
|q(m_b)|+|\mathcal D q(m_b)|\le Q^C
\]
on a polynomial enlargement of the source interval, because
\[
q''=q''_{\can},\qquad
|q''_{\can}|+|\mathcal Dq''_{\can}|\le Q^C
\]
then imply polynomial bounds for \(q,q'\), and \(q''\) on the extracted source
interval.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures the ordinary zero-separated transfer, pole-set guardrail, and real-normal-form requirement that the current Gate 2 proof relies on. The draft currently references this package but does not state it as a standalone theorem.

## Edit 2 — Strengthen the primitive-free remark without using it as mainline

**Where:** Replace the entire current remark

```latex
\begin{remark}[Primitive-free strengthening not used]
...
\end{remark}
```

i.e. `\label{rem:l2-rigidity-primitive-free-not-used}`.

**Replace with:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Primitive recovery is optional, not part of the safe proof]
\label{rem:l2-rigidity-primitive-free-not-used}
Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe} is stated with the safe primitive
bounds
\[
\|q\|_\infty+\|q'\|_\infty+\|q''\|_\infty\le Q^C.
\]
There is, however, a useful primitive-recovery mechanism.  Since
\[
F(q)=6q-2q^3,\qquad u=F(q)+g,
\]
one has the pointwise algebraic inequality
\[
|q|^6\le C(1+|F(q)|^2).
\]
Thus \(F(q)\in L^2(J)\), together with polynomial \(u\)-control and
\(L^2\)-small \(g\), gives polynomial \(L^6\)-control of \(q\).  Since
\(q''=u\), one-dimensional interpolation then gives polynomial control of
\(q'\) in \(L^2\) and \(L^4\) on shrunken intervals.  These are the norms
actually used by the multiplier proof.

This primitive-recovering version may eventually replace the safe primitive
hypothesis.  It is not used in the main argument here; the proof above keeps
the stronger \(L^\infty\) primitive bounds to avoid exceptional-set
bookkeeping.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** The draft currently says the primitive-free strengthening is “not used.” This replacement captures the useful derived mechanism without making the proof depend on it. This matches the current safest state: safe theorem first, primitive-free as a strengthening.

## Edit 3 — Add a short theorem for row mobility

**Where:** After `\end{remark}` of `\ref{rem:d3-replaced-by-wall-escape-plus-d4}` and before `\section{Current proof state after the local package audits}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility from a pointwise row lower bound]
\label{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to\mathbb C^M\) be a finite row vector.  Suppose
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\qquad (m\in I).
\]
Then
\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C'}|I|
\]
for some polynomial exponent \(C'\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For
\[
|m-m_\ast|\le \frac12Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]
the derivative bound gives
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)-\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\le \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]
Thus
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]
on a subinterval of length at least \(Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|\), after taking a
one-sided subinterval if \(m_\ast\) is near the boundary.  Integrating the
square over that subinterval gives the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Exact-point versus row-energy output]
\label{rem:exact-point-versus-row-energy-output}
The wall-escape theorem is an interval/energy statement.  It is admissible when
the downstream row obstruction is formulated as existential row output or row
energy on the packet.  If instead the final contradiction requires a fixed
preassigned point \(m_0\), wall escape does not apply and the \(q_0\)-adic
source-robust row-pencil route remains the fallback.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** Row mobility has been repeatedly used as a structural bridge, but the draft’s wall-escape theorem currently invokes it rather than isolating it. This makes the row-energy admissibility precise.

---

## Edit 4 — Add a wall-to-annulus caution / why pointwise escape remains mainline

**Where:** After the row mobility lemma above, or immediately after `\ref{rem:d3-replaced-by-wall-escape-plus-d4}` if you prefer to keep all wall comments together.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Wall-to-annulus transfer is a possible strengthening, not the main route]
\label{rem:wall-to-annulus-transfer-fallback}
One can try to replace pointwise wall escape plus row mobility by a fully
measure-level statement
\[
\text{wall mass}\Longrightarrow\text{annular mass}
\Longrightarrow\text{D4 energy}.
\]
This would be stronger and would align directly with integrated row energy.
However, a direct wall-mass to fixed-annulus-mass theorem is not automatic: a
wall component can touch or cross an annulus rapidly, and the annular layer may
require a first-exit/Vitali refinement.

The main route in this paper is therefore the safer hybrid:
\[
\text{live wall mass}
\Longrightarrow
\text{first-exit non-wall samples}
\Longrightarrow
\text{D4 pointwise row lower bound}
\Longrightarrow
\text{row energy by Lemma~\ref{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}}.
\]
The purely \(L^2\) wall-to-annulus transfer remains a possible strengthening,
not a dependency of the present downstream package.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures the measure-based wall-to-annulus idea and its no-go boundary, without making it a dependency.

## Edit 9 — Add a quotient-coordinate D4 theorem after the carrier-quotient theorem

**Where:** Immediately after `\end{proof}` of `\begin{theorem}[D4 carrier-quotient row conversion through order nine]` and before `\begin{remark}[Scalar \(I\)-coordinate incidence is a collapse artifact]`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Two-coordinate carrier-quotient D4 conversion]
\label{thm:two-coordinate-carrier-quotient-d4}
Let
\[
E_{\rm car}
:=
\bigl([\mathsf C_7]\ [\mathsf C_{Y12}]\bigr)
\]
be the two-column carrier response map into \(\mathcal Q_{\rm car}\).  Assume
its quotient Gram matrix
\[
G_{\rm car}:=
E_{\rm car}^\ast E_{\rm car}
\]
satisfies
\[
\det G_{\rm car}\ge Q^{-C}.
\]
Equivalently, the two carrier classes
\[
[\mathsf C_7],\qquad [\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]
are polynomially independent in the carrier quotient.

Let \(B_7,B_9\) denote the dual quotient coordinates associated to this
basis.  Suppose the carrier-row class satisfies
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
B_7\\[1mm]
B_9
\end{pmatrix}
=
H
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\[1mm]
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
+
\epsilon,
\]
with
\[
|\epsilon|
\le
\frac12 |H|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
Then
\[
\left|[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}]\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}
\ge
Q^{-C}
|H|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
Consequently, combined with Gate~2 and wall escape, carrier-quotient row
mobility gives
\[
\int_I
\left|[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}(m)]\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The determinant lower bound for \(G_{\rm car}\) gives a polynomial lower frame
bound for the two quotient carrier coordinates.  The displayed coordinate
identity says that, in this frame, the leading carrier response is exactly
\(H(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\), up to a half-leading error.  The lower bound
follows by the triangle inequality and the frame lower bound.  Row mobility
then upgrades the pointwise carrier-quotient lower bound to integrated
carrier-quotient row energy.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** This captures the refined “two scalar quotient coordinates” formulation. It also formalizes why scalar \(I\)-coordinate cancellation is irrelevant if the carrier quotient is accepted.

```latex
\begin{remark}[When the scalar order-nine wall matters]

\[
F_9^I=0
\]
is not a D4 obstruction in the carrier-quotient row-energy formulation.

\[
S_I(\mathcal A_N)

R_{\rm corr}^{I,(9)}

\[
\{F_9^I=0,\ yq''\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0\},
\]

\end{remark}
```

## Edit 11 — Add an exact “Definition repairs / consistency” note near the final status

**Where:** In `\section{Final status after the downstream closure repairs}`, after `\begin{remark}[What is closed downstream and what remains upstream] ... \end{remark}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Definition consistency required for the downstream package]
\label{rem:definition-consistency-required-downstream}
The downstream package uses one and the same scalar \(q\) in four places:
\[
u=q''_{\can}=q'',
\]
\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G'',
\]
and the D4 row factor
\[
H\sim-\frac{q\,u^3}{288}.
\]
This gauge-locking is essential.  If the \(q\) used for wall escape, the \(q\)
used in \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\), and the \(q\) used in the D4 factor are not
the same real-canonical scalar, then wall escape may move the wrong coordinate.
In that case the downstream package must be rebuilt with the correct scalar or
with explicit residuals:
\[
u-q'',\qquad
\Gamma_G-(q''-6q+2q^3),
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}-\left(2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\right).
\]
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This is a definition-level guardrail repeatedly identified in the conversation.

# Edit 1 — Add the missing row-mobility lemma

**Where:** Immediately after `\end{proof}` of Theorem `\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}`, before the remark `\begin{remark}[D3 is replaced by wall escape plus D4]`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Row mobility from a pointwise row lower bound]
\label{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}
Let \(\mathbf A_N:I\to\mathbb C^M\) be a finite row vector.  Assume
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\ge Q^{-C_A}
\]
for some \(m_\ast\in I\), and
\[
|\mathbf A_N'(m)|\le Q^{C_D}|I|^{-1}
\qquad(m\in I).
\]
Then
\[
\int_I|\mathbf A_N(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-C'}|I|
\]
for some polynomial exponent \(C'\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For
\[
|m-m_\ast|\le \frac12 Q^{-C_A-C_D}|I|,
\]
the derivative bound gives
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)-\mathbf A_N(m_\ast)|\le \frac12Q^{-C_A}.
\]
Thus
\[
|\mathbf A_N(m)|\ge \frac12Q^{-C_A}
\]
on a one-sided or two-sided subinterval of length at least
\[
Q^{-C_A-C_D-O(1)}|I|.
\]
Integrating \(|\mathbf A_N|^2\) over this subinterval gives the claim.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** The wall theorem concludes “D4 + row mobility gives row energy,” but row mobility is not yet stated as a lemma in the draft.

---

# Edit 2 — Make the D4 carrier-quotient theorem proof-usable

**Where:** Replace the entire theorem

```latex
\begin{theorem}[D4 carrier-quotient row conversion through order nine]
\label{thm:d4-carrier-quotient-through-order-nine}
...
\end{theorem}
```

including its proof.

**Replace with:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[D4 carrier-quotient row conversion through order nine]
\label{thm:d4-carrier-quotient-through-order-nine}
Assume the carrier-quotient row-energy formulation is admissible downstream.
Let
\[
W_{\rm car}:=\operatorname{span}\{[\mathsf C_7],[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\}
\subset \mathcal Q_{\rm car}.
\]
Assume the quotient Gram matrix of the ordered pair
\[
[\mathsf C_7],\qquad [\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\]
has determinant bounded below by \(Q^{-C}\).

Assume that, in \(\mathcal Q_{\rm car}\), the order-seven and order-nine row
classes have the form
\[
[\mathcal A_7]
=
H\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]+\mathcal E_7,
\]
\[
[\mathcal A_9]
=
H\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]+\mathcal E_9,
\]
and that the quotient projection of the residual into \(W_{\rm car}\) is
half-leading:
\[
\left|
P_{W_{\rm car}}
\left(
\mathcal E_7+\mathcal E_9
\right)
\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}
\le
\frac12
|H|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
Then
\[
\left|
[\mathcal A_7]+[\mathcal A_9]
\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}
\ge
Q^{-C}
|H|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
Consequently, combined with Gate~2, gauge-locked wall escape, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:row-mobility-point-to-energy}, one obtains carrier-quotient row
energy
\[
\int_I
\left|[\mathcal A_N^{\rm car}(m)]\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-C}|I|.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Gram determinant lower bound gives a polynomial lower frame bound for the
two quotient carrier directions.  Therefore
\[
\left|
H\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]+H\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\right|_{\mathcal Q_{\rm car}}
\ge
Q^{-C}
|H|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
The residual bound is half-leading in the only quotient directions that can
cancel the leading response.  The triangle inequality gives the pointwise row
lower bound.  Row mobility upgrades the pointwise lower bound to row energy.
\end{proof}
```

**Why:** The current theorem uses `\sim` inside a theorem statement. This replacement turns it into a precise conditional row-conversion theorem with a clear residual hypothesis.

# Edit 3 — Add two-coordinate quotient-coordinate formulation

**Where:** Immediately after the replacement theorem above, before `\begin{remark}[Scalar \(I\)-coordinate incidence is a collapse artifact]`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Two quotient coordinates for D4]
\label{rem:two-quotient-coordinates-d4}
Equivalently, choose dual quotient coordinates \(B_7,B_9\) for the pair
\[
[\mathsf C_7],\qquad [\mathsf C_{Y12}].
\]
Then D4 may be checked by the two scalar identities
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
B_7\\
B_9
\end{pmatrix}
=
H
M_Q
\begin{pmatrix}
\Gamma_G\\
\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}
+
\epsilon,
\]
with
\[
|\det M_Q|\ge Q^{-C},
\]
and
\[
|\epsilon|
\le
\frac12
|H|\,
\sigma_{\min}(M_Q)
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]
In the expected clean carrier normalization,
\[
M_Q=I_2
\]
up to the fixed nonzero scalar already absorbed into the definition of the
carrier coordinates.  This two-coordinate formulation is the smallest D4
correction-control statement: residual components orthogonal to the carrier
anisotropy plane cannot cancel the leading row response.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** This captures the “two scalar quotient-coordinate” reduction from the conversation and makes D4 easier to audit.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Historical fallback Gate--2 source--anisotropy vector observability]
\label{hyp:source-anisotropy-vector-observability}
On an admissible interval \(I_\rho\), one may ask for a source-weighted
anisotropy lower bound
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}(m)|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2

\ge
Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.

\[

\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

This hypothesis is retained only as a historical or fallback formulation.  In
the ordinary real-canonical branch it is supplied by
Theorem~\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity}, assuming Gate~1, source
Lipschitz control, and Lemma~\ref{lem:l2-input-real-rigidity-safe}.  It is not
an additional active downstream input in that branch.
```

**Why:** As written, this still says Gate 2 is a separate missing input. That is stale after the new source-thickening \(L^2\)-rigidity theorem.

# Edit 9 — Add a gauge-locking definition/remark near wall escape

**Where:** Immediately before Theorem `\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Gauge-locked wall scalar]
\label{def:gauge-locked-wall-scalar}
The wall scalar \(q_0\) is gauge-locked to the Gate--2 and D4 package if the
same scalar \(q_0\) satisfies, in the same normalized derivative convention,
\[
q_0''=u=q''_{\can},
\]
\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]
and the D4 source factor has leading form
\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0u^3}{288}.
\]
If these identities hold only up to residuals, the residuals must satisfy
\[
|q_0''-u|\le c\tau,
\]
and
\[
\left|
\Gamma_G-(u-6q_0+2q_0^3)
\right|
\le c\tau
\]
on wall-escape neighborhoods.
\end{definition}
```

**Why:** The theorem defines residuals, but the gauge-locking condition is so important that it should be stated explicitly before use.

# Edit 14 — Optional but useful: add a one-line source-thickening complex note

**Where:** After Lemma `\ref{lem:source-thickening-one-large-point}`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Complex-valued source thickening]
The proof only uses the Lipschitz property of \(|u|\), namely
\[
\bigl||u(m)|-|u(n)|\bigr|\le |u(m)-u(n)|,
\]
so the source-thickening lemma remains valid for complex-valued \(u\).  In the
main Gate--2 argument \(u\) is real by the real-canonical normal form.
\end{remark}
```

**Why:** It records the small technical fix without changing the main real Gate 2 route.

## What I would not change

I would **not** remove the older pointwise propagation / ODE rigidity material entirely. It is useful as historical/fallback structure and for explaining why the new \(L^2\)-input route is better. But it must be clearly marked fallback, not active.

I would also **not** promote the primitive-free \(L^2\) rigidity strengthening into the main theorem yet. The safe primitive-bounded lemma is enough and already much cleaner.
